اگر کسی خاتون و غیره نائب قاضی کے مقدمہ کی کاروائی ترتیب دینے کی حیثیت سے مقدم کی نائب قاضی کا روائی مرتب کرے تو اس میں تفصیل ہے جیسا کہ کرالائق ہیں میں مٹ جے ہیں ہے : ما نصه صدر الشهيد النائب يقضى بما شهد وعند الاصل و كذا الأصل ويقضى بما شهد وعند النائب الخ نیز بعض جزئیات نقل کرنے کے بعد ہے ۔ تخالف بعضها بعضا فالى صل أن القاضي اذا ولى الخليفة القضاء عمل بقوله وان ولأو سماع الدعوى والشهادة لا يعمل فلا تناقض الخ بحر الرائق مٹ ج اگر کسی مقدمہ کا فیصلہ کسی کیٹی کے سپرد بورڈ یاکمیٹی کے فیصلہ کی حیثیت کر دیا جائے جیسا کہ بعض مرتبہ کسی عدالت کے جموں کی جیوری کے سپرد ہوتا ہے یا پنچ کے سامنے پیش ہوتا ہے یا کوئی مقدمہ چند حضرات کی کمیٹی کے سپرد ہوتا ہے تو اس صورت میں ان تمام ارکان کا مسلمان ہونا شرط ہے کوئی غیر مسلم حج اور مجسٹریٹ اور مبر بھی اس کا رکن ہو تو شرعاً اس جماعت کا فیصلہ کسی طرح معتبر نہیں ، اس قسم کے فیصلہ سے تفریق (علیمی گیا) وغیرہ ہرگز صحیح نہیں ہوگی۔ جس جگہ مسلمان حاکم موجود نہ ہو یا سلمان حاکم اگر مسلمان مجسٹریٹ نہ مل سکے ؟ کی عدالت میں مقدمہ لے جانے کا قانونا اختیار لے لیکن یہ صورت طلاق وغیرہ کی جب ہوسکتی ہے جبکہ شوہر عاقل و بالغ ہوادر مفقود (بالکل لاپتہ ) نہ ہو کیونکہ مجنون اور نابالغ سے طلاق وغیرہ صحیح نہیں ہے اور مفقود سے طلاق لینے کی صورت نہیں ۔

نہ ہو یا مسلمان حاکم شرعی قانون کے مطابق فیصلہ نہ کرتا ہو تو ایسی صورت میں فقہ حنفی کے اعتبار سے تو عورت کی علیحد گی کے لیے شوہر کی طلاق وغیرہ کے بغیر کوئی صوت نہیں ہے
If a lady etc. appoints a deputy qadi to arrange proceedings of a case, and the deputy qadi arranges the proceedings, then there is detail in it, as is in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 'The text: The chief witness, the deputy judges by what he witnesses, and according to the original, likewise. And the original judges by what he witnesses, and according to the deputy, etc.' Also after quoting some details: 'If some contradict others, then the principle is that if the qadi appoints a deputy for judgment, his statement is acted upon, and if he appoints for hearing the claim and testimony, it is not acted upon, so there is no contradiction.' (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) If a case is referred to a committee or board for decision, as sometimes occurs in a court's jury or is presented before a panchayat, or a case is referred to a committee of several persons, then in that case it is a condition that all members be Muslim. If any non-Muslim, judge, magistrate, or member is also a member, then that group's decision is not valid in any way. A separation (talaq) etc. based on such a decision is never valid. Where a Muslim ruler is not present, or if a Muslim ruler takes legal permission to take the case to a non-Muslim court because a Muslim magistrate is not available, then this situation for talaq etc. is possible only when the husband is sane and adult and not missing (completely lost), because talaq from an insane or minor is not valid, and there is no way to obtain talaq from a missing person. Or if a Muslim ruler does not decide according to Sharia law, then according to Hanafi fiqh, there is no way for the woman's separation without the husband's talaq etc.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage presents three rulings from Hanafi fiqh regarding the validity of judicial decisions. First, it discusses the deputy qadi (na'ib qadi): if a deputy is appointed to arrange proceedings, his ruling is based on his own testimony, but if there is conflict between the original qadi and the deputy, the original qadi's statement prevails, as quoted from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. This is a rasm rule about delegation of judicial authority. Second, it addresses situations where a case is referred to a committee, board, or panchayat: all members must be Muslim. If any non-Muslim is a member (whether as judge, magistrate, or ordinary member), the decision is completely invalid in Sharia, including any talaq based on it. Third, it considers scenarios where a Muslim judge is absent or does not rule according to Sharia. In such cases, Hanafi fiqh allows taking the case to a non-Muslim court only if the husband is sane, adult, and not missing. If the husband is insane, minor, or missing, talaq from such a person is not valid. If a Muslim judge rules contrary to Sharia, there is no way for a woman to obtain separation without the husband's talaq. These rules guide the mufti when faced with complex situations involving non-Muslim courts or invalid judicial bodies.

Key Terms
پنچائیت (panchayat): A group of arbitrators (usually three or more) who decide a dispute
مفقود (mafqud): A person whose whereabouts are unknown and no news of life or death

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes a committee's decision invalid?
A) One non-Muslim member
B) Non-Muslim chairman
C) Majority non-Muslim
D) Decision about property

Key Takeaway
A judicial panel's decision is invalid if any member is non-Muslim; talaq from such a body is not valid unless conditions regarding the husband are met.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Conditions for Switching Madhhabs and Mufti Qualifications
Explaining conditions for switching madhhabs and mufti qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for adopting another madhhab and state the minimum qualifications for a mufti according to the Hanafi Rasm al-Mufti tradition.

Core Idea
Adopting another madhhab requires recognized necessity (darurat), not personal desire; a mufti must have expertise and awareness of custom, not necessarily ijtihad.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi clarifies the Hanafi position on when a mufti may issue a fatwa departing from his own madhhab. It establishes two key conditions: the necessity must be genuine and recognized by discerning scholars, and the mufti himself must be properly qualified—having studied under a master, being certified, and knowing the customs of his time. The discussion also provides practical guidance on referring cases to judges of other madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Prohibition
The author begins by prohibiting the giving of fatwa that abandons one's own imam's madhhab without a valid reason. Recognize this as the default position: one is bound to follow their own madhhab.
2
Define 'Darurat' (Necessity) and Its Conditions
Extract the definition: necessity must be severe (darurat shadidah), not due to personal desire, and it must be recognized by discerning scholars (ulama ahl-e-basirat). This is the key term that permits following another madhhab.
The legal definition dissector in this lesson unpacks the components of darurat.
3
List Mufti Qualifications
The minimum qualifications for a mufti after the age of ijtihad: he must have studied under a skilled teacher, be certified by experts, know the masail with their conditions and restrictions, be aware of custom ('urf), and have learned the method of fatwa from a master.
This is derived from the quote of al-Shami in 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti.
4
Apply the Conditions to the Maliki Judge Scenario
The hypothetical about Maliki judges illustrates the principle: when a case requires following another madhhab, it must be referred to the proper authority of that madhhab, not to a Hanafi judge. This reinforces that the channel must align with the madhhab being followed.
This demonstrates the practical application of the conditions.

لیے شرائط ر کے مذہب پر فائز ہونے) کے لیے اجتہاد کی شرط لگائی ہے اور یہ شرط اس زمانہ میں مفقود ہے پس کم از کم اس میں یہ شرط ضرور رہے گی کہ مسائل سے ان کی شرائط و قیودات کے ساتھ واقف ہو لینی) لے ایک بات یہ بھی پیش نظر رہنا چاہیے۔ اگر کسی جگہ مسلک مالکیہ کے قاضی نہ ہوں، یا جس جگہ بالکل قاضی ہی نہ ہوں اگر وہاں پر مالکہ کے مذہب کی پنچائیت ہو تو خفی ، قاضی اور حنفی پنچائیت کی طرف رجوع بند کیا جائے۔ اور اگر کوئی رجوع کرے تو ان کو مالکی مذہب پر فیصلہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ، بلکہ مالکی قاضی یا مالکی پنچائیت میں معامل پیش کیا جائے ۔ ایسی شرائط کہ جن کو حضرات فقہا اکثر بیشتر ترک کر دیتے ہیں اور اہل فن پر سکتی ہے کہ کم سے کم دو، چار محقق علماء دین کسی چیز میں ضرورت کو تسلیم کر کے دو دسر سے امام کے مذہب پر فتوی دیں۔ مذکورہ بالا شرائط کے بغیر اگر آج کل ضعیف اقوال اور دوسرے امام کے مذہب پر عمل کرنے کی اجازت دی جاتے تو اس کا لازمی نتیجہ ہم مذہب ہے (یعنی مذہب کو چھوڑ دنیا ہے جو کہ جائز نہیں ) والله اعلم بالصواب واليه المرجع والمآب
Do not give fatwa, until then everyone should not leave their own imam's madhhab, because adopting another madhhab means acting upon another imam's madhhab, and its condition is that this is not due to personal desire but due to severe necessity. And necessity is only that which the discerning scholars consider necessity. Also, it is necessary that the one giving fatwa is a person who has acquired the discipline from a skilled teacher, and the discerning scholars testify that he has complete expertise in fiqh. As al-Shami said in 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti': The early scholars conditioned ijtihad for the mufti, and this is lacking in our time. So at least one must condition that he knows the issues with their conditions and restrictions that they often omit or do not explicitly mention due to reliance on the understanding faqih. Similarly, it is better that he knows the custom of his time and the conditions of its people, and he acquires expertise in that from a skilled teacher. The meaning of the above statement is that the early scholars imposed the condition of ijtihad for the mufti to be qualified in the madhhab, and this condition is missing in this time. So at the very least, this condition remains: he must be acquainted with the issues along with their conditions and restrictions. Also, one thing should be considered: if in a place there are no Maliki judges, or if there are no judges at all, and there is a Maliki pancayat, then one should not refer to a Hanafi judge or Hanafi pancayat. And if someone does refer, they do not need to decide according to the Maliki madhhab; rather, the matter should be presented before a Maliki judge or Maliki pancayat. Such conditions that the jurists mostly omit and do not clearly state due to reliance on the experts. Similarly, it is also necessary for the mufti to be well aware of the customs of his time and the conditions of the time, and he should have acquired the method of giving fatwa from a skilled teacher (observed it). And in this age of trials and corruption, both these things coming together—i.e., complete piety and complete expertise in a person—are rare. For this reason, the only way to have assurance in this time is that at least two or four research scholars acknowledge necessity in something and then give fatwa on the madhhab of the imam. Without the above conditions, if nowadays weak opinions and acting upon another imam's madhhab are permitted, the inevitable result is abandonment of the madhhab (which is not permissible). And Allah knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and refuge.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the methodology of issuing fatwas, specifically regarding the transfer from one's own madhhab to another. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, begins by stating a general principle: a mufti must not give fatwa that abandons his own madhhab unless certain conditions are met. The first condition is that adopting another madhhab must not be due to personal desire (shahwat nafsani) but due to severe necessity (darurat shadidah). Necessity is not defined by the individual but by the discerning scholars (ulama ahl-e-basirat). Second, the mufti himself must be qualified: he must have studied under a skilled teacher (ustadh mahir) and be certified by experts as having complete mastery in fiqh. The author then quotes from Ibn Abidin's Shami (Radd al-Muhtar) on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, where the early scholars conditioned ijtihad for the mufti, but since that is lacking in later times, at minimum the mufti must know the masail with their conditions and qualifications, even those that experts often omit. He must also know the 'urf (custom) of his time and the ahwal (conditions) of the people, and obtain expertise from a skilled teacher. The author then applies this to a hypothetical: if there is no Maliki judge or qadi, one should not refer to a Hanafi judge or pancayat; rather, the case should go to a Maliki authority. This shows the importance of following the proper channel. Finally, the author notes that in his corrupt times, both piety and expertise are rare, so the safest way is for a group of qualified scholars to concur on necessity before issuing fatwa on another madhhab. Without these conditions, permitting weak opinions leads to abandonment of the madhhab, which is impermissible.

Key Terms
ضرورت (darurat): A severe necessity that justifies adopting another madhhab; must be recognized by discerning scholars.
مفتى (mufti): A person qualified to issue fatwas; must have studied under a skilled teacher and be certified by experts.
مذہب (madhhab): The legal school of an imam; one is generally bound to follow one's own madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary condition for permitting a person to act upon another madhhab?
A) Personal preference
B) Severe necessity recognized by discerning scholars
C) The availability of a Maliki qadi
D) The mufti's ijtihad

Key Takeaway
Adopting another madhhab is permissible only with genuine necessity verified by qualified scholars, and the mufti must have proper training and awareness of custom.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Permissibility of Following Another Madhhab Under Necessity
Ruling on necessity-based fatwa from another madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule that permits issuing fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab when genuine necessity (darurah) exists, and evaluate the objection that this was limited to the era of ijtihad.

Core Idea
Necessity (darurah) permits following another madhhab in any era; it is not confined to early ijtihad.

This lesson examines a crucial principle in Hanafi fatwa methodology: when and how a mufti may depart from the dominant Hanafi position and adopt a ruling from another madhhab. The source contrasts the absolute prohibition stated by the three Imams with the later allowance based on genuine necessity. It then refutes the argument that such flexibility ended after the fourth century AH. You will learn to identify the conditions and reasoning that make this permissible for a qualified mufti.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Baseline Prohibition
Identify that the three Hanafi Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) are reported to have absolutely prohibited following another madhhab without necessity. A muqallid must stay within the transmitted rulings of his own madhhab.
This prohibition protects against arbitrary disregard of one's madhhab.
2
Recognize the Exception for Necessity
Note that some later shaykhs made exceptions due to necessity (darurah). The word 'necessity' is general and applies to any time, not only the early period. Allamah Shami in 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti explicitly permits following customs and necessities in every era.
Necessity is a valid legal ground (shar'i 'udhr) for changing a fatwa.
3
Analyze the Objection of Qiyas Discontinuation
Some opponents argue that after 400 AH, qiyas is discontinued, and later muftis cannot adopt positions not taken by early Hanafi mujtahids. Therefore, following another madhhab is only allowed if early scholars already did so in that specific issue.
The objection relies on the claim that ijtihad has ceased.
4
Apply the Principle of Precedence
The author refutes the objection by citing the principle: 'A ruling mentioned in its own section takes precedence over one mentioned elsewhere.' Since Allamah Shami's ruling on necessity in fatwa methodology is explicit and general, it overrides any contrary inference from other texts. Thus, a qualified mufti can follow another madhhab when necessity arises, even in new issues.
This principle (al-hukm al-madhkur fi babihi awla) is a standard Hanafi interpretive tool.

Source Text

مذہب الغیر مخصوص تھا زمانہ اجتہاد کے ساتھ جو چوتھی صدی پر ختم ہو چکا پس چوتھی صدی کے بعد خواہ کیسی میں عمر درست شدیدہ اور حالت اضطرار پیش آجاد سے مگر جس
مسئلہ میں زمانہ اجتہاد کے مشائخ نے مذہب غیر کو اختیار نہیں فرمایا ۔ اس مسئلہ میں بعد کے علماء کو مذہب غیر پر فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں مقصود ان حضرات مستدلین کا یہ ہے کہ اس رسالہ میں جو مذہب مالکیہ کے مسائل لکھے گئے ہیں اُن میں اکثر مسائل ایسے ہیں جن کو زمانہ مذکورہ میں کسی حنفی مجتہد نے نہیں لیا اس واسطے ہم کو ان پر فتوت لے دینے کا اختیار نہیں ہے سو اس کا جواب اولاً تو یہ ہے کہ جب خود علامہ موصوف ہر زمانہ میں اس کے جواز کی تصریح فرما چکے (جیسا کہ عبارت مذکورہ بالا از عقود رسم المفتی سے واضح ہے) اور قاعدہ ہے الحكم المذكور في بابه أولى من المذكور في غير بابه تو پھر اگر اس عبارت [؟] سے مدعا جواز بھی ثابت ہو جائے تب بھی قابل تقسیم نہیں۔ ضرورة دوسرے امام کی اتباع دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ اس عبارت کا ہی مطلب یہ ہے کہ ضرورت کی وجہ سے دوسرے امام
No. And where they stated that the madhhab of our three Imams is absolute prohibition, despite the clarity of evidence, and some shaykhs allowed some things and justified that by necessity (darurah) permitting violation of the original madhhab. How can a muqallid be allowed to pursue that and completely exit the madhhab without a necessary need? Even if one claimed to include something that contains necessity not stated by them, we can reject it even if the cause exists, unless he is one of the people of qiyas. For he said in some of his treatises that qiyas after four hundred (AH) is discontinued. So no one can analogize one issue to another. What about exiting the madhhab? So the muqallid must follow transmitted rulings. Therefore, we do not see anyone who said it is permissible to hire for Hajj based on what later scholars gave fatwa on.
[Urdu: The above-mentioned acts of worship are all related to following another imam's madhhab in matters of trade and...] "Without a necessary need". From the word 'necessity' it is understood that at the time of necessity, following another imam is permissible. And there is no condition in this necessity that its verification must be of a specific time; rather, the word 'necessity' is used absolutely, which is general for every kind of [need], whether that necessity occurs in any time. As Allamah Shami also made necessity general in 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti... Then if it is said: Custom changes time after time. So if a new custom appears that conflicts with the earlier time, is it permissible for the mufti to oppose the textual ruling and follow the new custom? I say: Yes, because the later scholars [have authority]... but only if the mufti has sound judgment and knowledge of the principles of Shariah, so that he can distinguish between custom on which rulings may be based and other customs. For the early scholars required ijtihad in the mufti, and that is absent in our time, so the least that can be required is knowledge of the issues... 
[Urdu: This clearly states that in this time as well, due to a change of time because of a new necessity, the people of fatwa are permitted to give fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab. However, some people have argued that issuing fatwa according to another madhhab was specific to the era of ijtihad, which ended after the fourth century. So after the fourth century, no matter how severe the necessity or compulsion, if the scholars of the ijtihad era did not adopt that non-Hanafi madhhab in that issue, later scholars are not permitted to give fatwa according to that madhhab. The intent of these objectors is that in this treatise, most of the Maliki issues were not taken by any Hanafi mujtahid in that era, so we have no authority to give fatwa on them. The answer to this is: First, when the author himself clearly stated its permissibility in every era (as is clear from the above passage from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti') and the principle is: a ruling mentioned in its own section takes precedence over that mentioned elsewhere. So even if the intended permission is proven from this passage, it is still not subject to division. Following another imam due to necessity second point is that the meaning of this passage is that following another imam due to necessity...
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about when a Hanafi mufti may issue a fatwa according to another madhhab. The author begins by quoting a text that states the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) absolutely prohibit following another madhhab unless there is necessity. The quote warns that a muqallid (non-mujtahid) should not exit the Hanafi madhhab without genuine need. It also mentions that qiyas (analogical reasoning) is discontinued after 400 AH, meaning later scholars cannot create new analogies. The author then comments in Urdu, explaining that necessity is general and not restricted to a particular time. He cites Allamah Shami's 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' to show that custom and necessity can change rulings. The subsequent Arabic quote confirms that a mufti with sound knowledge can follow a new custom if it changes, provided he has the competence to distinguish valid custom. The Urdu refutes the objection that following another madhhab was only allowed in the era of ijtihad. The author argues that since the authority (Allamah Shami) explicitly permits it in every era, and the principle 'a ruling mentioned in its own section takes precedence' applies, the objection is invalid. Thus, a Hanafi mufti may give fatwa according to another madhhab when genuine necessity arises, even in later times.

Key Terms
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that justifies departing from the dominant Hanafi position and adopting a ruling from another madhhab.
مذهب الغير (madhhab al-ghayr): Any madhhab other than Hanafi (e.g., Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) whose ruling may be adopted in cases of necessity.
مقلد (muqallid): A non-mujtahid who must follow a particular madhhab; in this context, one who may not arbitrarily follow another madhhab without necessity.
تغير الزمان (taghayyur al-zaman): Change of times and customs that may necessitate a change in fatwa, as recognized by later Hanafi jurists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum qualification for a mufti to issue a fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab due to necessity?
A) He must be a mujtahid.
B) He must have sound judgment and knowledge of Shariah principles.
C) He must have the approval of three scholars.
D) He must only follow the positions of early Hanafi scholars.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may issue a fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab when genuine necessity exists, and this permission is not restricted to the era of ijtihad but applies in any time, provided the mufti is qualified.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Conditions for Adopting Another Madhhab in Fatwa
Defending permissibility with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-hukm al-madhkur fi babihi awla' to defend the permissibility of adopting a non-Hanafi ruling and identify the conditions: genuine necessity and explicit textual transmission (manqul).

Core Idea
Adopting another madhhab in fatwa is permitted only if the ruling is explicitly established (manqul) and necessity is genuine.

This lesson explores the conditions under which a Hanafi mufti may issue a fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab. The passage defends this practice against objections that it was restricted to the era of ijtihad, clarifying the operative criteria and the role of legal maxims in resolving scholarly disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed question
Determine the exact issue: whether a Hanafi mufti after the 4th century AH may give fatwa according to another madhhab.
The objectors argue it was exclusive to the ijtihad period.
2
Extract the Hanafi position and its dalil
The author cites explicit permission from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti and invokes the maxim 'al-hukm al-madhkur fi babihi awla' to prioritize this text over historical restrictions.
The maxim gives weight to a ruling stated in its own proper context.
3
Analyze the condition of explicit transmission
The adopted ruling must be manqul (explicitly stated) in the other madhhab, not derived via qiyas. Non-mujtahids cannot analogize across madhhabs.
The example of payment for Quran recitation illustrates a ruling not explicit in any madhhab.
4
Apply the maxim to the dispute
Compare the strength of the explicit permission (from works on iftaa) with the objection (from historical arguments). The maxim dictates that the context-specific permission prevails.
This resolves the thamarah al-khilaf: fatwa according to other madhhabs is permissible under conditions.

There is clarification in this that in this time too, when change of time occurs due to a new necessity, then the people of fatwa are permitted to give fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab. Some people have argued that giving fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab was specific to the era of ijtihad, which ended in the fourth century. So after the fourth century, no matter how severe the necessity and desperate situation, in any matter in which the scholars of the era of ijtihad did not adopt a non-Hanafi madhhab, it is not permissible for later scholars to give fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab. The intent of these objectors is that in this treatise, among the Maliki issues written, most are such that no Hanafi mujtahid in the mentioned era took them. Therefore we do not have permission to give fatwa on them. So its answer is firstly that when the respected Allama himself has explicitly stated its permissibility for every time (as is clear from the above-cited passage from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti), and the principle is: 'A ruling mentioned in its own context is preferable to one mentioned in another context.' Then even if from this building being discussed... the permissibility is established, still it is not subject to division. Necessarily following another imam. The second point is that the meaning of this situation is that due to necessity, taking the madhhab of another imam, a fatwa can be given only on the permissibility of that matter whose permissibility is explicitly proven and stated in the madhhab of the other imam. Not on something that is not explicit in the other madhhab and clearly stated, by proving its permissibility via analogy on the other imam's madhhab. And then giving fatwa on that presented permissibility due to necessity, as some people in the time of Hazrat Allama Shanai claimed necessity and considered taking payment for recitation of the Quran permissible, and in this matter analogized upon the permissibility of payment for teaching. Its explanation is clearly present in the madhhab of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, and at this point the Allama's main purpose is to refute this invalid analogy. So the conclusion of the above is that the necessity of taking payment for recitation of the Quran is not acceptable, which would justify leaving one's own madhhab. And even if we accept its necessity, it still cannot be permissible because its permissibility is not explicit in any madhhab. And teaching, which is explicit, to analogize recitation upon it is not permissible for the people of this time due to being non-mujtahids, even though conveying reward from the Quran is also present in recitation, which is evident in the noble hadith regarding the original issue, i.e., Ruqya or giving something etc. And due to the same... Hazrat Imam Malik and Hazrat Imam Shafi'i have... as they do not have the right to analogize upon their own madhhab.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the permissibility for a Hanafi mufti to give fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab in cases of genuine necessity. The author begins by citing that such permission is clearly mentioned in 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, and then addresses an objection raised by some scholars who argue that this permission was restricted to the era of ijtihad (ended in the 4th century AH). The objectors claim that if earlier mujtahids did not adopt a non-Hanafi ruling for a particular issue, later scholars cannot do so. The author refutes this in two stages. First, he invokes the legal maxim 'A ruling mentioned in its own context is preferable to one mentioned in another context'—meaning the explicit permission from the works on iftaa takes precedence over objections based on historical restriction. Second, he clarifies the actual condition for adopting another madhhab: the ruling must be explicitly established (manqul) in that madhhab, not derived via qiyas. He illustrates with the case of taking payment for Quran recitation: some claimed necessity and analogized from teaching, but the permissibility of payment for recitation is not established in any madhhab, whereas teaching is. Therefore, even if necessity is claimed, such qiyas is invalid because the mufti is not a mujtahid and cannot extend rulings by analogy from one madhhab to another.

Key Terms
مذہب غیر (madhhab ghayr): A school of fiqh other than the Hanafi school.
منصوص (mansus): Explicitly stated or established in the primary texts of a madhhab.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning applied to derive a ruling for a new case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is a key condition for a Hanafi mufti to adopt a ruling from another madhhab?
A) The ruling must be derived via qiyas from the other madhhab's principles.
B) The ruling must be explicitly established (manqul) in the other madhhab.
C) The mufti must be a mujtahid.
D) The necessity must be accepted by all scholars.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may adopt a non-Hanafi ruling only when genuine necessity exists and the ruling is explicitly established in that madhhab, not derived by analogy.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Following Another Imam’s Madhhab in Necessity
Discusses conditions for transferring to another madhhab in dire need

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule that transferring to another madhhab is permissible under dire necessity, and evaluate the evidence from the historical extension of ijarah rulings.

Core Idea
A mufti may give fatwa from another madhhab in any century when dire necessity makes the original position unbearable.

This passage addresses a critical question for muftis: can one ever turn to another school's ruling when the Hanafi position imposes hardship? The author uses a surprising historical development—the gradual expansion of permissible wages for teaching religious sciences—to demonstrate that later Hanafi scholars did precisely this. By tracing how early restrictions were relaxed by later jurists, we see a practical precedent for adopting another imam's opinion under necessity. The lesson will walk through the evidence and extract the operative rule for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical pattern
Examine the sequence of Hanafi authorities from Qadi Khan and al-Kanz (7th century) to later scholars like the author of Mukhtaṣar al-Wiqāya, al-Nahr al-Fā’iq, al-Islāḥ wa al-Īḍāḥ, and Tanwīr al-Abṣār. Notice how each added new acts of worship to the permissibility of ijarah, teaching fiqh, imāma, adhān, etc.
This expansion was done by scholars who were not absolute mujtahids.
2
Recognize the key inference
Understand that by extending the ruling beyond the original permission, these later scholars effectively adopted opinions from other madhhabs (since the original Hanafi position only allowed wages for teaching Qur’an). This shows that adopting another madhhab is permissible.
The author uses this as evidence that the alleged restriction after the fourth century is incorrect.
3
Formulate the rasm rule
The text explicitly states: 'دوسرے امام کے مذہب پر فتوی دینا ہر زمانہ میں جائز ہے بشرطیکہ سخت ضرورت ہو' – giving fatwa according to another imam's madhhab is permissible in every age, provided there is dire necessity.
This is the operative rule for muftis.
4
Define 'dire necessity' (sakht zarūrat)
Identify the condition: an unbearable hardship that necessitates abandoning the original madhhab ruling. The text does not give an exhaustive list but requires a genuine, pressing hardship.
The condition is strict; not every inconvenience qualifies.
5
Distinguish from the alleged position of 'Allama Thanawi
The passage refutes a misunderstanding that 'Allama Thanawi forbade following another imam after the fourth century. The author shows that later scholars did exactly that, so the correct position is permissibility with necessity.
The dispute is resolved in favor of permissibility.

Source Text

تعلیم قرآن کے ساتھ تعلیم فقہ ملتی ہے یعنی صاحب مختصر وقایہ کی رائے میں تعلیم قرآن پر اجرت درست ہے اور تعلیم فقہ پر بھی اجرت درست نہیں ہے، (واضح رہے کہ) صاحب مختصر وقایہ کی وفات ست سو چون میں ہے اور صاحب النهر الفائق (متوفی نو سو بانوے) نے امامت کا اضافہ کر دیا ہے اور صاحب الاصلاح والايضاح متوفی دس سو بیس نے تعلیم فقہ پر اجرت لینے کو جائز فرمایا ہے اور صاحب تنویر الابصار متوفی دس سو چون نے تعلیم قرآن وفقہ اور امامت کے ساتھ اذان کو بھی شامل کر دیا یعنی صاحب تنویر الابصار کی رائے میں اذان پر بھی اجرت لینا درست نہیں ہے۔ (واضح رہے کہ تنویر الابصار کا حاشیہ موجودہ فتاوی شامی کے ساتھ شائع شدہ ہے، اور فتاوی شامی تنویر الابصار اور در مختار کا مجموعہ ہے) اور بعض فقہاء کرام نے اقامت اور وعظ کا بھی اضافہ کر دیا یعنی بعض فقہاء کی رائے میں اقامت اور وعظ پر بھی اجرت لینا درست نہیں ہے۔ سخت ضرورت میں دوسرے امام کے قول پر فتوی کی گنجائش جب یہ تفصیل علامہ موصوف خود تحریر فرما رہے ہیں اور ان تمام تفصیلات کے ساتھ جواز کا فتوی دے رہے ہیں جو کہ چوتھی صدی سے کافی عرصہ پہلے دوسرے (امام کے) مذہب سے ماخوذ ہیں اور خود ان فقہاء کرام کا مجتہد نہ ہونے اور زمانہ اجتہاد ختم ہو جانے کے باوجود دوسری اشیاء کو ملحق کرنا اس کی واضح دلیل ہے کہ حضرت علامہ تھانوی کا یہ مفہوم لینا صحیح نہیں ہو سکتا کہ چوتھی صدی کے بعد کسی دوسرے امام کا قول اختیار نہیں ہے بلکہ دوسرے امام کے مذہب پر فتوی دینا ہر زمانہ میں جائز ہے بشرطیکہ سخت ضرورت ہو کہ دوسرے امام کے مذہب پر عمل کرنے کے لیے کوئی ناقابل تحمل تکلیف یعنی سخت ضرورت اور سخت مجبور کن صورت حال پیش آجائے۔ كما نتا و من قبل ايضاً هذا ما من بالبال والله اعلم بحقيقة الحال

تنبیہات ضروریہ تعلق جماعت مسلمین شرعی کمیٹی کے لیے رہنما اصول

جماعت مسلمین کی صورت میں جماعت المسلمین عدول (یعنی شرعی کمیٹی کے لیے عادل افراد ہوں) کے الفاظ میں اور عدل سے مراد وہ شخص ہے جو کہ فاسق نہ ہو تمام کبیرہ گناہوں سے بچتا ہو اور چھوٹے چھوٹے گناہوں پر بھی مصر نہ ہو اور اگر کبھی کوئی گناہ ہو جاتا ہو تو فوراً توبہ کر لیتا ہو۔
هكذا ذكرهم العلامه بلا تسميه في رد المحتار
And Qadi Khan and others like him, who are great scholars of takhrij and tarjih, in their time only permitted salary for teaching the Qur'an; apart from that, they kept ijarah for other acts of worship impermissible. And they declared wages for other acts of worship impermissible. And al-Kanz, which holds a distinguished status among the commonly circulated texts, i.e., it is of exceptional importance, even after the end of the seventh century restricted the permissibility of ijarah only to teaching the Qur'an. The author of al-Kanz passed away in 751 AH. But after him, most of the authors of primary texts (mutūn) and commentators (shurrāh), and the people of fatwa, the honorable muftis, have annexed to teaching the Qur'an the teaching of fiqh, imāma, and adhān as well. As in Mukhtaṣar al-Wiqāya, teaching of fiqh is attached to teaching of the Qur'an; i.e., in the opinion of the author of Mukhtaṣar al-Wiqāya, wages for teaching the Qur'an are permissible, and for teaching fiqh also wages are not permissible. (It should be clear that) the author of Mukhtaṣar al-Wiqāya passed away in 754 AH, and the author of al-Nahr al-Fā’iq (d. 992 AH) added imāma; and the author of al-Iṣlāḥ wa al-Īḍāḥ (d. 1020 AH) declared taking wages for teaching fiqh permissible; and the author of Tanwīr al-Abṣār (d. 1054 AH) included adhān along with teaching Qur'an and fiqh and imāma; i.e., in the opinion of the author of Tanwīr al-Abṣār, taking wages for adhān is also not permissible. (It should be clear that the gloss on Tanwīr al-Abṣār is published along with the current Fatāwā Shāmī, and Fatāwā Shāmī is a compilation of Tanwīr al-Abṣār and al-Durr al-Mukhtār.) And some jurists have also added iqāma and wa‘z; i.e., in the opinion of some jurists, taking wages for iqāma and wa‘z is also not permissible. The allowance for issuing fatwa according to the statement of another imam in severe necessity: Since this detail the respected ‘Allāma himself is writing, and despite the fact that these rulings were derived from the madhhab of another imam long before the fourth century, and despite the fact that these jurists themselves are not mujtahids and the age of ijtihad has ended, yet they annexed other things. This is clear evidence that it cannot be correct to take the meaning of Hadrat ‘Allāma Thanawi that after the fourth century the statement of another imam cannot be adopted. Rather, giving fatwa according to the madhhab of another imam is permissible in every age, provided that there is a dire necessity, i.e., an unbearable hardship comes about, which necessitates acting according to the madhhab of another imam. As we have also mentioned before. This is what came to my mind. And Allah knows the reality of the situation.

Necessary admonitions concerning the guiding principles for the Islamic Committee of the Jama‘at Muslimeen.

In the wording of the Jama‘at Muslimeen, 'al-Jamā‘at al-Muslimīn 'udūl (i.e., for the Shari‘ah committee, its members should be just persons). And 'adl means a person who is not a sinner, avoids all major sins, and is not persistent in minor sins, and if a sin occurs from him, he immediately repents. Thus the ‘Allāma mentioned them without naming in Radd al-Muhtār.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti discussion about the conditions under which a mufti may issue a fatwa according to another madhhab. The author cites a historical development regarding the permissibility of receiving wages (ujrah) for teaching religious sciences. Early Hanafi authorities like Qadi Khan and the author of al-Kanz only permitted wages for teaching Qur'an, not for other acts of worship. Yet later scholars—such as the authors of Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya, al-Nahr al-Fa'iq, al-Islah wa al-Idah, and Tanwir al-Absar—gradually extended permissibility to teaching fiqh, imama, adhan, and even iqamah and wa‘z. This extension is significant because these later scholars were not absolute mujtahids, and the classical period of ijtihad had ended. The key principle derived from this is that it is permissible to give fatwa according to another imam’s madhhab at any time, provided there is a dire necessity (darurah) that makes adhering to the original Hanafi position unbearable. The author refutes an alleged claim by 'Allama Thanawi that after the fourth century, acting upon another imam’s opinion is impermissible. Instead, the correct view is that it is allowed whenever necessity demands. The final part defines 'adl (just) for the members of a Shari‘ah committee, requiring avoidance of major sins and not persisting in minor sins.

Key Terms
سخت ضرورت (sakht zarūrat): An unbearable hardship that necessitates abandoning the ruling of one's own madhhab for another imam's opinion.
عدل (ʿadl): A person who avoids major sins, does not persist in minor sins, and repents immediately if a sin occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, under what condition may a mufti give a fatwa according to the statement of another imam after the fourth century?
A) Only if the mufti is a mujtahid
B) Only in matters of worship (ibadat)
C) Only if there is a dire necessity that cannot be avoided
D) Only during the lifetime of the imam

Key Takeaway
Transferring to another madhhab is permissible whenever dire necessity arises, as demonstrated by the practice of later Hanafi scholars.

Defining 'Adl for Shari'ah Committee Members
Defines 'adl for Shari'ah committee members

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'adl and identify its three components as required for serving on a Shari'ah committee.

Core Idea
An 'adl person avoids major sins, does not persist in minor sins, and repents immediately upon sinning.

This short passage provides a practical definition of 'adl (justness) specifically for members of a Shari'ah committee. While the term is common in Islamic law, the passage clarifies what qualifies a person to serve in a collective religious body. The definition is taken from Radd al-Muhtar and is concise yet comprehensive. Understanding it is essential for anyone involved in forming or assessing such committees.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition in the text
Find the sentence beginning with 'اور عدل سے مراد وہ شخص ہے' – here the author defines 'adl with three criteria.
The definition is quoted from Radd al-Muhtar without naming the commentator.
2
Break down the three components
Identify the three requirements: 1) Not a fasiq (avoiding major sins), 2) not persistent in minor sins, and 3) if sin occurs, immediate repentance. Each component is necessary.
Persistence in minor sins is a form of fisq.
3
Apply to committee membership
Understand that these criteria are prerequisites for serving on a Shari'ah committee. The text mentions 'al-Jamā‘at al-Muslimīn 'udūl' meaning the committee must consist of just persons.
The definition ensures integrity of religious decisions.

Takhayyur Under Dire Necessity: Permissibility in Every Age
Rasm al-mufti rule on takhayyur under necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition for valid takhayyur and explain why, according to Hanafi usul al-ifta, following another imam's madhhab is permissible in any era when dire necessity arises.

Core Idea
Following another imam's madhhab is permissible in any era when dire necessity makes one's own madhhab unbearable.

A common misconception among students is that after the closure of ijtihad, adopting a ruling from another school becomes absolutely forbidden. This passage, from a classical Hanafi usul al-ifta work, clarifies that takhayyur remains valid, but only under a specific and stringent condition: dire necessity (sakht zarurat). Let us examine the author's argument and the precise legal condition he establishes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested claim
First, locate the claim that the author refutes: that after the third century, adopting the saying of another imam is not permissible. Understand who held this view (e.g., 'Allamah Shanai) and why.
The author argues that later jurists themselves, though not mujtahids, attached new issues to existing rulings by analogy, proving that takhayyur remains operative.
2
State the Hanafi position
The author asserts that giving fatwa according to another madhhab is permissible in every age, provided there is dire necessity (sakht zarurat). Note that this is not a blanket permission but a conditional license.
The term 'sakht zarurat' means an unbearable hardship that makes following one's own madhhab intolerable.
3
Analyze the evidence (istidlal)
The author uses the practice of later jurists (who were not mujtahids) as proof. They analogized new issues to existing rulings, which implies that they allowed following other madhahib in the process. This practice demonstrates that takhayyur is not restricted to the early centuries.
This is not a citation of a specific Quranic verse or hadith but an argument from practice (amal) within the Hanafi tradition.
4
Define the condition: sakht zarurat
The passage defines 'dire necessity' as a situation where acting upon one's own madhhab creates unbearable hardship. Identify the criteria: the hardship must be intolerable, not merely inconvenient.
This is a stricter standard than general necessity (darurah) and is specific to the Hanafi school's approach to takhayyur.
5
Apply to fatwa practice
As a mufti, you must assess whether the inquirer's situation meets the condition of sakht zarurat. If it does, you may validly issue a fatwa from another madhhab on that particular issue. Otherwise, you must adhere to the Hanafi position.
This rule is part of rasm al-mufti – the proper method for a Hanafi mufti in multi-madhhab contexts.

اضافہ کر دیا ریعنی بعض فقہاء کی رائے میں اقامت اور وعظہ پر بھی اجرت لینا درست نہیں لیا سخت ضرورت میں دیگر امام کے قول پر مٹکی گنجائش جب یہ تفصیل علامہ موصوف خود تحریر فرمارہے ہیں اور ان تمام تفصیلات کے ساتھ جواز کا فتویٰ دے رہے ہیں جو کہ چوتھی صدی سے کافی عرصہ پہلے دوسرے (امام کے) مذہب سے ماخوذ ہیں اور خود ان فقہاء کرام کا مجتہد نہ ہونے اور زمانہ اجتہاد ختم ہو جانے کے باوجود دوسری اشیاء کو ملحق کرنا اس کی واضح دلیل ہے کہ حضرت علامہ شنائی کا یہ مفہوم لینا صحیح نہیں ہو سکتا کہ جو تھی صدی کے بعد کسی دوسرے امام کا قول ہے کا اختیار نہیں ہے بلکہ دوسرے امام کے مذہب پر فتوی دینا ہر زمانہ میں جائز ہے بشرطیکہ سخت ضرورت ہو کہ دوسرے امام کے مذہب پر عمل کرنے کے لیے کوئی نا قابل تحمل تکلیف یعنی سخت ضرورت اور سخت مجبور کن صورت حال پیش آجائے۔ كما نتا و من قبل ايضاً هذا ما من بالبال والله اعلم بحقيقة الحال
Addressed that remuneration for iqamah and waz is not correct in the opinion of some jurists. In dire necessity, permission to act upon the saying of another imam. When this detail the aforementioned Allamah himself writes and with all these details gives a fatwa of permissibility, which are taken from the madhhab of another imam long before the fourth century. And despite these jurists themselves not being mujtahids and the era of ijtihad having ended, attaching other things to it is clear proof that the understanding of Allamah Shanai cannot be correct — that after the third century adopting the saying of another imam is not permissible. Rather, giving fatwa according to the madhhab of another imam is permissible in every age provided there is dire necessity, such that acting upon the madhhab of another imam causes unbearable hardship — meaning a dire necessity and extremely compelling situation arises. As we have mentioned before as well. This is what came to mind. And Allah knows the reality of the situation.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (rasm_rule) concerning the permissibility of takhayyur (selective following) of another imam's school. The author refutes the notion that after the third or fourth century, it becomes impermissible to adopt a ruling from another madhhab. He argues that the practice of later jurists themselves, who were not independent mujtahids, attaching new issues to existing rulings by analogy proves that takhayyur remains valid. The key condition is dire necessity (sakht zarurat), defined as an unbearable hardship. This is a standard Hanafi position in the usul al-ifta: when a muqallid faces a situation where following his own madhhab leads to intolerable difficulty, he may validly follow another madhhab on that particular issue. The author emphasizes that this is not a blanket permission but is restricted to cases of genuine necessity.

Key Terms
سخت ضرورت (sakht zarurat): An unbearable hardship that makes following one's own madhhab extremely difficult, justifying adoption of another imam's ruling.
تخیر (takhayyur): Selectively following a ruling from another madhhab when necessity arises.
الحاق (ilhaq): Attaching a new case to an existing ruling by analogy (qiyas), performed by a jurist who is not a mujtahid mutlaq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is it permissible to give a fatwa according to another imam's madhhab?
A) At any time, without restriction
B) Only during the first three centuries of Islam
C) When there is dire necessity that causes unbearable hardship
D) Never, because ijtihad has ended

Key Takeaway
Takhayyur is a valid concession in Hanafi fatwa practice, but only when dire necessity makes following one's own madhhab unbearable.

Requirement of Religious Uprightness for Committee Members
Ruling that immoral persons cannot be committee members, with delegation solution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement of religious uprightness for Shariah committee members in Maliki-based arbitration, explain the Hanafi counter-position, and construct a valid delegation solution when default members are not religious.

Core Idea
Religious uprightness is mandatory for committee members in Maliki-based arbitration; delegation solves the problem of influential but non-religious members.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najijah addresses a practical problem in modern Islamic arbitration: what if the influential people who would serve on a Shariah committee are not religious? The author rules that such persons cannot serve, based on the Maliki school's condition of 'adala. He then provides a legal stratagem (hila) to delegate authority to religious persons while still benefiting from the influence of the powerful. This lesson unpacks the madhhab reasoning and the limits of acting on another madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The author states that a person who is a usurer, takes bribes, shaves his beard, lies, or neglects prayers cannot be a member of the Shariah committee. The basis is that the committee follows the Maliki school, so all Maliki conditions apply.
2
Understand the Maliki condition of 'adala
According to the Malikis, a judge (or committee member) must be 'adil (upright) for his ruling to be valid and enforceable. This is derived from the Quranic verse about rejecting the testimony of a fasiq, extended to judges.
Maliki position: 'adala is a condition for validity (shart al-sihha).
3
Compare the Hanafi position
Hanafis do not require 'adala for the validity of a judge's ruling; a fasiq's ruling is valid but it is haram to appoint him. However, in this context, the committee adopts Maliki, so the stricter condition governs.
Hanafi position: 'adala is not a condition for validity but is a condition for permissibility of appointment.
4
Analyze the practical solution (hila)
If influential but non-religious persons are the default members, they should delegate full authority to religious persons. The influential persons may remain involved for their influence but are not responsible for the ruling.
The delegation ensures the ruling is attributed to religious persons, satisfying the Maliki condition.
5
Determine the limits of following another madhhab
Acting on a different madhhab (here, Maliki) is only permissible under genuine necessity (darurah), defined as unbearable hardship. Mere convenience is insufficient.
The author criticizes a pamphlet that incorrectly equates necessity with risk of destruction; the correct standard is unbearable hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لہذا وہ شخص جو کہ سود خور ہو یا رشوت وغیرہ لیتا ہو یا ڈاڑھی منڈاتا ہو یا جھوٹ بولتا ہو یا نماز روزہ کا پابند نہیں ہے وہ شخص اس جماعت (یعنی شرعی کمیٹی ) کا ممبر نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ کیونکہ یہ مسئلہ مالکیہ کے مذہب سے لیا گیا ہے ، اس وجہ سے اس کو تمام شرائط مذہب مالکیہ سے لینا لازم ہے اور ان کے نزدیک قاضی وغیرہ (یا شرعی کمیٹی کے ممبران کے لیے، معادل ہونا شرط ہے ، اس وجہ سے غیر عادل کا حکم نافذ نہیں ہوگا اور احناف کے نزدیک اگر چہ قاضی کا عادل ہونا شرط کے درجہ میں نہیں ہے لیکن غیر عادل شخص سے فیصلہ کرانا حرام ہے اس لیے ان کے نزدیک بھی غیر عادل کو اس پنچائیت (کمیٹی کا رکن بنانا جائز نہیں ہے، (خلاصہ یہ کہ پنچائیت یعنی شرعی کمیٹی کا دیندار ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اگر بد قسمتی سے کسی جگہ کے با اثر حضرات ارکان شرعی کمیٹی اگر دین دار نہ ہوں تو یہ صورت اختیار کر لی جائے کہ وہ با اثر حضرات ، چند دین دار حضرات کو اختیار دے دیں تا کہ شرکا فیصلہ کی نسبت دین دار حضرات کی جانب ہو اور با اثر حضرات کی شرکت اگر چہ ضروری نہیں ہے لیکن ان کے اثر و رسوخ سے کام میں آسانی ہوتی۔ اس وجہ سے اس طریقہ کا کام بھی بن جائے گا اور ان با اثر حضرات کو ثواب بھی ملے گا۔ کے ایک مطبوعہ رسالہ میں دیکھا کہ ذہب خیر پر عمل جب جائز ہے جب اندیشہ ہلاکت ہو لیکن کسی کتاب کا حوالہ نہیں دیا اور نہ دے سکتے ہیں ضرورت کی صحیح تفسیر وہ ہی ہے جو کہ ہم نے کی ہے یعنی تکلیف ناقابل برداشت چنانچہ خود اس رسالہ میں بھی ایک جگہ تکلیف نا قابل برداشت کا لفظ استعمال کیا ہے ۔
Therefore, that person who is a usurer, or takes bribes etc., or shaves his beard, or lies, or is not punctual in prayer and fasting, cannot be a member of this group (i.e., the Shariah committee). Because this issue has been taken from the Maliki school, therefore it is necessary to take all conditions from the Maliki school. According to them, it is a condition that the judge (or members of the Shariah committee) be righteous ('adil). Hence the ruling of a non-righteous person will not be enforceable. And according to the Hanafis, although the righteousness of the judge is not required as a condition, it is haram to seek a ruling from a non-righteous person. Therefore, according to them as well, making a non-righteous person a member of this panchayat (committee) is not permissible. Summary: The panchayat, i.e., the Shariah committee, must be religious. If, unfortunately, in some place the influential persons who are members of the Shariah committee are not religious, then this course of action should be adopted: those influential persons should authorize several religious persons so that the attribution of the decision is to the religious persons. Although the participation of the influential persons is not necessary, their influence makes the task easier. Therefore, this way the work will also be accomplished and those influential persons will also receive reward. I saw in a published pamphlet that acting on the better opinion (madhhab khair) is permissible only when there is fear of destruction, but they did not give a reference to any book, nor can they. The correct interpretation of necessity is what we have given, i.e., unbearable hardship. Indeed, in that same pamphlet, in one place the term 'unbearable hardship' is used.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage lays down the ruling on the qualification of members of a Shariah committee established for arbitration, particularly in cases like annulment of marriage (faskh nikah) where the Maliki school is being followed. The author states that a person who engages in major sins (usury, bribery, shaving the beard, lying, neglecting prayers and fasting) cannot be a member of such a committee. The reason given is that the ruling on the committee's authority is taken from the Maliki school, and thus all conditions of the Maliki school must be fulfilled. According to the Malikis, a judge (or committee member) must be 'adil (upright). Without this, the ruling is not enforceable. Although the Hanafi school does not require 'adala as a condition for validity of a judge's ruling, it is still haram to appoint a fasiq (sinner) as judge, and therefore the conclusion is the same: the committee must be composed of religious persons. The passage then addresses a practical problem: if in a locality the influential people who would naturally be on the committee are not religious, they can delegate authority to a group of religious persons. The influential people need not be members themselves; they merely lend their influence, and both the work gets done and they receive reward. Finally, the author clarifies a common misunderstanding: this permission to act on another madhhab (Maliki) is only valid when there is genuine necessity (dharurah), defined as unbearable hardship. This is distinguished from an incorrect interpretation that requires a risk of destruction.

Key Terms
عادل (ʿādil): A person who avoids major sins and minor sins and maintains general uprightness in religious matters.
دیندار (dayandār): Religious; one who fulfills obligatory acts and avoids forbidden acts.
شرعی کمیٹی (sharʿī kamīṭī): A committee established to resolve disputes according to Shariah, especially in matters of faskh nikah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The member must be knowledgeable in fiqh.
B) The member must be a mujtahid.
C) The member must be 'adil (upright).
D) The member must be a descendant of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
In Maliki-based arbitration, uprightness is essential; delegation to religious persons is a valid stratagem when influential members lack it.

Conditions for a Valid Shari'ah Committee and the Requirement of Consensus
Stating conditions for valid Shari'ah committee and effect of agreement vs disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid Shari'ah committee and apply the rule that only unanimous decisions are binding.

Core Idea
A Shari'ah committee's decision is void unless members are knowledgeable and act unanimously.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's work establishes the foundational rules for Shari'ah committees in matters like faskh nikah. It emphasizes that laypeople cannot be entrusted with such decisions; only scholars—or at least one scholar consulted at every step—can issue valid rulings. Moreover, unanimity is required; a split decision is null. This principle is rooted in the Hanafi rule for arbiters (hakamayn) and reinforced by Maliki jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three-tier condition for committee composition
The passage states three scenarios: (1) all members are knowledgeable, (2) at least one scholar is included and all actions are done after consulting him, or (3) if impossible, the committee's decision cannot be valid and the matter must be referred to scholars.
The second tier requires actual consultation, not mere presence.
2
Extract the rule for ignorant judges
Even if an ignorant judge's ruling happens to be correct, it is invalid because he failed to consult scholars. The analogy to prayer without piety is given: abandoning the obligation renders the act invalid.
This is supported by Maliki sources quoted in the passage.
3
Recognize the requirement of consensus
The committee must agree unanimously; disagreement renders any decision null. This is analogous to the two arbiters (hakamayn) in marital disputes, who must both agree per Al-Hidayah.
The passage explicitly states: if members disagree, no separation can occur.
4
Apply the rule to a modern scenario
In a contemporary fatwa council, if members disagree, no binding ruling can be issued; the matter must be referred to a higher authority or resolved through further deliberation.
This prevents arbitrary rulings from a subset of the committee.

Source Text

شرعی کمیٹی میں اہل علم افراد کی شرکت
اگر افسخ نکاح و غیره ) فیصلہ پنجائیت یعنی شرعی کمیٹی کے سپرد کر لیا جائے
تو چونکہ عوام کی پنچائیت کا کچھ اعتبار نہیں ہے نہ معلوم کس جگہ شرعی احکام کی خلاف ورزی کریں اس وجہ سے سب سے پہلے تو یہ چاہیئے کہ پنچائیت یعنی شرعی کمیٹی کے تمام ممبران ) اہل علم ہوں اور اگر ایسا نہ ہو سکے یعنی تمام ممبران اہل علم نہ سکیں تو کم سے کم ایک معاملہ فہم عالم کو پنچائیت یعنی شرعی کمیٹی میں اس طریقہ سے شامل کر لیا جائے کہ شروع سے آخیر تک جو کچھ بھی کریں اُن سے دریافت کر کے کریں۔ اور اگر یہ بھی ممکن نہ ہو تو پنجائیت (یعنی شرعی کمیٹی کا فیصلہ ) نافذ اور معتبر ہونے کی کوئی صورت نہیں ہے کہ معاملہ کی مکمل رو نداد دکھلا کر دینی فسخ نکاح وغیرہ کے مقدمہ کی کاروائی کی پوری فائل دکھلا کہ ) ہر ایک جنز کے شرعی حکم کو معاملہ فہیم محقق علماء کرام (یا مفتیان کرام) سے دریافت کر کے ان کے فتویٰ کے موافق فیصلہ کیا جائے اگر ایسا نہ کیا گیا بلکہ عوام نے بعض ایسی انے سے فیصلہ کر دیا تو وہ حکم نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ اگر چہ اتفاقاً فیصلہ صحیح بھی ہوگیا ہو جیسا کہ فقہاء مالکیہ نے اس کی وضاحت فرمائی ہے ۔ جیسا کہ مختصر خلیل (نامی کتاب میں ہے انہوں نے کہا ہے ۔
ونبد حكم جائر وجاهل لو يشاور والا تعقب ومعنى غير الجور وقال شارعه العلامة الدويدار تحت قوله لو يشاور اى العلماء ولو وافق الحق، والى ان قال ( وان تعقب مع المشاورة وان عرف الحكم فقد لا يعرف ايقاعه لانه يحتاج لزيادة نظر فى البينه وغيرها من احوال المتداعين اذا القضاء ضاعته دقيقة لا يهتدى اليه كل الناس قلنا ونظيره على قول بعض من صلى بغير التقوى نان صلوته لا تقم

ونظيره ماكتبنا ان اختلافی فیصلہ تسلیم نہ ہونے سے تعلق فی عبارت الحكمين اذا اختلفا
لا ينفذ حكم احد منهما قال صاحب الهدايه لوحكما رجلين لا بد من اجتماعهما لانه امر يحتاج فيه الى الرائي وفي شرحها النهايه حتى لو حكم احدهما دون الآخر لا يجوز لانهما رضيا برأيهما و رأى الواحد
لا يكون كرأى الاثنين - هدايه ما ج ٣ الخ -
قلنا فكما ان تفويض الحقيقي الحكمين يقتضى اجتماع کی آیھما علی حكم واحد فكلا تفويض الشرع الحكو الى الجماعه يقتضى اجتماع آرائهم
Participation of knowledgeable people in the Shari'ah Committee. If the decision of faskh nikah etc. is entrusted to a panchayat, i.e., a Shari'ah committee, since the panchayat of common people has no credibility—it is not known where they will violate Shari'ah rulings—therefore, first of all, it is necessary that all members of the panchayat, i.e., the Shari'ah committee, be knowledgeable. If that is not possible, i.e., all members cannot be knowledgeable, then at least one scholar experienced in affairs should be included in the panchayat, i.e., the Shari'ah committee, in such a way that whatever they do from beginning to end, they do it after consulting him. And if even this is not possible, then there is no way for the panchayat's (i.e., the Shari'ah committee's) decision to be enforceable and valid. It is that the complete report of the case should be presented, and for each item, the Shari'ah ruling should be ascertained from experienced and verifying scholars (or muftis) and the decision should be made according to their fatwa. If this is not done, but common people made a decision based on some such things, then that ruling will not be enforceable, even if coincidentally the decision turned out to be correct, as the Maliki jurists have explained. As mentioned in the book Mukhtasar Khalil, they said: 'We reject the judgment of an unjust and ignorant person if he does not consult, otherwise it is subject to challenge.' The meaning of 'unjust' is other than injustice. Its commentator, Allamah al-Duwidar, said under his statement 'if he does not consult' i.e., the scholars, even if it coincides with the truth. And up to where he said: 'And it is subject to challenge even with consultation, because even if he knows the ruling, he may not know its application, as it requires additional scrutiny of evidence and other circumstances of the litigants, for judgment is a precise matter not every person can guide to.' We say, and its analogy is the statement of some that one who prays without piety, his prayer is not valid even if he hit the qibla, because he abandoned the obligation of piety. Similarly, if an ignorant person abandons the obligation of consulting scholars, his judgment is not executed even if it coincides with the truth. As for the challenge to his judgment after consulting scholars, that is the duty of the judge, and the validity of the judgment suffices us. And he said in the chapter of judgment: 'As for the ignorant and the disbeliever, it is not permissible to appoint them as arbiters.' So he said: 'If a disputant or a disbeliever or an ignorant person is appointed, his judgment is not executed.' Sharh al-Dardir p. (2). We say that the non-execution is specific to when the ignorant person does not consult scholars. And Allah knows best. The status and powers of the Shari'ah committee: The Shari'ah panchayat, i.e., the Shari'ah committee, as described above, if by unanimous agreement they effect a Shari'ah separation (i.e., issue a ruling of talaq etc.), then their decision will stand in place of the judge's decision, and the separation etc. will be valid. If, God forbid, there is a difference of opinion among the members of the panchayat and Shari'ah committee regarding a case or matter, then the separation etc. cannot occur. And if some (members of the committee) made a decision, that decision will be considered null and void. Its analogy is what we wrote: the issue of a differing decision not being accepted is in the statement of the two arbiters: 'When they differ, the judgment of neither is executed.' The author of Al-Hidayah said: 'If two men are appointed as arbiters, their meeting is necessary because it is a matter requiring opinion.' And in its commentary, Al-Nihayah: 'Even if one of them judges without the other, it is not allowed because they consented to their combined opinion, and the opinion of one is not like the opinion of two.' (Al-Hidayah, vol. 3 end). We say: Just as the actual delegation to two arbiters requires their meeting upon a single judgment, similarly, the Shari'ah's delegation of judgment to a group requires the meeting of their opinions.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage establishes the rules for the composition and decision-making of a Shari'ah committee (شرعی کمیٹی) when entrusted with matters like faskh nikah. The author begins by stressing that because laypeople's panchayats lack credibility, the committee must consist entirely of knowledgeable members. If that is not possible, at least one experienced scholar must be included and all actions must be taken after consulting him. If even this is impossible, the committee's decision cannot be valid, and the case must be referred to proper scholars or muftis. The passage then reinforces this by quoting Maliki jurists: an ignorant or unjust judge's decision is invalid if he does not consult scholars, even if the ruling happens to be correct. The second part clarifies the committee's authority: if all members agree, the decision is binding like a judge's. If they disagree, no decision can be made. If some members attempt to issue a ruling without consensus, it is null. This is analogous to the rule for two arbiters (حکمین) in marital disputes: they must both agree, and one cannot decide alone. The author draws on Al-Hidayah and its commentaries to support this.

Key Terms
شرعی کمیٹی (shar'i committee): A panel of scholars appointed to adjudicate Shari'ah matters such as faskh nikah.
پنچائیت (panchayat): A traditional council, used here interchangeably with the Shari'ah committee.
مشاورہ (mushawara): Consultation with scholars to determine the correct Shari'ah ruling.
حکمین (hakamayn): Two arbiters appointed to resolve marital disputes; their decision requires agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for a Shari'ah committee to issue a valid decision?
A) All members must be scholars.
B) At least one knowledgeable person must be included and all decisions must be made after consulting him.
C) Any decision is valid if it agrees with Shari'ah, regardless of the members' knowledge.
D) Majority vote suffices even if some members are ignorant.

Key Takeaway
A Shari'ah committee must have qualified members and reach unanimous decisions; otherwise its rulings are void regardless of their substantive correctness.

The Requirement of Unanimity in Arbitration (Tahkim): A Maliki-Influenced Rule in Hanafi Iftaa
Maliki sources argue against majority rulings in arbitration; unanimity required.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that a fatwa committee's decision requires unanimity among all appointed members, and distinguish this from majority rule in arbitration cases.

Core Idea
In arbitration, only unanimous decisions are binding; majority opinion has no evidentiary basis.

This lesson examines a rule derived from Maliki fiqh regarding arbitration (tahkim): when two or more arbitrators are appointed, their ruling must be unanimous. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, quotes Maliki authorities to argue that a majority vote is insufficient. This rule is relevant for fatwa committees and modern shari'ah boards. We will parse the arguments and understand the legal maxim underlying the requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Parse the passage to identify the legal actors: حكم (ruling), حكمان (two arbitrators), جماعت (group of arbitrators), كثرة رائے (majority opinion). Understand their roles.
These terms are central to understanding the rule.
2
Trace the arguments of the Maliki scholars
Identify each quoted authority (Imam Malik, al-Baji, Sahnun, Ibn Kinana) and their statements. Understand the logical flow: if two arbitrators disagree, no ruling; if a group agrees, ruling is valid.
Pay attention to the pronouns and who is speaking.
3
Extract the legal maxim (qawida)
From the Maliki statements, derive the principle 'إذا اجتمع حكمان فلا يلزم حكم أحدهما دون الآخر'. This maxim governs the arbitration scenario.
This maxim is the foundation of the ruling.
4
Apply to a modern fatwa committee
Consider a shari'ah committee of three members. If two rule in favor of a divorce but one dissents, is the divorce effective? According to this maxim, no, because unanimity is required.
This has practical implications for family law arbitration.

Upon one ruling. And it is [unclear] stated by Imam Malik regarding the two arbitrators in the answer about marriage and divorce from volume 3, part 2, where he said: I said, 'If they disagree, and one of them divorces but the other does not divorce?' He said: 'Then there is no separation, because each of them is [joined] with his companion by their mutual agreement on it' etc. And clearer than it is what al-Baji al-Maliki said in al-Muntaqa: 'If the two disputants appoint two men as arbitrators, and one of them rules but the other does not rule, then that is not permissible for him' - said by Sahnun in the book of his son [؟] and [؟]. (Shami) The above passage indicates that the decision of the Muslim community (or shari'ah committee) is only valid if it is unanimous; majority opinion is not considered. Because there is no evidence for its validity, and without evidence no ruling can be established. However, the woman has the right to a review. The proceedings are exactly the same; if nothing new arises, separation is not effected. And that is in al-Mudawwanah, beginning of the book of Judgments, page 4. [؟] after that, he wanted to [؟] that did not say that from them.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage establishes a rule of arbitration (tahkim) within the Maliki school, which the author quotes to argue that a ruling by a majority of arbitrators is not valid; only a unanimous decision is binding. The Arabic quotes from Imam Malik, al-Baji, and others emphasize that when two arbitrators are appointed, they must both agree on the ruling; if only one rules, it is not binding. Similarly, if a group of arbitrators is appointed, all must agree. The Urdu commentary (attributed to 'Shami') clarifies that this principle applies to any shari'ah committee: only unanimous decisions are valid. Majority opinion has no basis. However, the woman has the right to a second review, and if in that review the arbitrators unanimously agree on separation, it becomes effective. The text cites al-Mudawwanah as a source. This is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) regarding how a fatwa committee's decisions are formed.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): A ruling or judgment; here, the decision of an arbitrator in a dispute.
كثرة رائے (kasrat ra'y): Majority opinion; the view of the majority of arbitrators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A simple majority vote
B) A unanimous decision by all appointed members
C) The decision of the most senior member
D) Approval by a higher court

Key Takeaway
A ruling in arbitration is only binding if all appointed members unanimously agree; majority opinion has no evidentiary basis and is not recognised in this view.

Invalidation of Khiyar by I'rad
Rasm al-Mufti: Expanding khiyar invalidation from standing to all indications of i'rad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that khiyar al-majlis is invalidated by any indication of i'rad, and identify the scope of i'rad based on the expansion from standing to general turning away.

Core Idea
Any act indicating turning away invalidates the option, not only physical departure.

This lesson examines a critical rasm al-mufti rule: the invalidation of khiyar (option) by i'rad (turning away). The source expands the commonly held view that the option is lost only by standing up. Instead, any conduct that clearly shows disinterest or abandonment of the session—such as starting a new conversation or praying—legally invalidates the option. This expansion is grounded in a principle extracted from the primary texts, as quoted from al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Note that the default understanding is that khiyar al-majlis ends when the parties physically separate (e.g., stand up). This lesson challenges that limited view.
The text explicitly states that standing is not the exclusive cause.
2
Recognize the expansion
The author asserts that any evidence of i'rad (turning away) invalidates the option. Examples include starting a new conversation or praying.
The phrase 'بل كل ما يدل على الاعراض' is the core of the ruling.
3
Examine the dalil
The proof cited is from al-Durr, which says that standing was mentioned as an example (tamthil), and the real intent is absolute i'rad.
The extraction of the general principle from the specific example is a key Hanafi usul operation.
4
Note the practical implications
Acts that may not involve standing but show disinterest—like looking away, engaging in unrelated activities, or ignoring the other party—can all invalidate the option.
The mufti must assess whether the act unambiguously indicates turning away.
5
Reference the source authority
The text directs readers to al-Tahtawi's commentary on al-Durr for further details on changing the session.
This demonstrates reliance on later Hanafi fatwa works (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثلاً عورت کوئی دوسری گفتگو کرنے لگے یا نماز پڑھنے لگے وغیرہ جو کہ اعراض یا پہلوتہی پر دلالت کرتی ہوں۔ اور مجلسی بدل جانے کی تفصیل تاوی شامی باب تفوین الطلاق سے معلوم ہوسکتی ہے ۔ والدليل على أن بطلان الخيار لا يختص بقيامها وقيام القاضي بل كل ما يدل على الاعراض، بيطل الخيار قول الدرجيث قال الووجه منهما دلیل اعراض بان قامت الولان هذا يدل على ان القيام ذكر حيت ذكر تميثلا والمراد مطلق الاعراض هذا ما عندنا والله اعلم
For example, if a woman starts another conversation or begins to pray, etc., which indicate turning away (i'rad) or negligence. And the detail of the session changing can be known from Tawiyya Shami, chapter Tafwid al-Talaq. And the evidence that the invalidation of the option is not specific to her standing and the standing of the qadi, rather everything that indicates turning away invalidates the option is the statement of al-Durr: 'He said: The [؟] from them both is evidence of turning away, because she stood up and [؟].' This indicates that standing was mentioned as an example, and the intended meaning is absolute turning away. This is what we have, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (rasm) about the invalidation of an option (khiyar). The author explains that the option is not only invalidated when the person physically stands up (as might be assumed from the example of standing), but rather any act that clearly indicates turning away (i'rad) or disinterest invalidates the option. Examples given are the woman starting another conversation or praying, which show she has abandoned the session. The author references the commentary of al-Tahtawi on al-Durr al-Mukhtar for further details on changing the session. The evidence quoted from al-Durr emphasizes that standing is merely an example; the real criterion is any indication of turning away. This is a standard Hanafi principle: the option of the session (khiyar al-majlis) is lost by any act that contradicts remaining in the state of deliberation.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): An option or choice, usually in contracts or divorce, that gives the right to rescind or confirm.
اعراض (i'rad): Turning away or showing disinterest, which legally invalidates the option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Quran verse
B) Hadith
C) Statement from al-Durr
D) Analogy (qiyas)

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-majlis is invalidated by any act that clearly indicates turning away, as established in later Hanafi fatwa works.

Adopting a Maliki Ruling Due to Necessity
Concluding remarks on Hanafi-Maliki agreement and adoption of Maliki ruling in panchayat issue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of darura to justify adopting a ruling from another madhhab in a fatwa.

Core Idea
Necessity (darura) permits a Hanafi mufti to adopt a Maliki ruling when needed to avoid hardship.

In normal circumstances, a Hanafi mufti is bound by the positions of the Hanafi school. However, situations may arise where following the Hanafi position leads to hardship that cannot be avoided without resorting to another madhhab. This passage illustrates such a case: the author adopts the Maliki ruling on panchayat arbitration due to necessity, while affirming that the Hanafi position remains the default.

Guided Path
1
State the default Hanafi position
Identify the well-known and established Hanafi ruling on panchayat decisions: they are not legally binding ('la yu'taddu bihi').
This is the default position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the Maliki exception
Note that the Maliki school considers panchayat decisions valid and authoritative, based on their sources (e.g., the 19th narration).
The author states that in most other details, Maliki agrees with Hanafi, but this specific point differs.
3
Determine the condition for adopting a foreign ruling
Recognize that the author adopts the Maliki view only due to necessity (darura), not because it is stronger.
Darura must be genuine and limited to the extent of the need.
4
Apply the condition to this case
Understand that in this treatise, the necessity arises from practical hardship that would occur if the Hanafi position were strictly followed.
The exact nature of the hardship is not detailed, but it justifies the departure.
5
Note the limits of adoption
The author cautions that this is only for this specific part (panchayat validity) and for other issues one should consult qualified scholars.
This prevents wholesale abandonment of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جو اوپر مذکور ہے فقہ حنفی کا مشہور اور مسلمہ مسلہ ہے اور اس کے حوالہ سے نقل کیا گیا ہے اور اس مسئلہ میں مذہب مالکیہ بھی تقریبا تمام جزئیات میں مسلک احناف کے ساتھ بالکل متفق ہے جیسا کہ علامہ صالح تونسی الکی ، مفتی مدینہ منورہ کے فتویٰ کی عبارت عشا [؟] سے معلوم ہوتا ہے۔
