له إلى بعض المسائل كما أن ترامي الأثر وجبين بالتأجيل كاف عندهم كما هو مصرح به في الرواية التاسقة عشر وعندنا لا يعتد به كما في البحر وغير مصرح. وما لم نشاهد ضرورة المصير إلى مذهب المالكية في هذا الجزء له نأخذ به رعاية للاحتياط في أمر الفونج [؟]
What is mentioned above is the well-known and established position of Hanafi fiqh, and it has been transmitted with reference to it. In this issue, the Maliki school also agrees almost entirely in all particulars with the Hanafi school, as appears from the fatwa text of Allama Salih Tunisi al-Makki, the Mufti of Medina [؟]. However, only one element, i.e., that the decision of the panchayat is considered valid—which has been described above—is a specific issue of the Maliki school, and in this treatise, a fatwa has been given on it due to necessity. One note: This brief explanation has been written to the extent necessary; besides this, in many other particulars, when needed, one should ask the scholars who are qualified to issue fatwas. He has to some issues like that the compounding of wounds and [؟] with deferment is sufficient according to them as stated in the nineteenth narration, and according to us it is not considered as in al-Bahr and other works. And as long as we do not see the necessity of resorting to the Maliki school in this part, we do not adopt it, but due to precaution in the matter of [؟].
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage serves as a concluding clarification regarding the Hanafi position on the issue of panchayat (arbitration) decisions. The author explains that the Hanafi school is well-established, and in most details, the Maliki school agrees with it. However, the specific ruling that a panchayat's verdict is authoritative is unique to the Maliki school. Because of pressing necessity, this treatise adopts the Maliki position in this particular matter, allowing for a fatwa that would otherwise not be permissible in the Hanafi school. The author emphasizes that this is a limited exception and that for other issues, one should consult qualified scholars. The garbled Arabic at the end mentions a rule about compounding of wounds with deferred payment being valid in Maliki (based on the 19th narration) but not in Hanafi, and again underscores that they only adopt the Maliki view when necessity is evident, for the sake of caution (ihtiyat).

Key Terms
پنچائیت (panchayat): An informal arbitration council; the author discusses whether its decisions are legally binding.
ضَرُورَة (darura): Necessity that permits adopting a concession or another madhhab's ruling to avoid hardship.
فتویٰ (fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a qualified mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Because the panchayat must be respected.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may adopt a Maliki ruling only when necessity dictates and only in the specific issue that requires the concession.

Wife's Right to Faskh Due to Husband's Dangerous Insanity
Ruling and conditions for faskh due to dangerous insanity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for a wife's right to annul her marriage due to her husband's dangerous insanity and apply the Hanafi maxims that derive these conditions.

Core Idea
Dangerous insanity gives the wife the right to annul, but only if conditions not explicit in texts are derived via general principles.

This passage from a contemporary Hanafi work explains the ruling and procedure for a wife facing a dangerously insane husband. The author details the steps before the qadi, the one-year respite, and the conditions for the wife's option. Crucially, the passage demonstrates how Hanafi jurists derive conditions for this option using general legal maxims (qawa’id kulliyyah) rather than explicit texts, linking to Maliki sources for support.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish dangerous from minor insanity
Identify that only dangerous (khatir) insanity qualifies for the wife's right to faskh; minor insanity does not.
As stated in Mabsut and Kitab al-Athar.
2
Outline the procedural steps
The wife applies to the qadi, proves dangerous insanity, qadi grants one-year respite, then upon re-application and persistence, the wife is given the option in the same session.
The qadi addresses the guardian if any; otherwise appoints a representative.
3
List the four conditions derived from qawaid
1) No knowledge before marriage, 2) No consent after knowledge, 3) Exercise option in same session, 4) No voluntary intercourse or preliminaries after knowledge.
The first three are derived from the maxim: 'Options are restricted to the session and invalidated by prior consent or explicit acceptance.'
4
Understand the retroactive effect of faskh
The annulment by qadi completely nullifies the marriage, making it as if it never existed (raf' rather than just fasakh).
Terms used: 'رفع' in Kitab al-Athar, 'فسخ' in Fath al-Qadir.
5
Apply the maxims to similar scenarios
Use the general maxim to derive conditions for other options (e.g., khiyar al-'ayb) and note the Maliki source for confirmation.
The passage cites Maliki texts as supporting these conditions.

ضرر کا اندیشہ ہو تو قاضی مجنون کو ایک سال کی مہلت دے گا اور مجنون کے سی مال سے عورت کا نان و نفقہ ادا کیئے جانے کا حکم ہو گا۔ اگر اس زمانہ میں مجنون ٹھیک ہو جائے تو بہتر ہے ورنہ عورت کو نکاح فسخ کرنے کا اختیار ہے ۔ خطر ناک مجنون کا حکم تفریق کی دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ مجنون کی بیوی قاضی کی عدالت (یا شرعی کمیٹی میں ) درخواست ہے اور شوہر کا خطرناک مجنون ہونا ثابت کرے لیے قاضی (یا شرعی کمیٹی ) واقعہ کی تحقیق کرے اگر صحیح ثابت ہو تو مجنون کو علاج کے لیے ایک سال کی مہلت دے دے اور سال پورا ہونے پر اگر بیوی پھر درخواست دے اور شوہر کا من جنون ابھی تک موجود ہو تو عورت کو اختیار دے دیا جائے اگر اس پر عورت اسی مجلس اختیار میں علیحدگی کا مطالبہ کرے تو قاضی تفریق کر دے ریعنی نکاح فسخ کر دے جیسا کہ پہلے جواب میں فتاوی عالمگیری سے مذکور ہے ( اور یہ تفریق قاضی، نکاح کو بالکل ر کر دیا ہے یعنی نکاح کا لعدم متصور ہوگا جیسا کہ کتاب الاثار اور مبسوط سرخسی میں رو کا لفظ موجود ہے اور " فتح القد وغیرہ میں فسخ کا لفظ موجود ہے اور جو شرائط اختیار زوجہ عین کے لیے ہیں اور اس سے پہلے تفصیلی طور پر گزرچکی ہیں ان میں سے اکثر شرائط اختیار زوجہ مجنون کے لیے بھی نہیں جن کا خلاصہ یہ ہے ۔

-۳- جس وقت مہلت کا سال گزرنے کے بعد دوبارہ درخواست پر قاضی عورت کو اختیار دے دے تو عورت اُسی مجلس میں علیحدگی اختیار کرے اگر مجلس برخاست ہو گئی یا عورت خود یا کسی کے اٹھانے سے کھڑی ہوگئی تو اختیار نہیں رہے گا۔ " وهذه الشروط الثلاثه وان لو تكن مصرحة في كتينا الا ان القواعد الكليل المصرحه في المذهب تقتيضها فان امثال هذه الاختيارات تنقيد بالمجلس وتبطل باسلم قبل العقد وبتصريح الرضا بعد العقد وظاهر عبارة المالكيرية - في قول محمد يو جله سنة كالعنة ثم يغير المرأة بعد الطول يريده والله اعلم

ان گر خود ممنون کو حکم نانا کافی نہیں۔ بلکہ اگر اس کا کوئی ولی ہو تو ولی جواب ہی کرے گا اور ولی ہی کو حکم مہلت کا اور بعد انقضاء مدت تفریق کا حکم سنایا جاوے گا اور اگر ولی نہ ہو تو قاضی کسی شخص کو مجنون کی طرف سے جوا برسی کے لیے مختار بنادے کما قال في البحر ( صفحه ۱۳۳ جلدم باب العنين) ويفرق بين هما إلى قوله بخصومة ولى ان كان والا فمن ينصبه القاضي الخرما منه

الله اعلم ١٣ منه
If there is fear of harm, the qadi will give the lunatic a one-year respite, and the wife's maintenance shall be paid from the lunatic's wealth. If during this time the lunatic recovers, it is good; otherwise the wife has the option to annul the marriage. The second case of separation due to dangerous lunacy is that the wife of the lunatic applies to the qadi's court (or the shari'ah committee) and proves that the husband is dangerously insane. The qadi (or shari'ah committee) investigates the matter; if it is proven true, he gives the lunatic a one-year respite for treatment. After the year, if the wife again applies and the husband's lunacy is still present, the woman is given the option. If in that same session of the option she demands separation, the qadi effects a separation, i.e., annuls the marriage, as mentioned earlier from Fatawa 'Alamgiri. (And this separation by the qadi completely nullifies the marriage, i.e., the marriage is considered as if it never existed, as the word 'رفع' (lifted) is present in Kitab al-Athar and Mabsut al-Sarakhsi, and the word 'فسخ' (annulment) is present in Fath al-Qadir etc. The conditions for the wife's option in cases of impotence were detailed previously; most of them also apply to the option of the wife of a lunatic. Their summary is: 1) The woman did not know of the husband's insanity before marriage. 2) Upon learning of the insanity, she did not express consent. It should be clear that for minor insanity, the wife has no right to annul the marriage, as stated in Mabsut and Kitab al-Athar. 3) When after the year of respite the qadi gives the woman the option upon her second application, she must exercise the separation in that same sitting; if the sitting ends or she stands up on her own or someone lifts her, the option is lost. 'And these three conditions, even if not explicitly stated in our books, the general principles explicitly stated in the school require them, for such options are restricted to the sitting and are invalidated by [؟] before the contract and by expressing consent after the contract. It is apparent from the Maliki statement that in the view of Muhammad, he grants a year like the impotent, then the woman has [؟] after the [؟]. And Allah knows best. 4) Another condition for the wife of the lunatic's right of annulment to be lost is that after learning of the lunacy that is grounds for annulment, she did not allow intercourse or its preliminaries (like lustful kissing, lying down with the husband) by her own choice, contrary to the case of the impotent, because in that case the purpose is choice and testing. These conditions are not explicit in our books, but the purport of the principles is explicit in Maliki books, as will come from Sharh al-Dardir. Moreover, it is not sufficient to address the lunatic himself with the command; rather, if he has a guardian, the guardian will be addressed, and the command of respite and the command of separation after the term are given to the guardian. If there is no guardian, the qadi appoints someone as representative for the lunatic for the lawsuit. As stated in al-Bahr (page 133, vol. [؟], chapter of the impotent): 'Separation is made between them ... up to his saying: by the lawsuit of the guardian if there is one, otherwise the qadi appoints someone.' From this: And we have not seen the condition that she be not retqa' (female impotent) or qarqa' (another defect) in the option of insanity; apparently it is not a condition. Similarly the condition of her being a virgin [؟]. It is appropriate to stipulate that he [؟] and wait if she is not [؟] based on the case of the impotent's wife. Allah knows best. 13 from it.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage addresses a ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding the wife's right to annul her marriage (faskh) when the husband is dangerously insane (majnun khatir). The passage begins by stating the procedure: if harm is feared, the qadi grants the lunatic a one-year respite for treatment, during which the wife's maintenance is paid from his wealth. If he recovers, the marriage continues; otherwise, the wife may annul. The author then details the steps: the wife applies to the qadi, proves the dangerous insanity, the qadi investigates, grants a year, then upon re-application, gives the wife an option in the same session. The annulment is retroactive (the marriage is considered as if it never existed), using the term 'رفع' (lifting) in Kitab al-Athar and Mabsut, and 'فسخ' in Fath al-Qadir. The author then lists three conditions derived from general principles (al-qawa'id al-kulliyyah) even though not explicit in the madhhab's books: 1) the wife did not know of the insanity before marriage, 2) she did not consent after learning, 3) she exercises the option in the same session of the qadi's grant. A fourth condition is added later: that after learning of the insanity, she did not voluntarily allow intercourse or its preliminaries, unlike the case of the impotent ('anin) where the aim is testing. The passage also clarifies that the lunatic himself is not addressed; his guardian is the proper party, and if none, the qadi appoints a representative. Finally, it notes that conditions like the wife being free from certain defects (rutaqah, qarna') are not required in the case of insanity, contrary to some cases. The commentary highlights the Hanafi method of deriving conditions by applying general maxims and citing Maliki texts as support.

Key Terms
مجنون (majnun): Person suffering from insanity. Here specifically dangerous (خطرناک) lunacy that justifies annulment.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract, making it as if it never existed (relates back).
اختیار (ikhtiyar): Option or choice given to the wife to annul or stay, restricted to the same session (مجلس).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the wife stands up or the session ends after the qadi gives her the option to annul the marriage due to her husband's dangerous insanity?
A) She can still annul the marriage later because the option continues.
B) Her option is lost and she cannot annul the marriage.
C) She must apply again for a new option.
D) The qadi automatically annuls the marriage.

Key Takeaway
The wife's right to faskh due to dangerous insanity is subject to conditions derived from general Hanafi maxims, including lack of prior knowledge, no consent after knowledge, exercise in the same session, and no voluntary intercourse after knowledge.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Following Another Madhhab in Necessity
Ruling on inter-madhhab fatwa in necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a fatwa that follows a non-Hanafi madhhab in a case of severe necessity, ensuring all conditions of that madhhab are observed and avoiding talfiq.

Core Idea
Following another madhhab in necessity is permissible but requires full adoption of that madhhab's conditions — not piecemeal cherry-picking.

When a Hanafi mufti faces a case where the Hanafi ruling causes severe hardship — such as a woman unable to obtain maintenance — he may turn to another madhhab for a more lenient ruling. However, this is not a license for eclecticism. This lesson, drawn from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's work, clarifies that adopting another madhhab requires fully implementing all its conditions and avoiding talfiq (patchworking). The passage also illustrates the proper methodology: seeking detailed fatwas from scholars of that madhhab, as Thanwi did from Maliki scholars in Madinah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the necessity threshold
Determine whether the situation qualifies as severe necessity (darurat shadida) — e.g., inability to secure nafaqah or fear of falling into sin. Without genuine hardship, the original Hanafi ruling should be followed.
The passage states: 'as long as the woman can exercise patience, it is necessary to adhere to the original Hanafi madhhab.'
2
Select the target madhhab and verify its ruling
Choose the non-Hanafi madhhab that addresses the need (here, Maliki). Ascertain all conditions and restrictions of that madhhab for the specific issue. The mufti must not rely on secondhand reports; he should obtain authoritative fatwas from scholars of that madhhab.
Thanwi sent detailed questions to Maliki scholars in Madinah three times to ensure accuracy.
3
Guard against talfiq
Ensure that the fatwa does not combine elements from multiple madhhabs in a way that creates a ruling recognized by no madhhab. Talfiq is invalid by consensus. The fatwa must be fully consistent with the chosen madhhab's conditions.
The passage cites al-Haskafi and al-Shami: 'talfiq is invalid by consensus.'
4
Construct the fatwa with proper authority
Issue the fatwa citing the source madhhab and its conditions. State that the original Hanafi ruling is set aside due to necessity, and that all conditions of the adopted madhhab are fulfilled. Reference the fatwa collection and the correspondence with scholars for authenticity.
Thanwi notes that after correspondence, the fatwas were included in his book with numbered references.

مختار کے تحت ہے : وان الرجوع من التقليد بعد العمل باطل اتفاقاً وانه يجوز له العمل بما يخالف ما حمله على مذهبه مقلدا فيه الخ لہذا اس مسئلہ مفقود ہیں مالکیہ کی تمام شرائط الکیہ کی ام را کالی مروری را ملی کرنا نادم ہوا اور امی دیر علماء وغیرہ اخاف نے اس کے متعلق جو مذہب مالکیہ سے نقل کیا ہے وہ محض احتمال تھا۔ اور مسئلہ کی مکمل وضاحت اور اس کے تمام قیود و شرائط علماء مالکیہ سے ہی معلوم ہو سکتے تھے اس وجہ سے اس ضرورت کا احساس کر کے مسلک امام مالک کے مفتیانِ کرام کی خدمت میں مدینہ منورہ (زادها الله شرفا و تعظیما) تفصیلی طور پر سوال بھیجا گیا ، وہاں کے متعدد علماء محققین نے نہایت تفصیل اور وضاحت سوالات کی ضرورت ہوئی تو تیسری مرتبہ اُن حضرات کی خدمت میں سوالات ارسال کر کے ہوابات لیے گئے۔ یہ تمام خط وکتابت مدرسہ امداد العلوم تھانہ بھون میں محفوظ و ہے اور ان فتاویٰ کا مجموعہ اس کتاب کے آخیر میں شریک اشاعت کر دیا گیا ہے ان فتاوی کی جس جس عبارت سے ہمارے سوالات کا جواب نکلتا ہے اُن تمام پر الفاظ سے نمبر ڈال دیئے گئے ہیں اور جوابات مندرجہ ذیل میں ان عبارات کے حوالہ پر اکتفاء کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ عوام کو تو عربی عبارات کی ضرورت نہیں اور اہل علم حضرات اس نمبر کے حوالہ سے آخیر رسالہ میں استدلال کی عبارت خود ملا حظہ سکتے ہیں اب سوالات اور جوابات اُردو میں یہاں پیش کئے جاتے ہیں۔
Lewis... in my opinion... meaning: If in severe necessity a fatwa is given on a non-[Hanafi] madhhab, then my opinion is that there is no harm in it. And for some time, the honored muftis and the fatwa department in and out of the city have almost all chosen to give fatwa on this view, and this issue has now, in one respect, entered Hanafi fiqh itself. But as long as the woman can exercise patience, it is necessary to adhere to the original Hanafi madhhab. However, at times of severe necessity, when arrangements for women's expenses (nafaqah) cannot be made, or sitting [in patience] is not considered appropriate due to fear of falling into sin, then there is no harm in acting on the Maliki madhhab. And for such situations this fatwa has been compiled. But to adopt the madhhab of another imam in any matter, it is necessary that all the conditions that are required according to that imam in that matter be observed. The argument from the statement of Allamah Shami is under consideration: 'Indeed, talfiq is invalid by consensus.' And al-Shami said beneath it: 'Its example: a person who had wudu, had a wet spot on his body, touched a woman, then prayed; the validity of this prayer is talfiq from the Shafi'i and Hanafi madhhabs, and talfiq is invalid, etc.' Also in Shami, from Allamah Shurunbulali under al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'Indeed, returning from taqlid after action is invalid by agreement, and it is permissible for him to act contrary to what he previously followed as taqlid of his madhhab, etc.' Therefore, in this matter, all the conditions of the Malikis are missing... the Maliki... what was transmitted from the Maliki madhhab about it was merely a probability. And the complete clarification of the matter and all its restrictions and conditions could only be known from the Maliki scholars. For this reason, feeling this need, a detailed question was sent to the honored muftis of the Maliki school in Madinah Munawwarah (may Allah increase it in honor and veneration). Many scholarly investigators there wrote answers with great detail and clarity, but then some doubts remained and some new questions arose, so those honored muftis were inconvenienced to write a second response. After the second responses, there was still need for some more questions, so a third time questions were sent to them and answers were obtained. All this correspondence is preserved in Madrasah Imdad al-Ulum, Thana Bhawan, and the collection of these fatwas has been included at the end of this book. On each phrase of these fatwas from which the answer to our questions emerges, numbers have been placed with words, and in the answers below, suffice has been made with reference to these phrases, because the common people do not need Arabic phrases, and the learned can themselves see the evidentiary phrases from the number reference at the end of the treatise. Now the questions and answers are presented here in Urdu.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of a Hanafi mufti issuing a fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab in cases of severe necessity. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, begins by citing an opinion (likely from a prior scholar) that there is no harm in such a practice. He notes that this has become the established practice among contemporary muftis, to the extent that it is now considered part of Hanafi fiqh in a sense. However, he emphasizes that the original Hanafi madhhab should be adhered to unless there is genuine necessity, such as when a woman cannot obtain maintenance (nafaqah) or fears falling into sin. In such cases, the Maliki madhhab may be followed, but only by observing all its conditions. The author then invokes two key principles from Hanafi usul al-fiqh: (1) talfiq (patchworking between madhhabs) is invalid by consensus, as stated by al-Haskafi and al-Shami; (2) returning from taqlid after acting is invalid, but it is permissible to act contrary to one's previous taqlid if one now follows another madhhab. The author clarifies that the earlier transmission of the Maliki view was merely probable, so he sought detailed answers from Maliki scholars in Madinah through a three-stage correspondence to ensure all conditions are met. The fatwas obtained are appended to the book. The passage concludes by introducing the upcoming questions and answers in Urdu.

Key Terms
تلفیق (talfiq): Patchworking together parts of different madhhabs in a single action to achieve a ruling not recognized by any madhhab
ضرورت شدیدہ (darurat shadida): A situation of extreme necessity where following the original madhhab would cause unbearable hardship or sin
مفقود الخبر (mafqud al-khabar): A person whose whereabouts and life status are unknown despite investigation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a mufti do to avoid talfiq when issuing a fatwa based on a non-Hanafi madhhab?
A) Choose only the easiest parts of the other madhhab.
B) Follow all conditions of that madhhab for the specific issue.
C) Obtain permission from a Maliki scholar for each fatwa.
D) Never combine elements from different madhhabs in general.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may give a fatwa by a non-Hanafi madhhab in severe necessity, but must fully adopt that madhhab's ruling with all its conditions to avoid talfiq.

Substitutes for the Qadi in Non-Muslim Lands
Ruling on who can adjudicate when no shari'ah judge exists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the valid substitutes for a qadi in missing husband cases and state the conditions for their decisions to be binding.

Core Idea
When no qadi exists, a Muslim official or a shari'ah committee can issue a binding dissolution.

This passage addresses a pressing issue for Muslims living under non-Islamic law: how to obtain a shari'ah ruling when there is no qadi. It identifies two bodies that can step in—Muslim government officials and shari'ah committees—and emphasizes that their decisions are valid only if they follow the shari'ah conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary problem
Recognize that the passage addresses the absence of a shari'ah judge (qadi) in non-Muslim lands, creating a need for substitutes.
The context is missing husband cases, but the principle extends to other adjudicative needs.
2
Parse the first substitute
Identify that Muslim government officials with authority to decide such cases are one valid substitute.
These officials must be Muslims and decide according to shari'ah.
3
Extract the condition for the first substitute
Note the condition: the official must be Muslim and his decision must conform to shari'ah.
4
Parse the second substitute
Identify the shari'ah committee (a group of pious Muslims) as another valid substitute when no suitable official exists.
The committee must follow the same conditions as the qadi.
5
Note the overriding requirement
Understand that both substitutes must adhere to the conditions mentioned earlier in the book (e.g., proper investigation, following the madhhab of the wife).
These conditions are not repeated here but are essential for validity.

پانچویں سوال کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قاضی کے فیصلہ کے قائم مقام حضرات جن ملکوں میں شرعی قاضی موجود نہیں جیسے اسلامی ریاستوں کے علاوہ ہندوستان کے تمام شہروں کی حالت ہے تو وہاں پر وہ حکام جو کہ گورنمنٹ کی جانب سے اس قسم کے معاملات کے فیصلہ کرنے کا اختیار رکھتے ہیں اگر وہ مسلمان ہوں اور فیصلہ شریعت کے مطابق کریں تو ان کا فیصلہ بھی قاضی کے فیصلہ کے قائم مقام کہلاتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ گزر چکا۔ مسلمان حاکم نہ ملنے کی صورت میں کیا کریں کی جگہ اگر مسلمان حاکم موجود نہ ہو یا اُس کی عدالت سے شریعت کے قانون کے مطابق فیصلہ نہ ہوتا ہو تو پھر مذکورہ مذہب کے موافق دین دار مسلمانوں کی ایک جماعت بنا کر یعنی شرعی کمیٹی بنا کر مذکورہ بالا بیان کے مطابق تحقیق کرے اور مکمل تحقیق کے بعد فیصلہ دے تو یہ فیصلہ بھی قاضی کے فیصلہ کے درجہ میں ہوگا لیکن مذکورہ شرائط کے مطابق ہونا ضروری ہے جو کہ گزر چکیں ہیں۔
The answer to the fifth question is that the substitutes for the qadi: in countries where no shari'ah judge exists, as is the condition of all cities of India besides Islamic states, then those officials who have the authority from the government to decide such cases — if they are Muslims and they decide according to the shari'ah, then their decision is also called a substitute for the qadi's decision, as has passed. In the place of what to do if a Muslim ruler is not found: if a Muslim ruler is not present or his court does not decide according to the law of the shari'ah, then form a group of pious Muslims according to the aforementioned school, i.e., form a shari'ah committee, and investigate according to the above statement, and after complete investigation give a decision — then this decision will also be in the rank of the qadi's decision, but it is necessary that it be according to the mentioned conditions that have passed.

Commentary
This passage addresses the fifth question about who can act as a qadi in places where no shari'ah judge exists, such as non-Muslim states. It provides two alternatives. First, if a Muslim government official with authority to decide such cases exists and he judges according to shari'ah, his decision is considered a valid substitute for a qadi's ruling. Second, if no such Muslim official exists or his court does not apply shari'ah, then a committee of pious Muslims (shari'ah committee) should be formed, following the madhhab of the wife (or the relevant school), to investigate and decide. Such a decision is also valid. However, it must meet the conditions mentioned earlier in the book. This ruling is part of the hila for the wife of a missing husband to obtain a dissolution, providing a practical solution in non-shari'ah jurisdictions.

Key Terms
قاضی (qadi): A shari'ah court judge with jurisdiction over legal cases.
شرعی کمیٹی (shari'ah committee): A group of pious Muslims formed to adjudicate in the absence of a qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Marriage Without Guardian: The Role of Sultan's Jurisdiction
Parsing a ruling from Radd al-Mukhtar on territorial jurisdiction in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on marriage without a guardian in jurisdictions lacking a sultan to modern fatwa cases.

Core Idea
For a marriage without a guardian, the sultan's jurisdiction determines validity — without it, the contract is void.

This lesson examines a key rule from Radd al-Mukhtar about the marriage of a minor girl (or insane woman) who contracts her own marriage without a guardian. The central condition is the presence of a sultan or his delegate at the place of contract. Understanding this territorial requirement is essential for muftis dealing with diaspora communities where no Muslim authority exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Terms
First, identify the terms 'wilayah', 'sultan', and 'qadi' in the passage. Understand that 'wilayah' here refers to the guardianship authority of the Muslim ruler.
The passage uses 'sultan' and 'hakim' interchangeably.
2
Parse the Ruling's Condition
The ruling states that if the marriage occurs in a place with a sultan, it is suspended (tawaqquf). If no sultan or judge is present, the marriage is void. Determine the condition: the contract must be within the sultan's territorial authority.
The passage emphasizes 'fi mawdi' al-'aqd' (in the place of the contract).
3
Distinguish Scenarios
Apply the condition to two scenarios: with a sultan (suspended and effective after puberty) vs. without a sultan (void from the outset). Identify the types of locations mentioned: land of the Arabs, sea, desert, non-Muslim land.
4
Analyze the Maliki Comparison
The passage references the Maliki view that a judge cannot marry a woman outside his jurisdiction even if she is from his area. This reinforces the territorial condition. Note the agreement in principle.
The Hanafi position is not contradicted but rather supported by this.
5
Derive the Fatwa Hierarchy
Based on the passage, identify the mufta bihi ruling: the marriage is void if no sultan or judge is present. Recognize that this ruling comes from later Hanafi authorities like Ibn Abidin (Radd al-Mukhtar).
This rule is part of the mufti's methodology (rasm al-mufti) for assessing marriage contracts.

مفقود کے معاملہ میں برابر شمار ہوں گے ۔
رو المختار جلد ۲ باب الولی ہیں ہے : " وصغيرة زوجت نفسها ولا ولى وان حاكو تمه توقف ونفذ با جان ها بعد بلو عنها لان له مميزاً وهو السلطان. قوله ولا حاكو شمه اى فى موضع العقد - قوله توقف هذا مبنى على كفاية ذالك المكان تحت ولايته السلطان وان لم يكن تحت ولاية قاضي وعليه فبطلات العقد يتصور فيما اذا كان في دار العرب او البحر او المفازة ونحو ذلك بغلاف القرى والامصار ويدل عليه ما في العقد في فصل الوكالة بالنكاح حيث قال وما لا يجيز له اى ما ليس له من يقدر على الاجازة يبطل كما اذا كانت تحتدحرة فزيجه الفضولي امة اواخت امرأته او خامسة وزوجة معقدة او مجنونة او صغيرة يتيمة في دار العزب او اذا العريكن سلطان ولا قاض لحد ممن يقدر على الامضاء حالة العقد فوقع بالملك اهـ

بات كانت خارجة عنها اولا ولاية عليها وان كان اصلها من اهلها اه - صفحه ۹۶ جلد ۳) والله اعلم
They will be considered equal in the matter of the missing person. Radd al-Mukhtar, volume 2, chapter of the guardian, states: "And a minor girl who marries herself, and there is no guardian, and if there is a ruler, it is suspended, and it becomes effective after her coming of age, because he (the ruler) has authority, and that is the sultan. His saying: 'and there is no ruler' means in the place of the contract. His saying: 'it is suspended' is based on the sufficiency of that place being under the sultan's authority, even if it is not under the authority of a judge. Based on this, the invalidity of the contract can be conceived when it occurs in the land of the Arabs, or the sea, or the desert, and similar places, excluding villages and cities. This is indicated by what is in al-'Aqd in the chapter of agency in marriage, where he said: 'And what does not have one to authorize it becomes invalid, as when a woman is deceived, and the unauthorised agent marries her to a slave, or the sister of his wife, or a fifth wife, or a woman insane, or a minor orphan in the land of the non-Muslims, or if there is neither sultan nor judge, from those who have the power to execute at the time of the contract, so the marriage occurs by possession.' Because in this narration, 'insane woman' and 'minor in the land of war' is general, including whether she was originally in the land of war or previously in the land of Islam and then went to the land of war. Due to this generality, it is established that previous guardianship is not considered. Otherwise, that insane woman and minor who went from the land of Islam would have choice. Also, the statement of al-Shami: 'i.e., in the place of the contract' and 'that place under the authority of the sultan' makes it clear that for guardianship, being in the territory of the sultan and ruler is a condition. And the Malikis have clearly stated this. Thus in Sharh Dardir: 'The judge cannot marry a woman, i.e., he does not undertake the marriage contract for a woman who has no guardian except the ruler, and she is not under his authority if she is outside it, and there is no guardianship over her even if her origin is from its people' - page 96, volume 3. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a legal analysis of a ruling from Radd al-Mukhtar concerning the marriage of a minor girl (or insane woman) who contracts her own marriage without a guardian. The Hanafi position, as presented, is that if such a marriage occurs in a place under the authority of a sultan (i.e., a Muslim ruler), the marriage is suspended (tawaqquf) and becomes effective only after she attains puberty and the sultan or his delegate approves. The key condition is that the contract must take place within the sultan's jurisdiction. If the marriage occurs in a place where there is no sultan or judge (e.g., the desert, the sea, a non-Muslim land), the contract is void from the outset. This is derived from the general principle that the sultan is the guardian for those without a guardian. The passage also references the Maliki view, which similarly holds that a judge cannot marry a woman who is not under his territorial authority, even if she originally came from his jurisdiction. The analysis clarifies that prior guardianship (e.g., from the land of Islam) does not carry over when the woman moves to a place without that authority. This ruling has practical significance for the fatwa of a missing person (mafqud), as it establishes the importance of jurisdiction in marriage contracts.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship or authority over someone, specifically the sultan's authority to sanction marriage for those without a guardian.
سلطان (sultan): The Muslim ruler or his representative who has the authority to approve the marriage of a woman without a guardian.
قاضی (qadi): A judge appointed by the sultan to adjudicate matters, including marriage contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from Radd al-Mukhtar, what is the ruling on the marriage of a minor girl who marries herself without a guardian in a place where there is a sultan?
A) The marriage is void immediately.
B) The marriage is valid and effective immediately.
C) The marriage is suspended until she attains puberty and the sultan approves.
D) The marriage is valid only if she is not an orphan.

Key Takeaway
For a marriage without a guardian, the sultan's territorial authority determines validity: with it, the marriage is suspended; without it, void.

Fatwa Hierarchy: Tafriq as Talaq Bain
Fatwa clarification on the nature of tafriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the operative (mufta bihi) ruling for judicial separation (tafriq) in the Hanafi school and apply the mufti's hierarchy to choose between conflicting opinions.

Core Idea
Judicial separation is talaq bain – the husband cannot take his wife back without a new marriage contract.

In this passage, the author addresses a key question for a Hanafi mufti: when a qadi separates a couple due to harm or lack of maintenance, is that separation revocable (raj'i) or irrevocable (bain)? Two valid opinions exist within the school, but the author clarifies the relied-upon view. By working through this passage, you will learn how a mufti navigates intra-school disputes and arrives at the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible rulings
Locate where the author states 'One is that this tafriq be considered talaq raj'i...' and 'My opinion is that this tafriq be considered talaq bain'. Note the two competing views.
The first view (raj'i) allows the husband to take his wife back without a new marriage during the waiting period. The second (bain) requires a fresh contract.
2
Identify the preferred view and its authority
Find where the author mentions 'Allamah Salih' and his fatwa. The author adopts this view, saying 'our fatwa is...'
The preference is based on a reliable later scholar's opinion (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
3
Determine the practical consequences
Read what happens if the husband reforms during the waiting period: the wife must stay with him even without her consent, and a new marriage is recommended as a precaution.
This shows the ruling is talaq bain but includes a concession for reform – the wife must not leave, but the marriage is not automatically restored.
4
Classify the authority weight
Assess whether the preferred view comes from zahir al-riwayah, nawadir, or fatawa mutakhkhirin. The passage cites Allamah Salih, a later authority.
This is from fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatawa). The mufti is bound to follow the mufta bihi among later scholars.
5
Apply the rasm al-mufti rule
Explain why the author chooses one view over the other: 'consideration' and reliance on Allamah Salih. This reflects the principle that a mufti follows the weightier opinion in the school.
In Hanafi ifta, the mufti must choose between valid transmissions according to hierarchy (zahir riwayah > nawadir > fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک یہ کہ اس تفریق کو طلاق رجعی قرار دیا جائے اور عدت کے اندراندر رجعت کو صحیح قرار دیا جائے ۔ تفریق شرعی ، طلاق بائن کے حکم میں ہے جو میرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ اس تفریق کو طلاق بائن قرار دیا جائے اور شوہر کو بیوی کو نکاح میں لوٹانے کا اختیار نہ دیا جائے لیکن حضرت علامہ صالح نے پہلے احتمال یعنی طلاق بائن قرار دینے کو زیادہ قریب (بہتر) قرار دیا ہے جیسا کہ روایت کا اور علامہ صالح کے فتویٰ کی تلخیص میں ہے اور ہمیں بھی علامہ صالح کی رائے اور اُن کے فتویٰ میں عذر کرنے کے بعد درست معلوم ہوتی ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے ہمارے نزدیک فتوی یہی ہے کہ عدت کے اندر شوہر کے تعنت (بیوی کے حقوق سے لا پرواہ ہونے سے) باز آجانے کی صورت میں عورت کو اسی کے پاس رہنا پڑے گا۔ چاہے عورت راضی ہو یا نہ ہو کیونکہ رجعت میں عورت کی رضامندی ضروری نہیں ہے لیکن اگر احتیاطا دوبارہ نکاح پڑھا دیا جائے تو بہتر ہے۔ اور اسی مرد کے پاس رہنا ضروری ہے اس لیے عورت کو بھی لازم ہے کہ تجدید نکاح کرے لیکن اگر عورت اپنی بیوقوفی سے تجدید نکاح نہ کرے تو مرد کو جائز ہے کہ بدون تجدید ہی سے
One is that this tafriq be considered talaq raj'i and ruju' within the waiting period be considered valid. Judicial tafriq is in the ruling of talaq bain. My opinion is that this tafriq be considered talaq bain and the husband not be given authority to return the wife to marriage. But Allamah Salih (may Allah have mercy on him) considered the first probability, i.e., declaring it talaq bain, as closer (better), as is in the summary of the narration and the fatwa of Allamah Salih. And to us also, after consideration, his opinion and his fatwa appear correct. For this reason, our fatwa is that if within the waiting period the husband desists from his obstinacy (disregard of the wife's rights), the woman must stay with him, whether she agrees or not, because the wife's consent is not necessary for ruju'. But it is better to perform a new marriage as a precaution. And it is necessary to stay with that husband; therefore, it is also necessary for the woman to renew the marriage. But if the woman out of foolishness does not renew the marriage, then the husband is permitted to (continue) without renewal.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of judicial separation (tafriq) in Hanafi fiqh. The author presents two possible views: whether tafriq is treated as talaq raj'i (revocable) or talaq bain (irrevocable). He prefers the view of Allamah Salih that it is talaq bain, meaning the husband cannot take his wife back during the waiting period without a new marriage contract. However, if the husband reforms his behavior during the waiting period, the wife must stay with him regardless of her consent, as ruju' does not require her agreement. Nevertheless, performing a fresh marriage contract is recommended as a precaution. The passage underscores the importance of following the preferred fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation ordered by a qadi due to harm or lack of maintenance.
رجعت (ruju‘): Returning to the wife during the waiting period after a revocable divorce.
طلاق بائن (talaq bain): Irrevocable divorce; the couple cannot reunite without a new marriage contract.
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj‘i): Revocable divorce; the husband can take his wife back during the iddah without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The wife must stay with her husband, and a new marriage contract is recommended.
C) The husband must seek the wife's permission to return.
D) The separation is automatically cancelled and they are still married without any action.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, judicial separation (tafriq) is treated as talaq bain, but if the husband reforms during the iddah, the wife must stay and renewal of marriage is recommended as a precaution.

Procedure for Qadi on Separation Due to Musaharat
Procedural steps for qadi in musaharat claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to execute the procedural steps for a qadi when a wife claims separation due to musaharat, distinguishing claims against the husband from claims against relatives, and apply the appropriate oath formulations.

Core Idea
The burden shifts from husband's denial to wife's witnesses to husband's oath, with oath wording depending on the accused party.

In Hanafi family law, when a wife claims that an incident of musaharat (prohibited relationship) has occurred, the qadi follows a specific procedure to determine the truth and whether separation is warranted. This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah outlines that procedure, including the distinction between claims against the husband's own act and claims against another relative, the role of witnesses, and the oath formulations. Additionally, the author discusses the permissibility of talfiq (combining madhhabs) as a legal stratagem and warns against explicit zina accusations to avoid the hadd of qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim type
Determine whether the wife's claim is that the husband himself committed the prohibited act (e.g., grasping a relative with desire) or that another person (e.g., father-in-law) committed it. This determines the subsequent procedure.
The claim type affects the wording of the husband's oath.
2
Apply the procedural sequence
Follow the steps: (1) Take the husband's statement. If he denies, (2) demand witnesses from the wife. If no witnesses or conditions of testimony are met, (3) offer an oath to the husband.
The burden of proof is on the claimant; the defendant's denial is accepted upon oath.
3
Distinguish between oath types
If the husband is accused, he swears that he did not do the act or did not do it with desire. If another person is accused, he swears that his predominant belief is that the wife is not truthful, because he cannot swear about another's actions.
The oath for a third-party claim is based on the husband's state of belief.
4
Recognize acts establishing musaharat
Certain acts (kissing lips/cheek, touching private parts, touching breast) automatically establish musaharat without proof of desire. Grasping and touching require desire. This distinction affects what needs to be proven in court.
The requirement of desire is specific to Hanafi jurisprudence.
5
Apply the talfiq caution
Understand that talfiq (combining madhhabs) is permissible in this case with caution. Avoid explicit mention of zina to prevent the hadd of qadhf if witnesses cannot be produced.
This procedural caution is a key aspect of the mufti's role in drafting claims.

فیصلہ کا طریقہ جس وقت عورت دعوی کرے کہ " میرے شوہر اور میرے درمیان کے اصول و فروع یعنی اوپر کے پانچویں کے رشتوں میں سے فلاں شخص کے درمیان یا شوہر اور میرے اصول و فروع میں سے فلاں عورت کے درمیان اس قسم کا واقعہ پیش آیا ہے جو کہ حرمت مصاہرت کا باعث ہے اس وجہ سے مجھ کو میرے شوہر سے علیحدہ کر دیا جائے تو قاضی یا اس کا قائم مقام پہلے تو شوہر سے بیان سے (یعنی جواب دعوی ہے) اور اگر شوہر نے اس دعوی کی تصدیق نہ کی تو عورت سے گواہ لیے جائیں اگر گواہ پیش نہ ہوں یا ان میں شرائط گواہی موجود نہ ہوں تو شوہر سے حلف لیا جائے اگر وہ حلف کرے تو مقدمہ خارج کر دیا جائے یعنی نہ تفریق کی جائے اور نہ یہ فیصلہ کیا جائے کہ عورت بدستور شوہر کے ساتھ رہے اور اگر قاضی نے عورت کو اُس کے نکاح میں ہی رہنے کا حکم دے دیا تو اس صورت کا حکم آگے مذکور ہے۔ اور اگر وہ حلف سے انکار کر دے تو تفریق کر دی جائے۔

اگر شوہر کے فعل پر دعویٰ ہو مثلا یہ کہ اس نے بیوی کے اصول اور فروع میں سے فلاں عورت کو شہوت کے ساتھ پکڑا ہے جب تو شوہر سے حلف اس بات پر لیا جائے کہ اُس نے یہ فعل ہرگز نہیں کیا یا شہوت کے ساتھ نہیں کیا اور اگر دوسرے شخص کے فعل پر دعویٰ تھا مثلاً عورت اس طریقہ سے کہے کہ مجھ کو خسر نے شہوت کے ساتھ پکڑا ہے تو شوہر سے اس طریقہ سے حلف لیا جائے گا کہ خدا کی قسم میرا زیادہ تر خیال یہ ہے کہ عورت اس دعوی میں سچی نہیں اور اس واقعہ کا ہونا یا شہوت کے ساتھ ہونا میرے دل کو نہیں لگتا۔ حرمت مصاہرت سے تعلق ایک ضروری مسئلہ اور گواہ میں تفصیل ہے کہ ہونٹ اور گال پر بوسہ دینے اور شرمگاہ یا عضو مخصوص چھونے اور پستان چھونے کے دعوی میں تو صرف ان افعال کی گواہی دینے سے حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہو جائے گی شہوت کا بیان ضروری نہیں لیکن پکڑنے اور ہاتھ لگانے میں شہوت کا اعتبر ہے جس کی تفصیل صفحہ کے حاشیہ ۲ میں گزر چکی ہے مطلقا پکڑنا یا ہاتھ لگانا معتبر نہیں۔ منہ سے شامی وغیرہ کی عبارت سے مستفاد ہوتا ہے کہ نفی علم اور نفی اطمینان پر حلف کر لینا کافی ہے۔ ہمارے محاورہ میں یہ الفاظ اس کا ترجمہ ہے۔ اگر کسی جگہ کا عرف اس کے خلاف ہو تو اہل عرف سے تحقیق کر کے وہاں کے مناسب الفاظ تجویز کر لیے جائیں۔

پس تلفیق کی یہ صورت ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے جس کی تائید علامہ محمد بن علی بیضاوی مفتی مالکیہ کے فتوے کی روایت سے بھی ہوتی ہے تاہم عمل کے وقت احتیاط یہ ہے کہ عمل کرنے والا جواز تلفیق کے بارے میں کسی اپنے معتقد نیہ عالم محقق سے رجوع کر کے اُن کے فتوے پر عمل کرے۔ واللہ اعلم۔ ایک بات یاد رکھنے کے قابل یہ ہے کہ اگر واقعہ زنا کا پیش آیا ہو تو دوسرے میں زنا کو صراحتہ ظاہر نہ کیا جائے کیونکہ زنا کے دعوے پر چار گواہ پیش نہ ہو سکے تو حد قذف کا اندیشہ ہے، بلکہ صرف مباشرت فاحشہ وغیرہ کو بیان کرے یعنی یہ کہے کہ شرمگاہ کو شرمگاہ سے بغیر حائل کے لایا گیا ہے۔
The method of decision: When a woman claims, 'Between my husband and my usul and furu (i.e., the five prohibited relationships) such a person, or between my husband and my usul and furu such a woman, an incident occurred that causes the prohibition of musaharat, therefore separate me from my husband,' then the qadi or his deputy first takes a statement from the husband (i.e., his reply to the claim). If the husband does not affirm the claim, then witnesses are sought from the woman. If no witnesses are produced or they lack the conditions of testimony, then an oath is taken from the husband. If he takes the oath, the case is dismissed – i.e., no separation is made, nor is it decided that the woman should continue living with her husband? (and if the qadi ordered the woman to remain in his marriage, the ruling for that case is mentioned later). And if he refuses the oath, then separation is made.

If the claim is about the husband's act, e.g., that he grasped a certain woman from the wife's usul or furu with desire, then an oath is taken from the husband that he never did this act, or he did it without desire. And if the claim was about another person's act, e.g., the woman says in this manner, 'My father-in-law grasped me with desire,' then the oath will be taken from the husband in this way: 'By Allah, my predominant opinion is that the woman is not truthful in this claim, and I do not believe in my heart that this incident occurred or that it occurred with desire.' The relationship with musaharat is a necessary issue. And there is detail regarding witnesses: For claims of kissing the lips or cheek, and touching the private part or specific limb, and touching the breast, then giving testimony of these acts alone establishes musaharat; mentioning desire is not necessary. But for grasping and touching, desire is considered, whose detail has passed in the margin of page 2. Merely grasping or touching without desire is not considered. From the expressions in Shami etc., it is understood that an oath negating knowledge and negligence is sufficient. In our idiom, these words are its translation. If the custom of a place is contrary to this, then by investigating with the people of that custom, appropriate words should be devised.

Thus, this form of talfiq is permissible in our view, and it is also supported by a narration from Allamah Muhammad bin Ali al-Baydawi, the Maliki mufti. However, at the time of action, caution is that the one acting should refer to a just and scholarly authority regarding the permissibility of talfiq and act on his fatwa. And Allah knows best. One thing worth remembering is that if an incident of zina occurred, then one should not explicitly state zina in the claim, because if four witnesses cannot be produced for a claim of zina, there is fear of the hadd of qadhf; rather, only indecent intercourse etc. should be mentioned – i.e., say, 'The private part was brought to the private part without a barrier.'
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah presents the Hanafi procedural rules for a judge (qadi) when a wife claims that an incident has occurred causing prohibition by marriage (haram musaharat), and she seeks separation from her husband. The author outlines the step-by-step process: first, the husband is asked for his response; if he denies, the wife must produce witnesses; if she cannot, the husband is asked to swear an oath. If he swears, the case is dismissed and no separation occurs. If he refuses the oath, separation is decreed. The passage further distinguishes two situations: if the husband himself committed the prohibited act, he swears that he did not do it or did not do it with desire; if the act was committed by another person (such as the father-in-law), the husband swears that he believes the wife is lying. This distinction is due to the nature of the claim: the husband cannot swear about another's actions directly, so he swears on his own state of belief. The text also specifies which physical acts automatically establish musaharat (kissing, touching private parts, touching breast) regardless of desire, whereas grasping and touching require desire. Finally, the author discusses the permissibility of talfiq (combining different madhhabs) in such cases, warning that one should avoid explicit mention of zina to avoid the hadd of qadhf if witnesses cannot be produced. The overall framework follows the Hanafi principle that the burden of proof is on the claimant, and the denial of the defendant is accepted upon oath.

Key Terms
حرمت مصاہرت (hurmat musaharah): Prohibition of marriage due to an incestuous relationship between spouses and certain relatives, making the marriage invalid.
تلفیق (talfiq): Combining rulings from different madhhabs in a single legal situation to reach a permissible outcome.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina punishable by hadd unless proven by four witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi procedure in this passage, if a wife claims an incident of musaharat with her father-in-law (husband's father), what is the wording of the oath to be taken from the husband?
A) He swears that he himself did not commit the act.
B) He swears that his father did not commit the act.
C) He swears that he believes the wife is not truthful in her claim.
D) He swears that the act did not happen.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi procedure for musaharat claims protects the marriage by shifting the burden of proof to the wife, and the oath of the husband is tailored to the accused party.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Husband's Denial and Third Party Testimony in Hurmah Musaharah
Rules for establishing affinity prohibition through testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule to determine whether a husband's denial of kissing a wife's relative with desire is accepted, and assess the status of the third party's testimony.

Core Idea
The husband is believed with oath unless clear physical evidence contradicts; the third party is a witness, not defendant.

This lesson examines a critical fatwa scenario: when a wife claims her husband has committed an act that establishes hurmah musaharah (affinity prohibition) with her relative. The Hanafi school gives significant weight to the husband's denial, requiring an oath unless there is concrete evidence of desire. Equally important is the status of the third party who was allegedly involved—should they be treated as a defendant or a witness? Understanding these distinctions is essential for a mufti handling such sensitive cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and denial
Recognise that the wife claims a prohibited act (kissing/touching) with her relative, and the husband denies it. The act must be accompanied by desire to establish hurmah.
Desire is a condition per Hanafi school.
2
Apply the rule of tasdiq with yamin
The husband is believed (musaddaq) upon oath because he is the denier. This aligns with the general Hanafi principle: 'al-qawl lil-munkir' (the statement is for the denier).
Oath is mandatory; refusal may lead to divorce.
3
Evaluate evidence of desire
Despite the husband's denial, certain physical indications (qara'in) override tasdiq. Examples include: the husband standing with an erection, taking the breast, kissing on the mouth, or touching the private parts. If such signs exist, the wife's claim is upheld.
The text from al-Durr al-Muntaqa lists these exceptions.
4
Determine the third party's role
The third party (the relative) is not a defendant but a witness. They cannot be forced to make a statement as a defendant; their testimony is evaluated based on uprightness (adalah) and whether they confess to an immoral act.
This is derived from qawa'id: informing about another's right is testimony, not acknowledgment.

وذلك كله لما في الدر المنتقى: ادعت الشهرة في تقبيله او تقبيلها انبه وانكرها الرجل فهو مصدق إلا ان يقوم اليها منتشرا او ياخذ ثديها او يركب معها او يمسها على الفرج او يقبلها على الفم. قال الخدادي وفي الفتح يترأى الحاق الخدين بالفوالى ان قال وتقبل الشهادة على الاقراء باللمس والتقبيل. وانظر الى ذكره او فرجه عن شهوة في المختار تجنيس لان الشهرة مما يوقف عليها في الجملة بانتشار واثار. وفي رد المختار قوله: وادعت) ای ادعت الزوجة أنه قبل احد اصولها او فروعها بشهوة او ان احد اصولها او فروعها قبله بشهوة فهو مصدق لانه ينكر ثبوت العرمة والقول للمنكر. واما توجيه اليمين على الزوج فظاهر للقاعدة المفردة من ان قول المنكر انما يتحرر مع اليمين. ونص عليه الفقهاء في باب الرضاع وحرمة المساهرة نظير حرمة الرضاع. وأما الفاظ اليمين فما خوذه مما في الشامية عن الفتح وثبوت الحرمة بلمسها مشروط بان يصدقها ويقع فى اكبر رايه صدقها وعلى هذا ينبغي ان يقال في مسه ايا ما لا تحرم على ابيه وابنه الا ان يصدقاها او يغلب على ظنها صدقه. تو رأيت عن الى يوسف ما يفيد ذالك اه (شامی ۲۵ ج۲) تو ظاہر ہے کہ حرمت مصاہرت جن واقعات سے ثابت ہوتی ہے ان میں احد الزوجین کے ساتھ ایک اور کی شرکت بھی ہے اور واقعہ کی صحت و عدم صحت و نیز شہوت کے وجود و عدم کا اُس کو بھی علم ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن با وجود ستی بسیار کہیں یہ جوئیہ نہیں ملا کہ مقدمہ میں اُس سے بیان لیا جائے گا یا نہیں اور اگر اُس کا بیان ہو تو وہ کیا حیثیت رکھتا ہے ۔ لیکن قواعد میں غور و فکر کرنے کے بعد رحمان اس طرف ہے کہ وہ مدعا علیہ نہیں اس وجہ سے اس کو مدعا علیہ بنا کر بیان پر مجبور نہ کیا جائے بلکہ اس کو ایک گواہ سمجھا جائے۔ لأن الاخبار بحق الغير على الغير ليس با قرار بل هو شهادة والا قرار ايجار بحق عليه الغير كما هو مصرح في كتب الفقه . اور اُس کی گواہی معتبر ہونے نہ ہونے میں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ اگر وہ شخص اپنے دوسرے افعال و اقوال کے اعتبار سے عادل ہو ۔ اور اس واقعہ میں بھی کسی ایسے فعل کا اقرار نہیں ہے جو کہ مسقط عدالت ہو مثالاً ولی بالشبہ وغیرہ کا بیان دے جب تو اُس کی گواہی مقبول ہونے میں کچھ شہر نہیں۔ اور اگر کوئی ایسا فعل بیان کرے جس سے اس کا فسق ثابت ہوتا ہو تو اس کی یہ گوا ہی معتبر ہو گی یا نہیں ؟ اس میں
And all that is as in al-Durr al-Muntaqa: She claimed notoriety in his kissing or her kissing, and he denied it, so he is believed unless he stands up to her with an erection or takes her breast or rides with her or touches her on the private parts or kisses her on the mouth. Al-Khadadi said, and in al-Fath it appears that the cheeks are joined to the mouth? He said: And testimony is accepted concerning reports of touching and kissing. And look at his mentioning his private parts or his desire in al-Mukhtar? Tanzis? Because notoriety is learned generally by spreading and effects. And in Radd al-Mukhtar his saying: And she claimed) meaning the wife claimed that he kissed one of her ancestors or branches with desire, or that one of her ancestors or branches kissed him with desire, so he is believed because he denies the establishment of prohibition, and the statement is for the denier. And as for directing the oath to the husband, it is apparent because of the general rule that the statement of the denier is only binding with the oath. And the jurists have stated it in the chapter of breastfeeding and the prohibition of affinity similar to the prohibition of breastfeeding. And as for the wording of the oath, it is taken from al-Shamiyya from al-Fath: and the establishment of prohibition by touching is conditional on him believing her and it occurs in his greater opinion that she is truthful. And upon this, it should be said in his touching her that it does not become prohibited for his father and son unless they believe her or her truthfulness becomes predominant. So you saw from Abu Yusuf what benefits that. So it is apparent that the prohibition of affinity (hurmah musaharah) is established by events in which a third party shares with one of the spouses, and the correctness or incorrectness of the event, as well as the existence or absence of desire, are also known to that third party. But despite much investigation, it was not found whether his statement will be taken in the case or not, and if his statement is taken, what status does it have. But after reflection on the rules, the direction is that he is not the defendant, so he should not be forced to make a statement by making him a defendant, but rather he is considered a witness. Because informing about another's right against another is not an acknowledgment but is testimony, and acknowledgment is imposing a right against oneself as is stated in the books of fiqh. And regarding whether his testimony is acceptable, there is detail: if that person is upright (adil) according to his other actions and statements, and in this incident he does not acknowledge any act that would nullify his uprightness, such as if he gives a statement like 'wali bi shubha' etc., then there is no doubt that his testimony is accepted. And if he states an act by which his transgression (fisq) is established, then will this testimony be considered valid or not? There is [uncertainty].
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) for how a mufti or judge should handle claims of hurmah musaharah (affinity prohibition) based on testimony about physical acts. It opens by citing a ruling from al-Durr al-Muntaqa: if the wife claims her husband kissed her female relative (mother/daughter) with desire, the husband is believed upon denial unless there is external evidence of desire (erection, touching private parts, etc.). The husband's denial is given weight because he is the denier, but he must take an oath. The rule is parallel to rulings on breastfeeding prohibition (hurmat al-rida). The text then discusses the status of the third party (the person who was kissed/touched). The Hanafi position is that this third party is not a defendant (mudda'a alayh) but rather a witness (shahid). They should not be forced to make a statement as a defendant; instead, their testimony is evaluated on the basis of their moral uprightness (adalah). If the third party is upright and does not confess to an act that would disqualify them (e.g., fornication), their testimony is accepted. If they confess to an immoral act, their testimony's validity becomes questionable.

Key Terms
حرمت مصاہرت (hurmah musaharah): Prohibition of marriage due to affinity (e.g., between a man and his wife's mother/daughter after the marriage).
شہوت (shahwah): Sexual desire; presence is required for the act to establish hurmah.
تصدیق (tasdiq): Believing the denier's statement; the husband is believed in his denial of desire unless proven otherwise.
یمین (yamin): Oath taken by the husband to confirm his denial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if the wife claims her husband kissed her mother with desire and the husband denies it, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The wife's testimony is accepted and the husband must be divorced.
B) The husband is believed upon oath unless there are clear signs of desire.
C) The third party (the mother) must testify to confirm.
D) The case is dismissed automatically.

Key Takeaway
In Hurmah Musaharah cases, the husband's denial with oath is given weight unless physical evidence contradicts; the third party is a witness, not a defendant.

Conditions for Father or Grandfather's Marriage to a Non-Kuf'
Rasm rule: conditions for validity of father/grandfather's marriage to non-kuf'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that make a father's marriage of his minor child to a non-kuf' or with ghban fahish valid, and identify when the marriage is void.

Core Idea
A father's marriage to a non-kuf' is valid only if he is sane and not known for imprudence.

This lesson dissects the conditions under which a father or grandfather can validly marry a minor to a non-equivalent partner or with an egregiously deficient dower. The passage from Thanwi's As'ila al-Thani clarifies the two essential prerequisites: sanity and good management reputation. Understanding these conditions is crucial for muftis to avoid incorrectly invalidating marriages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the guardian
The act is marriage by father or grandfather of a minor child to a non-equivalent (non-kuf') or with egregious deficiency in the dower (ghaban fahish). Note that the ruling is specifically for this scenario.
This does not apply to other guardians, which are covered in a separate rule.
2
Apply the first condition: sanity at the time
The guardian must be in full possession of his senses. If he was intoxicated or otherwise impaired, the marriage is absolutely void regardless of other factors.
The condition is assessed at the moment of contracting the marriage.
3
Apply the second condition: not known for bad judgment
The guardian must not have a reputation for poor management or lack of foresight due to greed or imprudence. If such a reputation exists, the marriage is void even if the guardian was sane.
"Known for bad judgment" means prior incidents demonstrate disregard for welfare.
4
Differentiate between 'bad judgment' and mere 'fasiq'
A person who is simply reckless or shameless (fasiq) is not automatically considered lacking good judgment. The marriage of a fasiq father to a non-kuf' can be valid if he is not known for imprudence.
This nuance is often overlooked; many scholars mistakenly treat fasiq as disqualifying.
5
Determine the outcome
If both conditions are met, the marriage is valid and binding (lazim). If either condition is absent, the marriage is absolutely void (batil).
The same ruling applies whether the father acts directly or through a specific agent.

Source Text

کہ اُس زیادتی کو عموما ناگوار سمجھا جاتا ہے مگر غیر کفو کے ساتھ اور غبن فاحش پر نکاح کے صحیح ہونے کے لیے دو شرطیں ہیں ۔ اول یہ کہ وہ شخص نکاح کرنے کے وقت ہوش تو اس سالم رکھتا ہو پس اگر نشہ کی حالت میں مصلحت اور انجام بینی کو مد نظر نہیں رکھتا پس اگر کوئی شخص لالچ یا نا عاقیت اندیشی کے سبب بد تدبیری میں مشہور و معروف ہو وہ اگر نابالغ بیٹے یا بیٹی کا نکاح غیر کفو سے کر دے یا مہر میں غبن فاحش کرے تو ہیں۔ اور ان دونوں شرطوں کا لے اگر باپ، دادا خو د نکاح پڑھا دیں تب بھی یہی حکم ہے اور اگر مقدار ہر معین کر کے کسی معین شخص سے نکاح پڑھانے کے لیے کسی کو وکیل بنادیا ہے تب بھی یہی حکم ہے لیکن اگر تفصیل کو مہر کی مقدار اور شوہر کی تعیین کئے بدون ہی وکیل بنا دیا کہ میری لڑکی کا کسی جگہ نکاح کردو تو اُسی وکیل کو غیر کفو سے اور غبن فاحش پر نکاح کرنے کا اختیار نہیں اگر کر دیا تو بال ہے كما يأتي من الدر في العبارات الأتية من قوله دوان كان المزوج غيرهما الخردمن قوله لو حسين لوكيله القدر الذي مر غبن فاحش الخمر وكما اذا صرح في الوكيل ان ارقال زوجها بغبن فاحش زوجها بغير كفو حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب اُس نے نکاح کیا ہے اُس وقت اُس کی ظاہری حالت سے کم از کم خیر خواہی کی توقع ہوسکتی ہو۔ اور جب باپ نہ ہو تو دادا اولیٰ ہوتا ہے اور دادا جو نکاح کر دے حق ولایت اس میں وہی تفصیل ہے جو باپ کے متعلق گذر چکی یعنی مذکورہ دو شرطیں اگر پائی جاویں تب تو نکاح لازم ہو جاتا ہے ورنہ بالکل باطل ہے اور دادا کے بعد بھائی چا وغیرہ کو تبر تی ہے حق ولایت پہنچتا ہے مگر وہ باپ دادا کے برابر نہیں بلکہ ان کا جدا حکم ہے یعنی اگر باپ دادا کے سوا کوئی دوسرا ولی نابالغ لڑکے یالڑکی کا غیر کفو می نکاح کر دے یا مہر غبن فاحش کے ساتھ مقر کر دے تب تو نکاح بالکل ہی نہیں ہوتا خواہ اُس نے نہایت ہی خیر خواہی سے ایسا کیا ہو۔ کفو میں ہر صورت پر کیا ہوا نکاح اور اگر کفو کے ساتھ مہر پر کیا ہو تو اس وقت نکاح صحیح تو ہو جاتا ہے لیکن لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ یعنی لڑکے لڑکی کو بالغ ہونے پر اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ اس نکاح کو باقی رکھیں یا فسخ کرالیں جس کی شرط ابھی آتی ہے اور اس اختیار کو خیار بلوغ کہا جاتا ہے ۔ اور خیار بلوغ میں نکاح فسخ ہونے کے لیے قضائے قاضی ہر حال میں شرط ہے بدون قضائے قاضی کسی حال میں نکاح فسخ نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ اور جہاں قاضی نہ ہو وہاں مسلمان حاکم یا پنچائیت علی الترتیب فسخ کر سکتی ہے كما مر مع الشرائط في اصل الرسالة. شریعت نے خاص ترتیب کے ساتھ یکے بعد دیگرے ولایت کا حق بہت لوگوں کو دیا ہے جس کی تفصیل کتب فقہ سے معلوم ہو سکتی ہے الخ یعنی چاہے لڑکا بالغ ہو کر فسخ کا خواہاں ہو یا نہ
That this excess is generally considered objectionable, but for the validity of marriage with a non-equivalent and with egregious fraud in the dower, there are two conditions. First: that the person at the time of marriage possesses full sanity; so if he did so while intoxicated, the marriage is absolutely void. Second condition: that he is not known for bad choice; meaning no previous incident occurred on account of which people generally think that this person, due to carelessness in affairs etc., does not consider expediency and foresight. So if a person is notorious for bad management due to greed or imprudence, and he marries his minor son or daughter to a non-equivalent or with egregious fraud in the dower, that marriage is also absolutely void. And a person who is reckless, i.e. shameless and without honor, is under the ruling of free choice, as in the beginning of the chapter on guardians from al-Durr al-Mukhtar with al-Shami (important volume). Understand this well; most people are unaware of it. And considering these two conditions, if the father or grandfather themselves perform the marriage, the same ruling applies. And if he appoints someone as an agent for a specific amount and a specific person, the same ruling applies. But if he appointed an agent without specifying the amount of dower and the identity of the husband, saying 'marry my daughter wherever,' then that agent has no authority to marry to a non-equivalent or with egregious fraud; if he does so, it is void, as will come from al-Durr in the following expressions: from his statement 'while if the one marrying is other than them...' up to his statement 'if he appointed an agent...' the ruling already passed concerning egregious fraud, etc., and also when he explicitly states in the agency that he may marry her with egregious fraud, [the agent] marries her to a non-equivalent. The summary is that when he performed the marriage, at that time from his apparent state at least goodwill could be expected. And when the father is not present, the grandfather takes precedence. And the grandfather's marriage by guardianship has the same details as passed regarding the father, i.e., if the two mentioned conditions are present, then the marriage becomes binding; otherwise it is absolutely void. After the grandfather, brothers etc. receive the right of guardianship, but they are not equal to the father and grandfather; rather they have a separate ruling. That is, if a guardian other than the father and grandfather marries a minor boy or girl to a non-equivalent or fixes the dower with egregious fraud, then the marriage does not occur at all, even if he did so with extreme goodwill. A marriage done in proper equivalence and with proper dower: if he does it with equivalence and proper dower, then at that time the marriage is valid but not binding. That is, the boy and girl upon reaching adulthood have the option to keep this marriage or have it dissolved, whose condition will come later. And this option is called option of puberty. For the dissolution of the marriage by option of puberty, the verdict of a judge is necessary in all cases; without the judge's verdict the marriage cannot be dissolved in any case. And where there is no judge, a Muslim ruler or a panchayat can dissolve it in order, as has passed with the conditions in the original treatise. The Shari'ah has given the right of guardianship to many people one after another in a specific order, whose details can be learned from books of fiqh, etc., whether the boy upon becoming an adult desires dissolution or not.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule (methodological rule) for the mufti concerning the validity of marriages conducted by guardians for minors when the marriage involves a non-equivalent (non-kuf') or egregious deficiency in the dower (ghaban fahish). The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, explains the two essential conditions that must be met for the marriage to be valid and binding when performed by the father or grandfather. First, the guardian must be sane at the time of the marriage; if intoxicated, the marriage is void. Second, the guardian must not be known for poor judgment or lack of foresight in dealings; if he has a reputation for imprudence or greed, the marriage is also void. Importantly, the text clarifies that even a person who is simply reckless (fasiq) in the sense of being shameless and without honor is considered to have full authority (al-ikhtiyar) and his marriage in this case is valid if the conditions are met, though the author notes many are unaware of this nuance. The same conditions apply when the father or grandfather appoints an agent with specific instructions; if the agent is given general authority without specifying the dower or husband, he lacks the power to marry to a non-equivalent or with egregious fraud. The passage then distinguishes between the ruling for grandfather (who is treated like the father) and for other guardians (brothers, etc.). For grandfather, the same two conditions apply; if met, the marriage is binding; if not, void. For other guardians, any marriage to a non-equivalent or with egregious fraud is absolutely void regardless of their goodwill. However, if such guardians marry a minor to a proper equivalent with proper dower, the marriage is valid but not binding; the minor upon attaining puberty has the option (khiyar al-bulugh) to affirm or dissolve the marriage. The text emphasizes that dissolution requires a judge's decree, and in the absence of a judge, a Muslim ruler or panchayat can act accordingly. This rule is crucial for muftis to avoid issuing fatwas that overlook the distinction between types of guardians.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghaban fahish): Egregious deficiency in the dower (mahr) that is considered excessive and damaging to the minor's interest.
کفو (kuf'): Equivalence in lineage, religion, profession, and other relevant attributes for marital compatibility.
خیار بلوغ (khiyar bulugh): The option given to a minor upon reaching puberty to affirm or dissolve a marriage contracted by a guardian other than father/grandfather.
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship authority over a minor, specifically the right to contract marriage on their behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when a father who is intoxicated marries his minor son to a non-equivalent woman?
A) The marriage is valid because the father has ijbar authority.
B) The marriage is void because the first condition (sanity) is not met.
C) The marriage is valid but the son has khiyar al-bulugh.
D) The marriage is valid only if the father is not known for bad judgment.

Key Takeaway
For a father or grandfather's marriage to a non-kuf' or with ghban fahish to be valid, both sanity and absence of a reputation for bad judgment are required; otherwise the marriage is void.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Ruling for Other Guardians and the Option of Puberty (Khiyar al-Bulugh)
Rasm rule: other guardians' marriage and khiyar al-bulugh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the ruling for other guardians (non-father/grandfather) regarding marriage to non-kuf', and explain the khiyar al-bulugh option including its requirement for a judge's decree.

Core Idea
Other guardians' marriage to a non-kuf' is always void; with proper kuf', it's valid but the minor can cancel upon puberty.

This lesson covers the separate ruling for guardians other than father and grandfather. The passage explains that while these guardians have wilayah, their authority is weaker. Any marriage to a non-equivalent or with ghban fahish is absolutely void. If they marry to a proper equivalent with proper dower, the marriage is valid but not binding; the minor has the option to dissolve it upon puberty (khiyar al-bulugh), which requires a judge's decree. Muftis must observe this distinction to issue correct fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the guardian type
Determine whether the guardian is the father or grandfather, or someone else (e.g., brother, uncle). The ruling differs based on this.
The passage explicitly says 'father and grandfather have the same ruling, others have a separate ruling.'
2
Check the nature of the marriage
If the guardian married the minor to a non-kuf' or with ghban fahish, the marriage is absolutely void, regardless of the guardian's goodwill.
This is a strict rule: no conditions can cure the defect.
3
If marriage is with proper kuf' and proper mahr
In this case, the marriage is valid (sahih) but not binding (lazim). The minor, upon puberty, has the option to affirm or dissolve it.
This option is called khiyar al-bulugh.
4
Explain khiyar al-bulugh
The minor, after reaching puberty, can choose to keep the marriage or have it dissolved. This option is not available if the marriage was contracted by the father or grandfather.
The rationale: other guardians do not have ijbar authority.
5
Requirement for dissolution: judge's decree
The dissolution of the marriage through khiyar al-bulugh requires a verdict (qada) from a judge. Without it, the marriage remains valid. In the absence of a qadi, a Muslim ruler or a panchayat can act in order.
The minor cannot simply walk away; a judicial process is needed.

The passage then distinguishes between the ruling for grandfather (who is treated like the father) and for other guardians (brothers, etc.). For grandfather, the same two conditions apply; if met, the marriage is binding; if not, void. For other guardians, any marriage to a non-equivalent or with egregious fraud is absolutely void regardless of their goodwill. However, if such guardians marry a minor to a proper equivalent with proper dower, the marriage is valid but not binding; the minor upon attaining puberty has the option (khiyar al-bulugh) to affirm or dissolve the marriage. The text emphasizes that dissolution requires a judge's decree, and in the absence of a judge, a Muslim ruler or panchayat can act accordingly. This rule is crucial for muftis to avoid issuing fatwas that overlook the distinction between types of guardians.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghaban fahish): Egregious deficiency in the dower (mahr) that is considered excessive and damaging to the minor's interest.
کفو (kuf'): Equivalence in lineage, religion, profession, and other relevant attributes for marital compatibility.
خیار بلوغ (khiyar bulugh): The option given to a minor upon reaching puberty to affirm or dissolve a marriage contracted by a guardian other than father/grandfather.
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship authority over a minor, specifically the right to contract marriage on their behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required to dissolve a marriage through khiyar al-bulugh?
A) The minor's mere statement of dissent.
B) The father's permission.
C) A decree from a qadi (judge).
D) The guardian's agreement.

Key Takeaway
Marriages by other-than-father guardians to a non-kuf' are absolutely void; if to a proper kuf', they are valid but the minor has khiyar al-bulugh, requiring a judge's decree for dissolution.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
