Guardianship Hierarchy and Khiyar al-Bulugh Rules
Explains guardianship hierarchy and khiyar al-bulugh rules with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three categories of guardians for a minor's marriage in Hanafi fiqh and apply the rules for khiyar al-bulugh, including the requirement of qadi.

Core Idea
Only father and grandfather can make a marriage binding; other guardians give khiyar al-bulugh unless marriage is to a non-kufu or with grossly deficient mahr.

In Hanafi family law, the authority to contract a marriage for a minor depends on the guardian's relationship. The rules differ sharply: a father or grandfather can make a binding marriage if conditions are met; any other guardian grants the minor an option to annul upon puberty, known as khiyar al-bulugh. This lesson unpacks the hierarchy and the key conditions for this option to exist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the guardian categories
List the guardians mentioned: father, grandfather, and other guardians (brother, etc.). Note the two conditions for father/grandfather's marriage to be binding: (1) marrying to a kufu (equal) and (2) with proper mahr. If not, the marriage is void.
For father/grandfather, absence of either condition makes the marriage batil (void), not just voidable.
2
Distinguish the effect of other guardians' marriages
If a guardian other than father/grandfather marries the minor to a non-kufu or with ghaban fahish (gross deficiency in mahr), the marriage is void ab initio. If to a kufu with proper mahr, the marriage is valid but not binding—the minor gets khiyar al-bulugh upon puberty.
This is the key difference: for father/grandfather, the marriage can be binding (if conditions met) or void; for others, it can be void or suspended (mawquf) giving khiyar al-bulugh.
3
Define khiyar al-bulugh and its essential condition
Khiyar al-bulugh is the option to annul or affirm the marriage upon reaching puberty. A critical condition: annulment requires a qadi's ruling; without it, the marriage cannot be dissolved. If no qadi, a Muslim ruler or panchayat acts in order.
This condition is absolute—no self-annulment is valid in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Recognize the immediacy requirement
The option must be exercised immediately (fawran) upon puberty. Any delay, even slight, invalidates it. Similarly, any expression of consent (verbal or by action) after puberty makes the marriage binding.
This strict immediacy differs from other schools; it is essential for fatwa practice.
5
Apply the hierarchy to a scenario
Given a case: a brother marries his minor sister to a non-kufu. The marriage is void. If he marries her to a kufu with proper mahr, she has khiyar al-bulugh. Upon puberty, she must immediately go to qadi to annul or the marriage becomes binding.
Practice using the rules in a step-by-step manner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب اُس نے نکاح کیا ہے اُس وقت اُس کی ظاہری حالت سے کم از کم خیر خواہی کی توقع ہوسکتی ہو۔ اور جب باپ نہ ہو تو دادا اولیٰ ہوتا ہے اور دادا جو نکاح کر دے حق ولایت اس میں وہی تفصیل ہے جو باپ کے متعلق گذر چکی یعنی مذکورہ دو شرطیں اگر پائی جاویں تب تو نکاح لازم ہو جاتا ہے ورنہ بالکل باطل ہے اور دادا کے بعد بھائی وغیرہ کو بھی حق ولایت پہنچتا ہے مگر وہ باپ دادا کے برابر نہیں بلکہ ان کا جدا حکم ہے۔ یعنی اگر باپ دادا کے سوا کوئی دوسرا ولی نابالغ لڑکے یا لڑکی کا غیر کفو میں نکاح کر دے یا مہر غبن فاحش کے ساتھ مقرر کر دے تب تو نکاح بالکل ہی نہیں ہوتا خواہ اُس نے نہایت ہی خیر خواہی سے ایسا کیا ہو۔ اور اگر کفو میں اور مناسب مہر پر نکاح کیا ہو تو اس وقت نکاح صحیح تو ہو جاتا ہے لیکن لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ یعنی لڑکے لڑکی کو بالغ ہونے پر اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ اس نکاح کو باقی رکھیں یا فسخ کرالیں جس کی شرط ابھی آتی ہے اور اس اختیار کو خیار بلوغ کہا جاتا ہے۔ اور خیار بلوغ میں نکاح فسخ ہونے کے لیے قضائے قاضی ہر حال میں شرط ہے۔ بدون قضائے قاضی کسی حال میں نکاح فسخ نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور جہاں قاضی نہ ہو وہاں مسلمان حاکم یا پنچائیت علی الترتیب فسخ کر سکتی ہے كما مر مع الشرائط في اصل الرسالة۔

تنبیہ
بالغہ کے نکاح کے اختیار کی شرائط: بالغ ہونے پر جو اختیار حاصل ہوتا ہے اس میں اس امر کا خیال رکھنا نہایت ضروری ہے کہ وہ کب تک باقی رہتا ہے اور کس کس وجہ سے نکاح لازم ہو کر فسخ کا اختیار باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ لہذا اُس کی تفصیل بیان کی جاتی ہے تاکہ عمل کے وقت اس کا خاص طور پر دھیان رکھا جائے۔

تفصیل یہ ہے کہ جو لڑکی بالغ ہونے پر نکاح کو فسخ کرنا چاہتی ہے اگر وہ باکرہ ہو تو اس کو اختیار فسخ حاصل ہونے کے لیے یہ شرط ہے کہ جس وقت آثار بلوغ ظاہر ہوں اس وقت وہ باکرہ ہو۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نہ اس خاوند سے ہمبستری کی نوبت آئی ہو نہ اس سے قبل کسی اور سے۔ اور خاوند کے علاوہ دوسرے کا اعتبار نہیں۔ اور یہ بھی شرط ہے کہ پندرہ سال سے قبل آثار بلوغ ظاہر ہو جائیں ورنہ جب پندرہ سال پورے ہو جائیں تو اس وقت کا اعتبار ہو گا۔ مثلاً کوئی لڑکی رمضان سنہ ں کی تاریخ کو طلوع آفتاب کے وقت پیدا ہوئی اور رمضان سینہ ں تک کوئی علامت بلوغ کی نہ پائی گئی تو رمضان سینہ ں کو ٹھیک طلوع آفتاب کے وقت اس کو شرعاً بالغ سمجھا جائے گا۔ پھر اگر اس باکرہ نے اُسی وقت فوراً زبان سے نکاح فسخ کر دیا تو اس کا اعتبار ہوگا ورنہ اگر ذرا بھی تاخیر کی تو خیار بلوغ باطل ہو گیا۔ اور اسی طرح اگر اس نے یا کسی نے وقت مذکور کے بعد قولاً یا فعلاً رضامندی ظاہر کر دی تو نکاح لازم ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ بھی یاد رکھیں کہ شرعی حساب قمری سال سے کیا جاوے، انگریزی وغیرہ کا اعتبار نہیں۔ واختيار البلوغ بالسن في هذا الباب لم نره صريحا ولكن لفظ البلوغ في عادة الفقهاء مطلق فيندرج فيه جميع صور البلوغ والله أعلم.
The conclusion is that when he married, at that time from his apparent condition the minimum of goodwill could be expected. And when there is no father, the grandfather takes precedence. And regarding the right of guardianship for the grandfather who marries off, the same details apply as passed regarding the father, i.e., if the two mentioned conditions are found, then the marriage becomes binding, otherwise it is absolutely void. And after the grandfather, brothers etc. also get the right of guardianship, but they are not equal to the father and grandfather; rather their ruling is separate. That is, if a guardian other than the father and grandfather marries a minor boy or girl to a non-kufu person, or fixes a mahr with gross deficiency, then the marriage does not take place at all, even if he did so with utmost goodwill. And if he marries to a kufu person and with a suitable mahr, then the marriage is valid but not binding. That is, the boy and girl upon reaching puberty have the option to keep this marriage or annul it, the condition of which will come later, and this option is called khiyar al-bulugh. And in khiyar al-bulugh, for the annulment of marriage, the judgment of a qadi is a condition in all cases. Without the judgment of a qadi, the marriage cannot be annulled in any case. And where there is no qadi, a Muslim ruler or a panchayat can annul in order, as passed with the conditions in the original treatise.

Note: Conditions of the option of the marriage of a mature girl: In the option that is obtained upon reaching puberty, it is extremely necessary to keep in mind how long it remains and by what reasons the marriage becomes binding and the option of annulment becomes void. Therefore its detail is stated so that at the time of action special attention may be paid to it.

The detail is that if a girl wants to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty, if she is a virgin, then for her to have the option of annulment, the condition is that at the time signs of puberty appear, she is a virgin. This means that neither has intercourse occurred with this husband nor with anyone before him. And the condition regarding someone other than the husband is not considered. And it is also a condition that signs of puberty appear before fifteen years; otherwise, when fifteen years are completed, that time will be considered. For example, if a girl was born in Ramadan of the year such-and-such at sunrise, and in Ramadan of the year such-and-such no sign of puberty was found, then in Ramadan of the year such-and-such at exactly sunrise she will be considered legally mature. Then if this virgin annulled the marriage immediately with her tongue at that very time, it will be considered; otherwise if there is even a slight delay, the khiyar al-bulugh becomes void. Similarly, if she or someone else expressed consent verbally or by action after the mentioned time, then the marriage becomes binding. And also remember that the calculation for Shariah is by lunar years, not by English etc. And we did not see the option of puberty by age explicitly in this chapter, but the word 'bulugh' in the usage of the jurists is absolute, so it includes all forms of puberty. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (rasm) explaining khiyar al-bulugh and the conditions under which it operates. The author begins by summarizing the guardianship rules: a father's marriage for his minor child is binding if he acts with goodwill (khayr khwahi) and marries to a kufu with proper mahr. If not, it is void. Grandfather has the same authority. For guardians other than father and grandfather, if they marry a minor to a non-kufu or with excessive deficiency in mahr, the marriage is void ab initio. If they marry to a kufu with proper mahr, the marriage is valid but not binding; the minor has khiyar al-bulugh upon maturity. This option must be exercised immediately upon reaching puberty—delay nullifies it. Also, a qadi's verdict is required for annulment in all cases; where no qadi exists, a Muslim ruler or panchayat may act. The passage then details the conditions for khiyar al-bulugh for a virgin girl: she must be a virgin at the time of puberty (no prior consummation), and puberty must occur before age 15 (lunar years). If no signs appear by 15, she is considered mature at the completion of 15. She must annul immediately upon maturity; any delay or expression of consent (verbal or by action) makes the marriage binding. The author notes that the option by age is not explicitly stated in this chapter but is included because the term 'bulugh' is absolute. This clarifies that khiyar al-bulugh applies to all forms of puberty, whether by signs or age.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option granted to a minor who was married off by a guardian (other than father/grandfather in case of improper marriage, or any guardian other than father/grandfather even if proper) to annul or affirm the marriage upon reaching puberty.
کفو (kufu'): Equality in lineage, religion, and profession (etc.) between spouses for the validity of marriage by a guardian other than father/grandfather.
غبن فاحش (ghaban fahish): Gross deficiency in mahr, defined as less than the customary mahr by a significant amount (e.g., half or more depending on custom).
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship authority to contract marriage for a minor. The hierarchy: father, then grandfather, then brother, etc. Only father and grandfather have the authority to make a marriage binding; others have limited authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, when does a guardian other than father/grandfather's marriage give the minor khiyar al-bulugh?
A) Whenever the guardian marries the minor, regardless of kufu and mahr.
B) Only when the marriage is to a non-kufu or with ghaban fahish.
C) Only when the marriage is to a kufu with proper mahr.
D) Never; other guardians cannot give khiyar al-bulugh.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khiyar al-bulugh is available only when the guardian is other than father/grandfather and the marriage is to a kufu with proper mahr; annulment requires a qadi's ruling and must be immediate upon puberty.

Detailed Conditions of Khiyar al-Bulugh for a Virgin Girl
Details the specific conditions for a virgin girl's khiyar al-bulugh, including timing and age-related puberty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific conditions under which a virgin girl may exercise khiyar al-bulugh, including the definition of virginity, the timing of puberty, and the rule for puberty by age.

Core Idea
A virgin girl must have reached puberty without signs by completing 15 lunar years and must annul immediately upon that moment, or the option is lost.

The first lesson covered the general framework. Now we delve into the detailed conditions for a virgin girl (bikr) to validly exercise khiyar al-bulugh. The text addresses the critical point of when puberty is considered to have occurred (by signs or by age) and the strict immediacy required. It also touches on a subtle ikhtilaf regarding the option by age alone, which the author resolves by relying on the absolute usage of 'bulugh'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the intended subject
The detail is for a girl who wants to annul upon puberty. The condition explicitly mentions a virgin (bikr). Understand why the text specifies virgin: for non-virgins, different rules may apply (e.g., the option might be lost because consummation effects).
The text says 'جو لڑکی بالغ ہونے پر نکاح کو فسخ کرنا چاہتی ہے اگر وہ باکرہ ہو تو...'.
2
Define virginity for khiyar purposes
Virginity means no intercourse with the husband (or any other) before the signs of puberty appear. The condition is that at the moment signs appear (or at age 15), she must be a virgin. Intercourse after puberty but before exercise of option is not considered here.
The husband is the focus; other men's intercourse is ignored ('خاوند کے علاوہ دوسرے کا اعتبار نہیں').
3
Determine the trigger for puberty
Puberty can be by signs (menstruation, etc.) or by reaching 15 lunar years if no signs appear earlier. If signs appear before 15, the option arises at that moment. If no signs by 15, puberty is established at the completion of 15 years.
The example given: born at sunrise in Ramadan year X; if no signs by Ramadan year X+15, she is mature at sunrise on that exact date.
4
Apply the immediacy rule at the moment of puberty
At the exact moment she is deemed mature, she must annul immediately (fawran) with her tongue. Any delay, even slight, invalidates the option. Similarly, any expression of consent (verbal or by action) after that moment makes the marriage binding.
The text is strict: 'اگر ذرا بھی تاخیر کی تو خیار بلوغ باطل ہو گیا'.
5
Resolve the dispute about puberty by age
The author notes that he did not see an explicit text in this chapter regarding khiyar by age, but because the word 'bulugh' in the jurists' usage is absolute, it includes all forms of puberty. Therefore, a girl who reaches 15 without signs still has the option.
This is a subtle point; some might restrict khiyar to signs only. The author's conclusion is likely the relied-upon view.

تنبیہ
بالغہ کے نکاح کے اختیار کی شرائط: بالغ ہونے پر جو اختیار حاصل ہوتا ہے اس میں اس امر کا خیال رکھنا نہایت ضروری ہے کہ وہ کب تک باقی رہتا ہے اور کس کس وجہ سے نکاح لازم ہو کر فسخ کا اختیار باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ لہذا اُس کی تفصیل بیان کی جاتی ہے تاکہ عمل کے وقت اس کا خاص طور پر دھیان رکھا جائے۔

تفصیل یہ ہے کہ جو لڑکی بالغ ہونے پر نکاح کو فسخ کرنا چاہتی ہے اگر وہ باکرہ ہو تو اس کو اختیار فسخ حاصل ہونے کے لیے یہ شرط ہے کہ جس وقت آثار بلوغ ظاہر ہوں اس وقت وہ باکرہ ہو۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نہ اس خاوند سے ہمبستری کی نوبت آئی ہو نہ اس سے قبل کسی اور سے۔ اور خاوند کے علاوہ دوسرے کا اعتبار نہیں۔ اور یہ بھی شرط ہے کہ پندرہ سال سے قبل آثار بلوغ ظاہر ہو جائیں ورنہ جب پندرہ سال پورے ہو جائیں تو اس وقت کا اعتبار ہو گا۔ مثلاً کوئی لڑکی رمضان سنہ ں کی تاریخ کو طلوع آفتاب کے وقت پیدا ہوئی اور رمضان سینہ ں تک کوئی علامت بلوغ کی نہ پائی گئی تو رمضان سینہ ں کو ٹھیک طلوع آفتاب کے وقت اس کو شرعاً بالغ سمجھا جائے گا۔ پھر اگر اس باکرہ نے اُسی وقت فوراً زبان سے نکاح فسخ کر دیا تو اس کا اعتبار ہوگا ورنہ اگر ذرا بھی تاخیر کی تو خیار بلوغ باطل ہو گیا۔ اور اسی طرح اگر اس نے یا کسی نے وقت مذکور کے بعد قولاً یا فعلاً رضامندی ظاہر کر دی تو نکاح لازم ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ بھی یاد رکھیں کہ شرعی حساب قمری سال سے کیا جاوے، انگریزی وغیرہ کا اعتبار نہیں۔ واختيار البلوغ بالسن في هذا الباب لم نره صريحا ولكن لفظ البلوغ في عادة الفقهاء مطلق فيندرج فيه جميع صور البلوغ والله أعلم.
The conclusion is that when he married, at that time from his apparent condition the minimum of goodwill could be expected. And when there is no father, the grandfather takes precedence. And regarding the right of guardianship for the grandfather who marries off, the same details apply as passed regarding the father, i.e., if the two mentioned conditions are found, then the marriage becomes binding, otherwise it is absolutely void. And after the grandfather, brothers etc. also get the right of guardianship, but they are not equal to the father and grandfather; rather their ruling is separate. That is, if a guardian other than the father and grandfather marries a minor boy or girl to a non-kufu person, or fixes a mahr with gross deficiency, then the marriage does not take place at all, even if he did so with utmost goodwill. And if he marries to a kufu person and with a suitable mahr, then the marriage is valid but not binding. That is, the boy and girl upon reaching puberty have the option to keep this marriage or annul it, the condition of which will come later, and this option is called khiyar al-bulugh. And in khiyar al-bulugh, for the annulment of marriage, the judgment of a qadi is a condition in all cases. Without the judgment of a qadi, the marriage cannot be annulled in any case. And where there is no qadi, a Muslim ruler or a panchayat can annul in order, as passed with the conditions in the original treatise.

Note: Conditions of the option of the marriage of a mature girl: In the option that is obtained upon reaching puberty, it is extremely necessary to keep in mind how long it remains and by what reasons the marriage becomes binding and the option of annulment becomes void. Therefore its detail is stated so that at the time of action special attention may be paid to it.

The detail is that if a girl wants to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty, if she is a virgin, then for her to have the option of annulment, the condition is that at the time signs of puberty appear, she is a virgin. This means that neither has intercourse occurred with this husband nor with anyone before him. And the condition regarding someone other than the husband is not considered. And it is also a condition that signs of puberty appear before fifteen years; otherwise, when fifteen years are completed, that time will be considered. For example, if a girl was born in Ramadan of the year such-and-such at sunrise, and in Ramadan of the year such-and-such no sign of puberty was found, then in Ramadan of the year such-and-such at exactly sunrise she will be considered legally mature. Then if this virgin annulled the marriage immediately with her tongue at that very time, it will be considered; otherwise if there is even a slight delay, the khiyar al-bulugh becomes void. Similarly, if she or someone else expressed consent verbally or by action after the mentioned time, then the marriage becomes binding. And also remember that the calculation for Shariah is by lunar years, not by English etc. And we did not see the option of puberty by age explicitly in this chapter, but the word 'bulugh' in the usage of the jurists is absolute, so it includes all forms of puberty. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (rasm) explaining khiyar al-bulugh and the conditions under which it operates. The author begins by summarizing the guardianship rules: a father's marriage for his minor child is binding if he acts with goodwill (khayr khwahi) and marries to a kufu with proper mahr. If not, it is void. Grandfather has the same authority. For guardians other than father and grandfather, if they marry a minor to a non-kufu or with excessive deficiency in mahr, the marriage is void ab initio. If they marry to a kufu with proper mahr, the marriage is valid but not binding; the minor has khiyar al-bulugh upon maturity. This option must be exercised immediately upon reaching puberty—delay nullifies it. Also, a qadi's verdict is required for annulment in all cases; where no qadi exists, a Muslim ruler or panchayat may act. The passage then details the conditions for khiyar al-bulugh for a virgin girl: she must be a virgin at the time of puberty (no prior consummation), and puberty must occur before age 15 (lunar years). If no signs appear by 15, she is considered mature at the completion of 15. She must annul immediately upon maturity; any delay or expression of consent (verbal or by action) makes the marriage binding. The author notes that the option by age is not explicitly stated in this chapter but is included because the term 'bulugh' is absolute. This clarifies that khiyar al-bulugh applies to all forms of puberty, whether by signs or age.

Key Terms
باکرہ (bikr): A virgin girl. The condition for khiyar al-bulugh is that she must be a virgin at the time puberty occurs.
بلوغ بالسن (bulugh bil-sinn): Puberty by age – reaching 15 lunar years without physical signs. The text includes this under 'bulugh' absolutely.
فوراً (fawran): Immediately, without any delay. The option must be exercised at the very moment of puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens if a virgin girl delays even a moment after reaching puberty before annulling her marriage?
A) The marriage becomes binding and she loses the option.
B) She can still annul within three days.
C) She must repeat the annulment the next day.
D) Nothing; she is considered to have consented.

Key Takeaway
The khiyar al-bulugh for a virgin girl is extremely time-sensitive: she must annul immediately at the moment of puberty (whether by signs or at completion of 15 lunar years), or the option is lost.

Conditions for Khiyar al-Bulugh of a Virgin
Explaining the conditions and timing for a virgin's option to annul marriage upon puberty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a virgin's khiyar al-bulugh and apply the rule of immediate verbal rejection (fawran) to determine validity.

Core Idea
A virgin's option to annul marriage upon puberty is lost by any delay in verbal rejection; immediacy is the key.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilatul Najijah details the precise conditions for a virgin girl's right to annul her marriage upon reaching puberty. Understanding these conditions is crucial for a mufti to advise correctly in cases of minor marriages. The ruling emphasizes the immediacy of the rejection and the difference between a virgin and a non-virgin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Who has the khiyar al-bulugh? Only the virgin (bikr) married before puberty by her guardian.
A non-virgin (thayyib) does not have this option; she is considered to have tacitly consented.
2
Determine the moment of puberty
Puberty is determined by signs (e.g., menstruation) or by reaching age 15 lunar years. If signs appear before 15, the moment is when signs first appear; otherwise, age 15.
The passage mentions calculation by lunar calendar, not Gregorian.
3
Apply the condition of fawran (immediacy)
At the exact moment of puberty, the virgin must verbally reject the marriage immediately. Any delay without a valid excuse voids the option.
The rejection must be verbal; internal intention is insufficient.
4
Recognize valid excuses for delay
If she is unable to speak due to cough, sneeze, or being forcibly silenced, the delay is excused, provided she speaks immediately upon removal of the impediment.
Other excuses like sleep or forgetfulness are not mentioned and likely do not excuse.
5
Distinguish the non-virgin
A non-virgin (thayyib) retains the option indefinitely until she explicitly consents or engages in intercourse; silence does not void it.
This is a key practical difference.

Source Text

تنبيه
بالغہ کے نکاح کی شرائط: بالغ ہونے پر جو اختیار فسخ حاصل ہوتا ہے، اس میں اس امر کا خیال رکھنا نہایت ضروری ہے کہ وہ کب تک باقی رہتا ہے اور کس کس وجہ سے نکاح لازم ہو کر فسخ کا اختیار باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ لہذا اس کی تفصیل بیان کی جاتی ہے تاکہ عمل کے وقت اس کا خاص طور پر دھیان رکھا جائے۔
تفصیل یہ ہے کہ جو لڑکی بالغ ہونے پر نکاح کو فسخ کرنا چاہتی ہے، اگر وہ بکرہ ہو تو اس کو اختیار فسخ حاصل ہونے کے لیے یہ شرط ہے کہ جس وقت آثار بلوغ ظاہر ہوں اسے بکرہ ہونے کا یہ مطلب ہے کہ نہ اس خاوند سے ہمبستری کی نوبت آئی ہو نہ اس سے قبل اور خاوند کے ساتھ۔ یہ قاعدہ ہے کہ پندرہ سال سے قبل آثار بلوغ ظاہر ہو جائیں، ورنہ جس عمر میں پورے پندرہ سال کی ہو جائے اُس وقت کا اعتبار ہو گا۔ مثلاً کوئی لڑکی رمضان سنہ دو تاریخ کو طلوع آفتاب کے وقت پیدا ہوئی اور رمضان سنہ تک کوئی علامت بلوغ کی نہ پائی گئی تو رمضان کو ٹھیک طلوع آفتاب کے وقت اس کو شرعاً بالغ سمجھا جائے گا۔ پھر اگر اس بکرہ نے اسی وقت فوراً زبان سے نکاح فسخ کر دیا تو اس کا اعتبار ہوگا، ورنہ اگر ذرا بھی تاخیر کی تو خیار بلوغ باطل ہو گیا۔ اور اسی طرح اگر اس نے وقت مذکور کے بعد قولاً یا فعلاً رضامندی ظاہر کر دی تو نکاح لازم ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ بھی یاد رکھیں کہ شرعاً حساب تیرہ سال سے کیا جائے، انگریزی وغیرہ کا اعتبار نہیں۔ و اختیار البلوغ بالسن في هذا الباب لم نره صريحاً، لكن لفظ البلوغ في عبارة الفقهاء مطلق فيندرج فيه جميع صور البلوغ، والله أعلم.

اسی وقت فوراً بلا کسی تاخیر کے زبان سے یہ کہہ دے کہ میں اس نکاح پر راضی نہیں، چاہے اُس وقت کوئی اُس کے پاس موجود ہو یا نہ ہو، ہر حال میں فوراً زبان سے کہنا شرط ہے۔ البتہ اگر کھانسی یا چھینک وغیرہ کی وجہ سے فوراً بولنے کی قدرت نہ ہوئی یا کسی نے جبراً منہ بند کر دیا ہو تو اس مجبوری کی وجہ سے جو تاخیر ہو جائے اُس کے باعث خیار فسخ باطل نہیں ہوتا، بشرطیکہ مجبوری رفع ہوتے ہی فوراً کہہ دیا ہو۔ اور بدون کسی مجبوری کے اگر زبان سے کہنے میں ذرا بھی دیر کی تو اختیار باطل ہو گیا اور فسخ کرانا جائز نہ رہا۔ اگر غلط بیان کر کے فسخ کرالے گی تو سخت گنہگار ہوگی۔ ولكن ان احتالت للفساخ ينفذ القضاء ظاهراً و باطناً عند الإمام رحمه الله تعالى، والله أعلم.

نیز بکرہ کو اس کی بھی ضرورت ہے کہ زبان سے کہنے پر کم از کم دو مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کو گواہ بنا ہے تاکہ قاضی وغیرہ کے پاس معاملہ پیش ہونے پر کام آئیں۔ اور گواہ بنانے کا تفصیلی حکم روایات فقہیہ کے بعد بعنوان فائدہ موجود ہوگا، اس کو ضرور دیکھ لیا جائے۔ اور اگر وہ لڑکی ثیبہ ہے تو پھر اس کو فوراً کہنا ضروری نہیں بلکہ جب تک رضامند نہ ہو گی اُس وقت تک منظور رکھنے یا نہ رکھنے کا اختیار باقی رہتا ہے، چاہے کتنا ہی زمانہ گذر جائے، صرف خاموش رہنے کی وجہ سے ثیبہ کا خیار بلوغ باطل نہیں ہوتا۔ البتہ اگر بعد بلوغ زبان سے کہہ دے گی کہ یہ نکاح منظور ہے یا کوئی کام کیا جس سے ہمبستری ہو چکی ہو خواہ اس خاوند سے یا اس سے پہلے کسی اور خاوند سے، والموطوءة بالشبهة أو النكاح الفاسد والتي حدت بالزنا او تكرر ناها و شاع بين الناس ثيبة أيضاً كما في الدر المختار باب الولي تضمير البكر۔
Note: Conditions of the marriage of a mature girl: Regarding the option of annulment that becomes available upon attaining maturity, it is extremely necessary to consider how long it remains and due to which reasons the marriage becomes binding and the option of annulment becomes void. Therefore its detail is given so that at the time of action special attention is paid to it. The detail is that a girl who wants to annul the marriage upon attaining maturity, if she is a virgin, then for her to have the option of annulment, the condition is that at the time when signs of maturity appear, she is a virgin. This means that she has not had intercourse with this husband nor with any prior husband. The rule is that signs of maturity appear before fifteen years; otherwise, the time when she completes fifteen years will be considered. For example, a girl was born at sunrise on the 2nd of Ramadan in year two, and no sign of maturity was found until Ramadan of year two, then at exactly sunrise in Ramadan she will be considered mature by Shariah. Then if this virgin immediately verbally annuls the marriage at that moment, it will be considered; otherwise, if there is any delay, the option of puberty becomes void. Similarly, if after the mentioned time she expresses consent verbally or by action, the marriage becomes binding. And also remember that by Shariah the calculation is done from thirteen years; English etc. is not considered. And we have not seen the option of puberty by age explicitly in this chapter, but the word 'bulugh' in the expressions of the jurists is absolute, so all forms of maturity are included, and Allah knows best. Immediately, without any delay, she should say with her tongue, 'I am not pleased with this marriage,' whether at that time someone is present with her or not; in any case, saying immediately with the tongue is a condition. However, if due to cough or sneeze etc. she is not able to speak immediately, or someone forcibly closed her mouth, then the delay that occurs due to that compulsion does not invalidate the option of annulment, provided that as soon as the compulsion is removed she says it immediately. And if without any compulsion she delays even a little in saying it with her tongue, then the option becomes void and annulment is not permissible. If she gets annulment by false statement, she will be severely sinful. But if she resorts to a legal stratagem for annulment, the judge's decree is effective both externally and internally according to Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and Allah knows best. Also, the virgin needs to make at least two men or one man and two women witnesses to her verbal statement, so that they may be useful when the matter comes before a judge etc. The detailed ruling of making witnesses will come after the legal reports under the title 'fa'idah'; it must be seen. And if the girl is a non-virgin, then it is not necessary for her to say it immediately; rather, as long as she does not consent, the option to keep or not keep the marriage remains, even if a long time passes; merely remaining silent does not void the non-virgin's option of puberty. However, if after puberty she verbally says, 'this marriage is approved,' or does an act that constitutes intercourse, whether with this husband or a prior husband, and a woman who has been subjected to intercourse by mistake or through an invalid marriage, or who has been punished for fornication repeatedly and it becomes known among people, is also a non-virgin, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, chapter of wali, section on enshrouding the virgin.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) for a virgin (bikr) and then for a non-virgin (thayyib). The author begins by noting the importance of understanding when the option remains valid and what causes it to lapse. For a virgin, the key condition is that she must be a virgin at the moment she attains puberty (whether by signs or by reaching age fifteen according to the lunar calendar). She must express her rejection of the marriage immediately (fawran) with her tongue; any delay nullifies the option. Exceptions are made for unavoidable delays like coughing or being forcibly silenced. The author also stresses that the calculation of age is by the Islamic calendar (thirteen lunar years, though the text mentions fifteen for completion), not by the Gregorian calendar. For a non-virgin (thayyib), the option is not immediate; she retains the right to accept or reject the marriage indefinitely until she explicitly consents or engages in intercourse. The passage also mentions the need for witnesses for the virgin's rejection to be provable before a judge. It references Imam Abu Hanifa's view that if she uses a legal stratagem (hila) to get the marriage annulled, the judge's ruling is valid outwardly and inwardly. This ruling is from the Hanafi school, specifically the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The right of a minor married by her guardian to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty.
بکرہ (bikr): A woman who has never had sexual intercourse, whether with her current husband or any previous husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A virgin girl reaches puberty at sunrise. She remains silent until noon, then says she rejects the marriage. What is the ruling according to this passage?
A) Her rejection is valid because she is still a virgin.
B) Her rejection is invalid because she delayed without an excuse.
C) Her rejection is valid if she had no witnesses.
D) Her rejection is valid only if she makes a statement before the judge.

Key Takeaway
For a virgin, khiyar al-bulugh is an immediate right that must be exercised at the exact moment of puberty; any delay without a recognized excuse forfeits it.

Khiyar al-Bulugh: Conditions and Custom-Based Definition of Ghaban Fahish
Explaining khiyar al-bulugh and conditions for its annulment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for khiyar al-bulugh and apply the Hanafi rule that ghaban fahish is determined by custom.

Core Idea
The option of puberty remains until the minor consents; excessive deficiency in dower is defined by custom, not a fixed fraction.

As a mufti, you will encounter cases where a minor, married by a guardian other than the father or grandfather, seeks to annul the marriage upon attaining puberty. The key is to determine whether the minor has consented (voiding the option) and whether there was an excessive deficiency (ghaban fahish) in the dower or lack of kufu (equality). This lesson parses the Hanafi rules and the intra-school dispute on defining excessive deficiency, guiding you to the relied-upon position: refer to local custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Recognize that the passage establishes khiyar al-bulugh as an option for minors married by certain guardians. The option is lost only by explicit consent (verbal or by action).
Silence does not imply consent.
2
Parse the conditions for exercise
The minor must attain puberty, learn of the marriage (either before or after), and not have consented. Consent can be verbal or by action (e.g., intercourse).
If informed before puberty, option arises at puberty; if informed after, option arises upon knowledge.
3
Understand the guardian's role
When the guardian is other than father/grandfather, the marriage may be invalid if there is excessive deficiency or lack of kufu. If the guardian is father/grandfather with known bad choice, the marriage is void by consensus.
The father/grandfather are presumed to have good choice unless known otherwise.
4
Analyze the dispute on ghaban fahish
The passage presents two opinions: deficiency less than half the dower, or less than a tenth. Al-Shami confirms the relied-upon view is to refer to custom (urf).
The practical effect varies by society.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
For fatwa, determine ghaban fahish by local custom. The option exists if the deficiency is considered excessive by people of that locality.
This is a rasm al-mufti principle: custom governs when texts differ by time and place.

کرے گی میں سے رضامندی پائی جائے تو اختیار با مل ہو جائے گا۔ اور پھر شیبہ کو نامنظوری پر گواہ بنانے کی بھی ضرورت نہیں۔ بلکہ اس کو صرف یہ دعوی کرنا کافی ہے کہ میں شیبہ ہوں اور بالغے ہو چکی ہوں اب اس نکاح کو فتح کرانا چاہتی ہو اور لڑکے کا حکم بھی یہی ہے جو یہ کا ہے کا یعنی بالغ ہوتے ہی فوراً زبان سے کہنا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ جب تک قول یا فعلاً منظور نہ کرے اُس وقت تک اختیار باقی رہتا ہے۔ پس اگر کسی لڑکے یا یشبہ لڑکی نے بعد بلوغ ایک مرتبہ بھی زبان سے کہہ دیا کہ یہ نکاح منظور ہے تو اب فتح کا مطالبہ حرام ہے خواہ اس منظوری کو بالکل تنہائی میں یا آہستہ کہنے کی وجہ سے کسی اور نے سنا بھی نہ ہو اسی طرح اگر بلوغ کے بعد تقبیل وغیرہ کی نوبت آئی ہو۔ تب بھی خیار فسخ نہیں رہتا نیز دعوا سے کی صورت بھی لڑکے واسطے وہی ہے جو ثیبہ کے لیے ابھی گزر چکی۔ اور یہ سب تفصیل جب ہے جب کہ بلوغ سے پیشتر ان کو نکاح کی اطلاع ہو چکی ہواور اگر کسی کو بلوغ سے پیشتر نکاح کی خبر ہی نہ ہوئی ہو تو جب خبر ملے تب خیار بلوغ حاصل ہوگا۔ اور لڑکی لڑکے کے واسطے اختیار باقی رہنے نہ رہنے کی جو تفصیل ابھی گذری ہے اُس سب کا لحاظ شبر منے کے وقت سے کیا جائے گا۔

وفقا روان عرف لا يصح اتفاقا وكذا الوسكروان الخوفي رد المحمار تحت قوله (بنين فاحش) هو ما لا يتغابن الناس فيه اى لا تجعلون الغبن فيه احترازا عن العين اليسير وهو ما يتغابن الناس فيه اى تحملونه قال في الجوهرة والذى يتغابن فيه الناس ما دون نصف المهر قاله شيخنا موفقه الدين وقيل مادون العشراه وتحت قول ( بغير كفوء) بان زوج ابنه امة او بنته عبدا الخر وتحت قوله بنفسه احترز به ما اذا وكل وكيلا بتزويجهما رسیاتی بیانه تریام وتحت قوله (بنین) كان عليه ان يقول او بغير كفوء ولوقال المزوج بنفسه على الوجه المذكوركما قال في المنع المسلم من هذاح وتحت قوله (و ابن المجنونة ) ومثلها المجنون قال في البحر المجنون والمجنونة اذا زوجهما الابن ثوافاقا لا خيار لهما وتحت قوله الو يعرف منهما الخ ) اى من الاب والجد وينفي ان يكون الابن كذلك و تحت قوله مجانه وقتها ) وفي شرح المجمع حتى لا خيار لهما وتحت قوله الم يعرف منهما الخ ) الى الأب والمجد وينخى ان يكون الابن كذلك وتحت قوله رمجانة وفسقا ) وفي شرح المجمع حتى لو عرف من الاب سوء الاختيار بفه اونطمه لا يجوز عقده اجماعاده (مثلا) جلد ۲) ثم قال (وان كان المروج غيرها) ای غیر الاب وابيه ولو الأمر أو القاضي او وكيل الاب لكن في النهر بجمالو مين تو كيا له القدر صح الايصلح النكاح (من غير كفوه او بغين فاحش اصلا ) وما في صدر الشريعية صح ولهما فسخه و هم اوان كان كفوء وبمهر المثل صح و) لکن (هما) اى تصغير وصغيره ملحق بهما رخيار الفسخر) ولو بعد الدخول وبالبلوغ أو العلم بالنكاح بعده) (الى قوله ) بشرط القضاء للفسخ اه وقال له هذا يدل على ان الكفاءة معتبرة في نكاح كل من الصغير والصغيرة كما حققه العلامة الشامي کے ای ان كان العقد بغير الكفوء او يقين فاحش -
If consent is obtained from the thayyiba girl, the option [of puberty] is void. Then there is no need to make witnesses to her disapproval. Rather, it is sufficient for her to claim: 'I am a thayyiba and have become major; now I wish to annul this marriage.' The same rule applies to the boy: it is not necessary to speak immediately upon attaining majority; rather, as long as he does not consent verbally or by action, the option remains. So if a boy or a thayyiba girl says even once after puberty, 'I approve of this marriage,' then demanding annulment is forbidden, even if that consent was said in complete privacy or softly such that no one else heard. Similarly, if after puberty there is kissing, etc., then the option of annulment does not remain. Also, the case of a virgin boy is the same as that of a thayyiba girl just mentioned. All this detail applies when they were informed of the marriage before puberty. If someone was not informed of the marriage before puberty, then when news reaches him, he acquires the option of puberty. And for the girl and boy, the details of whether the option remains or not will be considered from the time of news. These issues are all in Durr al-Mukhtar with the commentary of Allama al-Shami, may Allah have mercy on him, where the author of Durr said: 'Bindingness of marriage when there is no excessive deficiency in her dowry or excess in his dowry, if he married her without kufu, if the guardian who married directly is other than father or grandfather, similarly the master and the son of a mad woman, if their bad choice is not known, foolishness and immorality.' [Interpolated Urdu:] By 'consent by action' is meant intercourse or its preliminaries, etc. [Arabic:] And in the marginalia of Bahr al-Raiq by Allama al-Shami: 'The closer opinion is the second.' I say: perhaps the difference is due to difference of time or place, so the guardian should not determine [by himself] but should look to custom, and Allah knows best. [Arabic from page 158:] 'According to custom it is invalid by agreement, and similarly the insane.' Then the commentary under his saying '(excessive deficiency)' is that which people do not overlook, i.e., they do not tolerate the loss, as opposed to slight loss which people do overlook. He said in al-Jawhara: 'That which people overlook is less than half the dower,' said by our teacher Muwaqqaf al-Din; and it was said: 'less than a tenth.' And under his saying '(without kufu)' that he married his son to a slave woman or his daughter to a slave. And under his saying '(himself)' excludes when he appoints an agent. And under his saying '(fahish)' he should have said 'or without kufu', and if he said 'the one who marries himself in the mentioned manner' as in al-Muqni'... And under his saying '(and the son of a mad woman)' and similarly a mad man. In al-Bahr: 'When a son marries off a mad man or mad woman and they agree, they have no option.' And under his saying '(whose bad choice is not known)' i.e., from the father and grandfather, and it is understood that the son is not like that. And under his saying 'foolishness and immorality' in Sharh al-Majma' that if the bad choice of the father is known by his foolishness or his beating, his contract is not valid by consensus. Then he said: 'And if the one who marries is other than him', i.e., other than the father and his father, even if it is a ruler, judge, or father's agent. But in al-Nahr: 'by a minor or one who has authority, the marriage is not valid without kufu or with excessive deficiency at all.' And what is in Sadr al-Shari'a: 'It is valid but they have the option to annul,' and if it is with kufu and proper dower, it is valid, but they have the option of annulment, even after consummation and after puberty or knowledge of the marriage afterwards. Up to his saying: 'on condition of judicial annulment.' And he said: 'This indicates that kufu is considered in the marriage of both minor and minor girl, as verified by Allama al-Shami, that if the contract is without kufu or with excessive deficiency.'
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage presents two related yet distinct rulings concerning the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) for minors who were married by their guardians. The first part, in Urdu, explains the general rule: once a minor (boy or thayyiba girl) attains puberty and learns of the marriage, the option of annulment is lost if he or she consents, either verbally or by action (such as intercourse or its preliminaries). Consent need not be public; even private approval suffices. Importantly, if the minor was not informed before puberty, the option only arises upon receiving news. The second part, an Arabic citation from Durr al-Mukhtar with commentary by al-Shami, delves into the validity and option of annulment when the marriage is contracted by a guardian other than the father or grandfather (e.g., brother, maternal uncle) or by a father/grandfather with a known bad choice. In such cases, if there is excessive deficiency (ghaban fahish) in the dower or lack of kufu (equality), the marriage is not binding and the minor (upon majority) has the option to annul. The definition of excessive deficiency varies: some say it is less than half the dower, others say less than a tenth, with custom being the final arbiter. The passage also clarifies that when the guardian is the father or grandfather and no bad choice is known, the marriage is binding. The key takeaway for the mufti is the intricate conditions surrounding the option of puberty and the role of guardians.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of annulment that becomes available to a minor upon reaching puberty when they were married by a guardian in a defective manner.
غبن فاحش (ghaban fahish): An excessive deficiency in the dower (mahr) that people would not normally overlook; defined by custom.
کفوء (kuf'): Equality between spouses in lineage, religion, profession, and other relevant matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, under what condition does a minor's option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) become void?
A) If the minor remains silent for one year after puberty.
B) If the minor explicitly consents verbally or by action after puberty and knowledge of the marriage.
C) If the guardian who contracted the marriage was the father.
D) If the marriage was contracted with a proper dower and kufu.

Key Takeaway
The option of puberty remains until the minor explicitly consents; excessive deficiency is defined by custom.

Khiyar al-Bulugh: Minor's Option to Annul Marriage by Non-Ascendants
Explains the khiyar rule for minors married by non-ascendants with conditions and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a minor married by a non-ascendant guardian retains the option to annul upon puberty or knowledge, subject to judicial decree, by identifying the conditions and exceptions.

Core Idea
A minor married by someone other than father/grandfather retains khiyar al-bulugh, but annulment requires a judge's ruling.

In Hanafi family law, the marriage of a minor is valid when contracted by a guardian, but the minor is not left without recourse. This passage from a classical commentary clarifies the rule when the guardian is not the father or grandfather—a situation that often arises in complex family dynamics. Understanding this khiyar (option) is essential for muftis advising on modern marriage cases, especially where guardianship is contested or absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the non-ascendant guardian
The rule applies when the person contracting the marriage is other than the father or paternal grandfather. This includes brothers, uncles, rulers, judges, or agents. Note that the son (of a mad parent) is also excluded from being a valid guardian for khiyar purposes.
If the father or grandfather marries the minor, no khiyar exists for the minor (provided no gross disparity).
2
Define ghabn fahish and kufu'
Gross disparity (ghabn fahish) in dower is defined as less than half the dower or less than one-tenth, depending on the scholarly view. Lack of suitability (ghayr kufu') refers to a match that is incompatible in lineage, status, or religious adherence. Both trigger the minor's option to annul.
The text cites al-Jawhara for the threshold of ghabn fahish.
3
Determine khiyar conditions
The minor has the option to annul upon reaching puberty (bulugh) or upon learning of the marriage after puberty. The option persists even after consummation. However, it must be exercised through a judicial decree (qada); mere announcement is insufficient.
The commentary adds that if the minor knows before puberty, the option starts at puberty.
4
Apply the exceptions
If the minor is mad (majnun) and married by a son (not father/grandfather), then when the madness is cured, no khiyar exists. This is because the son is not considered a valid guardian who would trigger the option.
The text extends the rule to 'mad man and mad woman' via analogy.
5
Formulate the fatwa
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that the marriage is valid but the minor retains khiyar al-bulugh subject to judicial decree. The mufti must assess the guardian, the dower, and suitability, and advise the minor on the procedure for annulment.
The requirement of judicial decree is a procedural safeguard, not a condition for the validity of the option itself.

According to the reliable [scholar], it is not valid by agreement, and likewise... under his saying (gross disparity) it is what people do not overlook in trade, i.e., they do not tolerate the loss in it, as opposed to slight loss, which is what people do overlook, i.e., they tolerate it. He said in al-Jawhara: What is overlooked among people is less than half the dower, as stated by our teacher Muwaqqiq al-Din; and it was said: less than one-tenth. Under his saying (without a suitable match): such as a man marrying his son to a slave woman or his daughter to a slave, etc. And under his saying (by himself): it excludes the case where he appoints an agent to marry them... its explanation will come. And under his saying (or without a suitable match): it was necessary for him to say, and if he said 'the one who marries by himself in the mentioned manner' as he said in al-Man'? The Muslim from this... And under his saying (and the son of a mad woman): similarly a mad man. He said in al-Bahr: The mad man and mad woman, if a son marries them, then they recover, there is no option for them. And under his saying (and it is not known from them): i.e., from the father and grandfather, and it excludes the son being such. And under his saying (at its time): and in Sharh al-Majma' so that there is no option for them. And under his saying (and it is not known from them): to the father and grandfather, and it excludes the son being such. And under his saying (a mad prostitute): and in Sharh al-Majma' even if bad choice is known from the father... his contract is not valid by consensus. Then he said (And if the one who marries is other than them): i.e., other than the father and his father, even if it is a ruler, judge, or agent of the father. But in al-Nahr... if he has the ability? the marriage is not valid (from a non-suitable or with gross disparity at all). And what is in Sadr al-Shari'a: it is valid and they have the option to annul it... and if he is suitable and with dower of the like, it is valid but they (i.e., the minor and the minor female) have the option of annulment, even after consummation, and upon reaching puberty or knowledge of the marriage afterwards. (up to his saying) with the condition of judicial decree for annulment. And he said: this indicates that compatibility is considered in the marriage of both the minor and minor female, as verified by Allama al-Shami. That is, if the contract was with a non-suitable or with gross disparity... Al-Shami under his saying (other than the father and his father): it is better to add 'the son and the master' due to what has passed. And under his saying (on the condition of his agency? the amount which is gross disparity) al-Nahr. And similarly... a man who is non-suitable, as researched by Allama al-Maqdisi. And under his saying (at all): i.e., not with a guardian?, not suspended after? And under his saying (and annexed to them): like a mad man and mad woman when the one who marries them is other than the father, grandfather, and son, such as a brother or uncle. And under his saying (upon reaching puberty): i.e., if they knew before or at it - al-Qahistani. And under his saying (or knowledge etc.): i.e., after puberty, that they reached puberty and did not know it, then knew after. And under his saying (for annulment): i.e., this condition is only for annulment, not for establishing the choice. The gist: when the one who marries the minor and minor female is other than the father and grandfather, they have the option upon reaching puberty or knowledge of it. So the announcement of annulment does not establish annulment except with the condition of judicial decree if they...
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn discussing the rules of khiyar (option to annul) for minors in marriage. The author explains the distinction between gross disparity (ghabn fahish) and slight disparity, citing al-Jawhara. The key ruling: when a minor is married by someone other than the father or grandfather (e.g., brother, uncle, ruler, judge, or agent), the marriage is valid but the minor has the option to annul upon reaching puberty or upon learning of the marriage, even after consummation. However, the annulment requires a judicial decree (qada). The commentary also includes exceptions for mad persons, where no option exists if married by a son. The author emphasizes that compatibility (kafa'a) is considered in the marriage of minors, and if the marriage is to a non-suitable partner or with gross disparity, the minor retains the option.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): The right to annul or confirm a marriage contract upon reaching puberty or knowledge.
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): Gross disparity in dower that is not tolerated in trade; threshold is half the dower or less according to the text.
كفوء (kufu'): Suitable match in terms of lineage, religion, and social status.
قضاء (qada): Judicial decree; required for the annulment to be effective in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what must happen for a minor's annulment of a marriage contracted by a non-ascendant guardian to be effective?
A) The minor must simply declare the annulment to the guardian.
B) The minor must wait until the age of 18.
C) A judicial decree (qada) is required for the annulment.
D) The marriage is automatically void, so no annulment is needed.

Key Takeaway
A minor married by a non-ascendant guardian retains the option to annul upon puberty, but annulment must be executed through a judicial decree.

Marriage Without Guardian: The Mukhtar Fatwa
Classifies marriages to non-kufu and details the ruling for marriage without guardian

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi relied-upon ruling for a mature woman's marriage without an 'asaba guardian and explain why it is void despite later ratification.

Core Idea
A marriage without the guardian's prior permission is completely void, even if he later agrees.

The passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah classifies marriages into several types based on compatibility and guardian consent. For the case of a mature, free, sane woman marrying without the permission of her 'asaba guardian, the author presents the relied-upon fatwa: the marriage is batil (void) from the start. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling, the intra-madhhab dispute, and the practical implications for a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the first type described in the passage: a mature woman marries without the permission of her 'asaba guardian, in a marriage with a non-suited partner. According to the mukhtar (relied-upon) fatwa, the marriage is completely void (batil).
The ruling applies even if the husband is kufu (suitable); the key issue is the absence of guardian consent.
2
Locate the basis in later texts
The author cites Durr al-Mukhtar and Radd al-Muhtar. In Durr al-Mukhtar: 'The annulment of the marriage of a mukallafa woman without a guardian if he is an 'asaba... in the most correct view.'
These are authoritative later Hanafi texts that form the basis for the fatwa.
3
Note the opposing narration
The passage mentions a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad (from Abu Hanifa) that such a marriage is nafidh (valid and binding) if the guardian is an 'asaba, even if not a mahram.
This is a nawadir (rare) transmission, not from the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Understand why the later view is preferred
The later authorities (Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, Allama Shami) supported the invalidity view because it is closer to precaution (ihtiyat) and avoids the woman being in sin. The condition of prior permission is considered essential.
This tarjih (preference) is based on the principle of ihtiyat and the need to protect the woman's religious standing.
5
Apply the fatwa hierarchy
As a mufti, you must follow the mukhtar position. Any narration that contradicts it (like Hasan ibn Ziyad's) is not acted upon. The marriage is batil, and the woman must renew it with proper guardian consent.
This is a key example of how a mufti navigates differences within the Hanafi school.

گیا ہے ۔ رو المختار میں ہے کہ یہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ ” سے حسن کی روایت ہے اور اس روایت کی صاحب در مختار نے عبارت " وهو المختار للفتویٰ سے اور علامہ شامی نے شمس الائمہ کے قول سے تائید فرمائی ہے اور یہ قول اختیاط سے زیادہ قریب ہے مذکورہ بالا عبارت سے اس صورت کا بھی حکم معلوم بلا اجازت والی نکاح ہو گیا کہ جس میں عورت کو شوہر کے بی ہوگیا غیر کفو ہو نے
Khiyar of Compatibility? There are several types of marriage to a non-compatible [partner]. In some, the marriage is completely void; in some, it becomes valid and binding, meaning there is no option of annulment; and in some, it is valid but not binding, meaning the option of annulment remains. The actual goal here is to explain only those types in which there is an option of annulment, because the need for the judge's ruling arises only in that case. However, for the general benefit, we record all types and write the separate ruling for each. Their details are as follows. The first type is that a mature woman marries without the permission of her guardian who is an 'asaba, in a marriage of ghair kufu (non-suitable). In this case, the fatwa is that the marriage does not occur but is completely void. Even if the 'asaba guardian later validates it, it is still not valid because permission before marriage is a condition. Therefore, it is necessary for the woman not to do this at all, because due to the non-existence of the marriage, the woman will always be in sin. As is in Durr al-Mukhtar: "The annulment of the marriage of a mukallafa woman without a guardian if he is an 'asaba, even if not a mahram, like a cousin, in the most correct view. The limit is that dhu al-arham and the mother are excluded. And the judge has the right to object in the case of a non-suitable (ghayr kufu) ... it is said that he gives fatwa on its non-validity originally." And in Radd al-Muhtar, this is a narration of Hasan from the Hanafiyya, and the author of al-Durr supported it with his statement "and it is the chosen for fatwa", and Allama Shami and others supported it with the saying of Shams al-A'imma. And this is closer to precaution. From the above statement, the ruling of this case is also known: that the marriage without permission [of a guardian] in which the woman married a non-suitable husband is [invalid].
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah discusses the types of marriage to a ghayr kufu (non-compatible) husband. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, classifies marriages into three categories: completely void, valid and binding (no option of annulment), and valid but not binding (with option of annulment). The focus is on the case where the woman has an option (khiyar) to annul. The first type presented is the marriage of a mature, free, sane woman without the permission of her 'asaba guardian (a male relative from the father's side who inherits as an 'asaba). According to the relied-upon fatwa (al-mukhtar), such a marriage is completely void (batil) from the start, even if the guardian later ratifies it. The condition of prior permission is essential; without it, the marriage is non-existent. The author cites Durr al-Mukhtar and Radd al-Muhtar, noting that the narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad (a nawadir transmission from Abu Hanifa) suggests that the marriage is nafidh (valid) if the guardian is an 'asaba, even if not mahram. However, the later preferred view (mukhtar) is that it is invalid, and this is supported by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and others. The judge also has the right to object if the husband is not kufu to the woman. This ruling emphasizes caution (ihtiyat) to avoid perpetual sin for the woman.

Key Terms
عصبت (‛asaba): A male agnate relative who inherits without a specified share (e.g., son, father, brother, paternal uncle). In marriage guardianship, the ‛asaba is the guardian who must give permission.
کفو (kufu’): Equality of status in marriage (lineage, religion, profession, freedom, etc.); a woman's guardian can object if the husband is not kufu.
مختار للفتویٰ (al-mukhtar lil-fatwa): The chosen or relied-upon position for issuing fatwa, as opposed to other narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi fatwa presented in the passage, what is the ruling for a mature woman who marries without the permission of her 'asaba guardian?
A) The marriage is valid and binding if the guardian is an 'asaba.
B) The marriage is completely void (batil) even if later ratified.
C) The marriage is valid but the woman has the option to annul.
D) The marriage is suspended until the guardian's consent.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon fatwa holds that a marriage without a guardian's prior permission is completely void, even if later ratified.

Woman Marries Non-Kufu: Fatwa Hierarchy and Nawadir
Fatwa hierarchy ruling on non-competent marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy to determine the mufta bih ruling when a woman marries a non-competent spouse, and explain why Nawadir overrides Zahir al-Riwayah in this case.

Core Idea
When Zahir al-Riwayah conflicts with stronger Nawadir, the mufta bih follows the latter.

This passage from Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najiya illustrates a critical principle in Hanafi ifta: even though the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah) give guardians the option to annul a marriage to a non-competent, the later authoritative position (mufta bih) relies on a narration from Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad that compels immediate separation. You will learn how to navigate this hierarchy of transmitted rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
A woman marries a man without knowing his lineage; later he proves non-competent (ghayr kufu). What is the ruling?
The marriage was contracted with or without a condition of kafa'ah.
2
Recognize the competing authorities
Zahir al-Riwayah (as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar) gives the guardians the option (khiyar). The Nawadir narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad says the marriage is void ab initio and the woman must separate.
The passage explicitly contrasts these two sources.
3
Apply the tarjih principle
The author states that Zahir al-Riwayah is abandoned (matruk) in favor of the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad, which is the chosen (mukhtar) for fatwa.
This is a case where a Nawadir narration is considered stronger than Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Derive the mufta bih
The woman must separate immediately upon discovery; the marriage was void from the start. Guardians have no option.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a mufti following the mufta bih will advise immediate separation, while following Zahir al-Riwayah would give guardians the option to annul or confirm.
The practical consequence is whether the marriage can continue or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کا علم نہ ہو اور کفن ہونے کی شرط کر کے یا بلا شرط نکاح کیا ہو ، اور بعد میں معلوم ہو جائے کہ وہ شخص کفو نہیں ہے تو عورت پر ضروری ہے کہ معلوم ہوتے ہی اس شخص سے علیحدہ ہو جائے ، کیونکہ مفتی بہ قول کے موافق غیر کفو سے ولی کی بلا اجازت نکاح پست نہیں ہوتا تو جس وقت اس کا غیر کفو ہونا ظاہر ہو گیا تو اس وقت ثابت ہو گیا کہ نکاح شروع سے ہی باطل تھا ۔ واما قول الدر المنهار فلو نكعت رجلاً ولو تعلمو حاله فاذا هو عبد لا خيارها بل الأولياء فهو مبنى على ظاهر الرواية والافلا معنى الخيار الأولياء وقد علمت ان ظاهر الرواية متروك براوية الحسن والمختار للفتوى -
She does not know, and the marriage was contracted with a condition of being a kufu or without condition, and later it becomes known that the person is not a kufu, then it is necessary for the woman that as soon as she knows, she separate from that person, because according to the mufta bih qawl, marriage without the guardian's permission to a non-kufu is not established, so when his non-kufu becomes apparent, then it is established that the marriage was void from the beginning. And as for the saying of al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'If a woman marries a man while not knowing his condition, and he turns out to be a slave, she has no option; rather the guardians do' – this is based on Zahir al-Riwayah, otherwise there would be no meaning to the option of the guardians. And you have known that Zahir al-Riwayah is abandoned in favor of the narration of al-Hasan and the chosen for fatwa.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a woman who marries a man without knowing his status of kafa'ah (equality in lineage, wealth, etc.), and later discovers he is not suitable (ghayr kufu). According to the relied-upon position (mufta bih), such a marriage contracted without the guardian's permission is invalid from the outset. The author contrasts this with the statement in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, which follows Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad) and gives the option (khiyar) to the guardians, not the woman. However, that view is abandoned in favor of the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad (Nawadir), which is the basis for the fatwa. Thus, the woman must separate immediately upon discovery.

Key Terms
کفو (kufu): Equality in lineage, religion, profession, and wealth between spouses, necessary for valid marriage.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books, considered primary authority.
مختار للفتوى (mukhtar lil-fatwa): The ruling selected as the basis for issuing fatwas, often from later authoritative scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bih position in this passage, what must a woman do upon discovering her husband is non-competent?
A) She may choose to stay or leave
B) She must separate immediately
C) She must seek the guardian's permission
D) She has no right to separation

Key Takeaway
The mufta bih in Hanafi school can override Zahir al-Riwayah when a stronger Nawadir narration exists, as in the case of a woman marrying a non-competent.

Father's Option Not Voided by Silence; Continues After Puberty
Clarifying that father's silence does not invalidate his option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm rule that the father's option in a minor's marriage is not voided by silence and identify the conditions under which it persists after puberty.

Core Idea
Silence does not waive the father's option; both father and child retain independent options after puberty.

This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah clarifies a critical point in Hanafi family law: the father's right to annul his minor child's marriage is not lost by mere silence. Even after the child reaches puberty, both the parent and the child hold independent options. The author supports this ruling with precedents from Fatawa Qadikhan and Khazanat al-Muftin, emphasizing that the option arises upon discovery of a defect and cannot be extinguished without explicit ratification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key actors
Recognize the father/grandfather as wali (guardian) and the minor child. The ruling concerns the khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) specific to Hanafi law.
2
Extract the primary ruling
The author states that the father's silence does not void his option. After puberty, both the child and the father have independent options to annul the marriage.
Contrast with view that silence implies consent.
3
Parse the conditions for the option to persist
The option remains as long as there is no explicit ratification (ijazah) after puberty. It activates upon discovering a defect (e.g., lack of kafa'ah or inability to provide maintenance).
The defect must be unknown at the time of contract.
4
Identify the thamarah (practical consequence)
The marriage becomes binding only with mutual consent of both father and child after puberty. If either wishes to annul, the marriage is voidable.
This differs from other schools where only the child's consent matters.
5
Examine the evidentiary support
Two sources are cited: Fatawa Qadikhan (case of drinker husband) and Khazanat al-Muftin (case of inability to maintain). Both confirm the father's option persists and is not lost by silence.
These are authoritative works from the Zahir al-Riwayah tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر باپ دادا نے سکوت کیا تو صرف اس کے سکوت سے اختیار باطل نہ ہو گا بلکہ باپ دادا کو بھی اختیار رہے گا اور بالغ ہونے پر لڑکے لڑکی کو بھی اختیار حاصل ہو جائے گا ۔ اس لیے بالغ ہونے کے بعد نکاح لازم ہونے کے واسطے دونوں کی رضامندی شرط ہے ۔ باپ دادا کی بھی اور لڑکے لڑکی کی بھی پس بلوغ کے بعد لڑکے یا لڑکی اور باپ یا دادا میں سے ایک بھی چاہے تو نکاح فسخ ہو سکتا ہے۔ اگرچہ دوسرا بقائے نکاح پر رضا مند ہو جاوے۔

لما قال في فتاوى قاضيخان (اجرا) رجل زوج ابنة الصغيرة من رجل ذكر انه لا يشرب المسكر فوجده شويبا مد منا فبلغت الصغيرة وقالت لا ارضى قال الفقيهه البوجعفر ان لم يكن اب البنت يشرب المسكر وكان غالب اهل بية الصلاح فالنكاح باطل لان والده الصغيرة لو يرضى بعدم الكفاءة وانما زوجها منه على ظن انه كفو عاه

اس جہنہ یہ ہیں اس کی تو تصریح ہے کہ صورت مذکورہ میں بعد بلوغ کے لڑکی کو اختیار ہے اور لڑکا کفارت کے باب میں لڑکی کا حکم رکھتا ہے۔ کما مد فی خیار البلوغ اور اس صورت میں باپ دادا کے منظور کرنے سے لازم ہو جانا اس وجہ سے ہے کہ اُس کو غیر کفو میں نکاح کرنے کا حق ہے جیسا کہ خیار بلوغ کے بیان میں مفصل گزرچکا اور اس جزئیہ مذکورہ میں لان والده الصغيرة الخرسے بھی منہو نا معلوم ہوتا ہے ونیز خزانہ المفتین میں باپ کو اختیار ہونے کی تصریح ہے ۔ فانه قال الاب اذا زوج ابنة الصغيرة من رجل وظن انه يقدر على البناء المعمل و النفقة توظهر عجزه عن ذالك كان الاب ان يفخر لانه يحل بالكفاءة ولم يتقط حقه لانه زوج على انه قادر خزانة المفتيمن ملا ج۲)

اور جب اس کو حالت ظاہر ہونے کے بعد اختیار ملے گا تو کسی ساقط کرنے والے کے بغیر ساقط ہونے کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے بالغ ہو نے کے بعد بھی باپ کو اختیار رہے گا۔
And if the father or grandfather remains silent, his option is not voided by his mere silence; rather, the father/grandfather retains his option, and upon maturity the boy/girl also obtains the option. Therefore, for the marriage to become binding after maturity, mutual consent of both is required: that of the father/grandfather and that of the boy/girl. After puberty, if either the boy/girl or the father/grandfather wishes, the marriage can be annulled, even if the other agrees to continue the marriage.

As stated in Fatawa Qadikhan: A man married his minor daughter to a man who claimed he does not drink intoxicants, but he was found to be a drinker. The girl reached maturity and said, 'I am not pleased.' Faqih Abu Ja'far said: If the girl's father does not drink and the general atmosphere of the household was pious, then the marriage is void because the father would not be satisfied with lack of kafa'ah; he only married her to him based on the assumption that he was suitable.

From this, it is clear that in the mentioned case the girl has an option after maturity, and the boy holds the same status as the girl regarding kafa'ah. As stated in Khiyar al-Bulugh, in this case, the marriage becoming binding upon the father/grandfather's approval is because he has the right to marry to a non-competent person, as detailed in the discussion of khiyar al-bulugh. And from the phrase 'because the girl's father...' in this particular incident, it seems that [the father's right] is not relinquished. Also in Khazanat al-Muftin, it is explicitly stated that the father has an option. He said: When the father marries his minor daughter to a man, assuming he is capable of maintenance and construction, but his inability becomes apparent, then the father has the right to annul because it pertains to kafa'ah, and his right is not terminated because he married him based on the assumption of ability. (Khazanat al-Muftin, Volume 2)

And when he obtains an option after the manifestation of the situation, there is no reason for it to be nullified without a nullifier. Therefore, after maturity, the father retains his option.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule regarding the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) in Hanafi law. The author establishes a key principle: the father's or grandfather's right to annul a minor's marriage is not lost by mere silence; it persists even after the child attains puberty. Both the parent and the child have independent options. The marriage becomes binding only with the consent of both. The ruling is supported by two sources: Fatawa Qadikhan and Khazanat al-Muftin. The first case involves a father who marries his minor daughter to a man who turns out to be a drinker. The daughter, upon puberty, rejects the marriage. The faqih rules that if the father himself is non-drinking and the family is pious, the marriage is void because the father would not accept a non-competent son-in-law. This implies that the father's assumed consent was based on a mistaken assumption; once the truth appears, his option revives. The second source, Khazanat al-Muftin, directly states that the father retains the option to annul when the husband proves unable to provide maintenance, even after the child's puberty, as long as no explicit nullification occurred. The author concludes that since the father's option arises upon the revelation of the condition, it cannot be extinguished without a specific act of relinquishment. Therefore, the father's right continues after the child's maturity. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah tradition, as it relies on the established books of the madhhab.

Key Terms
سكوت (sukūt): عدم التصريح بالفسخ أو الإجازة
خیار بلوغ (khiyār al-bulūgh): حق الفسخ الذي يثبت للصغير بعد بلوغه في نكاح عقده عليه وليه
کفاءة (kafā'ah): المساواة في النسب والدين والمال والحرفة بين الزوجين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His right is lost immediately.
B) His right remains until the child ratifies the marriage.
C) His right remains, and both he and the child have independent options after puberty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a guardian's silence does not waive his option to annul a minor's marriage; both guardian and child retain independent options after puberty and must explicitly consent for the marriage to be binding.

Knowing When a Qadhi's Verdict Is Required for Separation
Poem listing forms of nikah dissolution and condition of qadhi's verdict

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which forms of marital dissolution require a qadhi's verdict according to the Hanafi school, and apply this distinction when issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
Qadhi's verdict is required for all types of separation except talaq, khula', and a few exceptional cases.

This lesson examines a mnemonic poem from Durr Mukhtar that every Hanafi mufti should know. It systematically lists the forms of marital dissolution (tafriq shar'i) and highlights when a judicial decree (qada' al-qadi) is necessary. Understanding this distinction is critical because applying the wrong procedure can render a separation invalid or expose the mufti to legal error.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of separation listed
Scan the Arabic poem for words like 'faskh', 'talaq', 'khula' (implicit), 'li'an', 'ila'', etc. Note that the poem groups them under 'farq al-nikah'.
The exact list is partially garbled, but the key categories are faskh, talaq, khula', mubarat, li'an, and defects.
2
Understand the general rule from the key line
Focus on the line: 'قضاء قاض اتى شرط الجميع' – the qadhi's verdict is a condition for all. This is the default.
3
Identify the exceptions
Look for the exception clause: 'خلا ملك وعشق واسلام التي فيها تقبيل سبى مع الإيلاء'. Note that 'ملك' refers to when a husband owns his wife as a slave (the marriage dissolves by mere ownership), and 'اسلام التي فيها' refers to the wife accepting Islam while the husband remains a non-Muslim (separation occurs automatically).
The exception of 'عشق' is unclear; it may refer to a specific defect or a case of love (perhaps where the wife apostates and returns?). For now, treat it as one of the exceptions.
4
Apply the rule to a practical scenario
Given a situation where a wife seeks separation due to husband's impotence, determine whether qadhi's verdict is needed (yes – it is faskh). Conversely, if the husband pronounces talaq, no qadhi needed because talaq is unilateral.
This step cements the distinction between talaq (no judge) and faskh (judge needed).
5
Memorize the exceptions for quick recall
The poem is a mnemonic; commit the exceptions to memory to avoid mistakenly requiring a qadhi where it is not needed.
Use the line's key words: 'ملك', 'عشق', 'اسلام التي فيها', 'تقبيل سبى', 'الإيلاء'.

Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents a poem from Durr Mukhtar (by Ibn Abidin) that enumerates the various types of separation (farq al-nikah) in Hanafi fiqh. The poem is intended as a mnemonic for the mufti to recall which forms of marital dissolution require a qadhi's verdict (qada') and which are effective by the husband's unilateral act. The key line is 'قضاء قاض اتى شرط الجميع' – the qadhi's verdict is a condition for all types of separation except for certain exceptions. The exceptions mentioned include cases of ownership (milk), love ('ishq?), and when the wife accepts Islam after the husband remains a non-Muslim, etc. However, due to OCR corruption, the details of these exceptions are unclear. The purpose of this rasm rule is to guide the mufti in understanding the judicial authority required for different kinds of talaq, khula', faskh, etc. In Hanafi law, ordinary talaq (by the husband) does not require a qadhi, but talaq in cases of impotence, defect, or li'an might require a judicial decree. The poem serves as a quick reference for the trained scholar.

Key Terms
قضاء قاض (qada' al-qadi): The verdict or judgment of a qadhi (Islamic judge), which is a condition for effecting certain types of marital dissolution.
تفریق شرعی (tafriq shar'i): Legally recognized separation, including talaq, faskh, khula', mubarat, li'an, etc.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of marriage by judicial decree due to a defect or cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Faskh due to a defect
B) Khula' by mutual consent
C) Wife's acceptance of Islam
D) Li'an

Key Takeaway
The qadhi's verdict is required for all types of marital dissolution except talaq, khula' (by agreement), and a few exceptional cases where separation occurs automatically.

Basic Ruling on Marriage with Non-Muslims
Rasm al-mufti: conditions for Kitabiyya marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios of religious difference in marriage, identify the two conditions for a Muslim man to marry a Kitabiyya woman, and apply the Hanafi ruling regarding its permissibility and dislike.

Core Idea
A Muslim man may marry a Kitabiyya woman if she believes and is originally Kitabiyya, but it is makruh without necessity.

Marriage across religious lines is governed by specific rules. This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilatul Najijah explains the two forms of religious difference and the conditions under which a Muslim man may marry a woman from the People of the Book. While technically valid, such marriages are discouraged due to practical harms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios of religious difference
The passage states that difference of religion can exist before marriage or arise after marriage. Focus on the first scenario (pre-existing difference).
The second scenario (post-marriage change of religion) involves different rulings not covered here.
2
Extract the absolute prohibition
From the first scenario: a Muslim woman cannot marry any non-Muslim man; a Muslim man cannot marry any non-Muslim woman except a Kitabiyya under conditions.
This is independent of the type of disbelief.
3
List the two conditions for Kitabiyya marriage
Condition 1: She must genuinely believe in her religion (not merely nominal). Condition 2: She must be originally from that religion (not an apostate from Islam).
Both conditions must be satisfied for validity.
4
Identify the ruling on validity and dislike
If conditions are met, the marriage is valid (sahih) and contracted (mun'aqid). However, without severe necessity, it is makruh (disliked) due to many evils.
The dislike is based on potential harms to faith and family.
5
Note the evidence from Caliph Umar's prohibition
The passage cites that Caliph Umar (RA) prohibited Muslims from marrying Kitabiyya women during his caliphate, indicating the strength of the dislike.
This is a contextual prohibition, not a change in the fiqh ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
